601 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Baranello v. Suffolk County Legislature


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


126 A.D.2d 296; 513 N.Y.S.2d 444; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 41233



March 23, 1987 



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the order and judgment is reversed insofar as appealed from, and it is declared that Suffolk County Charter § C3-10 is constitutional, and that Michael LoGrande is the lawful Acting Suffolk County Executive, and the complaint and petition are otherwise dismissed; and it is further,

 [***2] Ordered that the cross appeal is dismissed as academic and it is further,

Ordered that the appellants-respondents appearing separately and filing separate briefs are awarded one bill of costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county executive and county legislature, sought review of an order and a judgment of the Suffolk County Supreme Court (New York), which held in favor of plaintiffs that Suffolk County Charter § C3-10 was unconstitutional and that the county executive was not authorized to serve in his position.


OVERVIEW: The former county executive appointed a deputy county executive, and 10 days later the former county executive resigned. The deputy county executive then became the county executive pursuant to § C3-10. Plaintiffs filed an action against the county executive and the county legislature. Plaintiffs sought to enjoin the county executive from acting as such, and sought a special election under N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 42, 43. The trial court held that Suffolk County Charter § C3-10 was unconstitutional and that the county executive had no authority to continue to act in that capacity. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and found that the trial court did not refer to any passage from the state or federal constitutions that was inconsistent with § C3-10. The court held that there was no rule of constitutional law that mandated that all vacancies of elective offices had to be filled at an election held as soon after the occurrence of the vacancy as reasonably possible. The court concluded that N.Y. County Law § 400(7) and N.Y. Pub. Off. Law §§ 42, 43, were inapplicable and that Suffolk County Charter § C3-10 complied with the state bill of rights for local governments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and judgment, which held that a portion of the county charter was unconstitutional and that the county executive was not authorized to serve in his position.


HEADNOTES

Counties -- Succession in Office of County Executive in Event of Vacancy

Suffolk County Charter § C3-10, which provides that in the event of a vacancy in the office of County Executive prior to the expiration of the incumbent's term of office, the Deputy County Executive designated by the incumbent shall become Acting County Executive until the vacancy is filled at a special election called by the Suffolk County Legislature or, if none is called, at the first general election after the occurrence of the vacancy is constitutional. Accordingly, since respondent was duly appointed as a Deputy County Executive by the incumbent and was designated by the latter to perform his duties in the event of his temporary disability or absence, by operation of section C3-10 respondent became the Acting County Executive upon the resignation of the incumbent. There is no rule of constitutional law which mandates that vacancies in all elective offices must be filled at an election held as soon [***3] after the occurrence of the vacancy as reasonably possible; NY Constitution, article XIII, § 3 authorizes the filling of vacancies in a public office by way of appointment, subject only to the limitation that the person so appointed may hold office for no longer than the commencement of the political year following the first annual election held after the occurrence of the vacancy, and the subject provision of the charter is in complete harmony with this section. County Law § 400 (7), which provides that, with certain exceptions, a vacancy in an elective county office shall be filled by the Governor by appointment, is inapplicable since the County Law has no application to the extent that it conflicts with the provision of the Suffolk County Charter ( County Law § 2 [b]). Public Officers Law § 42 (3), which provides that the Governor may proclaim a special election upon the occurrence of a vacancy in an elective office which cannot be filled by appointment for a period extending to or beyond the next general election is inapplicable since the office of County Executive was filled by an appointment to a term extending at least until the general election of 1987; similarly, Public [***4] Officers Law § 43, limited to cases in which vacancies occur with no provision of law for filling same, has no application here. The method of succession provided in section C3-10 is in full accordance with the bill of rights for local governments contained in N Y Constitution, article IX, § 1 and with the powers conferred upon local governments by the Municipal Home Rule Law § 10.

 

602 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Schwartz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


128 A.D.2d 783; 513 N.Y.S.2d 480; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 44467



March 23, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, in part to compel the disclosure of certain documents to respondent ticketed speeder prior to a hearing before appellant traffic violations bureau administrative law judge (ALJ), the ALJ sought review from so much of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County (New York), which declared that N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 15, § 123.1 was unconstitutional as applied to the ticketed speeder.


OVERVIEW: The ticketed speeder sought discovery of documents regarding the radar used to clock his speed. The ALJ denied such discovery on the ground that the rules and regulations of the Division of Administrative Adjudication made no provision for a subpoena duces tecum or the use of a bill of particulars/supporting deposition. The ticketed speeder then sought review of the ALJ's determination. The trial court converted the proceeding to an action for declaratory judgment and found that § 123.1 was unconstitutional as applied to the ticketed speeder. The court reversed that judgment, holding that the trial court erred in rewriting the regulations to suit the facts of the ticketed speeder's case because there was no constitutional infirmity in the substitution in the adjudication of traffic infractions of an administrative agency and administrative procedures for courts of criminal jurisdiction and judicial procedures.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that declared that the administrative procedures were unconstitutional as applied to the ticketed speeder by the ALJ.

 

603 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lerner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


128 A.D.2d 641; 512 N.Y.S.2d 886; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 44336



March 9, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York) that granted defendant's motion pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 330.30(1) to set aside a jury verdict finding him guilty of kidnapping in the first degree and dismissed that count of the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in an indictment with murder in the second degree, sodomy in the first degree, and kidnapping in the first degree. The trial court dismissed the two murder counts. At the conclusion of the State's case, defendant filed a motion for a trial order of dismissal of the kidnapping count. The trial court granted the motion and found that as a matter of law the prosecution had not proved its case for kidnapping. The prosecutor filed a motion to reargue the trial court's order, asserting that the trial court should reserve decision until the verdict was rendered and accepted by the trial court. It also argued that the trial court's order was not a trial order of dismissal but an order dismissing the kidnapping count on the ground that the State did not prove defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt and that the order was a nullity. On appeal, the court found that double jeopardy principles barred appeal unless there was available a determination of guilt, which without more may be reinstated in the event of a reversal and remand. The court dismissed the appeal and declared the jury's guilty verdict a nullity. The court reinstated the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal, and declared that the jury's verdict of guilty of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree was declared a nullity. The court reinstated the trial court's order that granted defendant's motion for a trial order of dismissal at the conclusion of all the evidence.

 

604 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Two Wheel Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


128 A.D.2d 507; 512 N.Y.S.2d 439; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 44201



March 2, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sellers sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York) which found the sellers, in an action brought by appellee state, to be in violation of N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 396(r) and enjoined them from selling or offering to sell any consumer goods for an unconscionably excessive price during any abnormal disruption of the market, ordered them to make restitution, and assessed a civil penalty against them.


OVERVIEW: The sellers increased prices on electric generators during a time when many people had lost power due to a hurricane. In an action brought by the state the sellers were found to have violated the prohibition on price-gouging found in § 396(r). The trial court enjoined the sellers from selling or offering to sell any consumer goods for an unconscionably excessive price during any abnormal disruption of the market, ordered them to make restitution, and assessed a civil penalty against them. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. First, the generators were within the ambit of § 396(r) because they were bought for household purposes. Moreover, § 396(r) specifically prohibited merchants from taking unfair advantage of consumers during a disruption in the market caused by a power failure. Second, increases in freight and labor expenses were not taken into account by § 396(r)(3) because they were not costs imposed by the sellers' suppliers. Third, the sellers' prices were unconscionably excessive. Finally, § 396(r) was not unconstitutionally vague because its standards were sufficient to apprise the sellers that their prices increases of 67 percent constituted price-gouging.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which found the sellers to be in violation of a price-gouging statute and enjoined them from selling or offering to sell any consumer goods or services for an unconscionably excessive price during any abnormal disruption of the market, ordered them to make restitution, and assessed a civil penalty against them.

 

605 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Emas Properties, Inc. v. Martinelli


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


127 A.D.2d 814; 512 N.Y.S.2d 213; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 43307



February 23, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed an order of the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), which denied portions of their summary judgment motion in their action to compel defendant city to comply with a prior order requiring the reimbursement of taxes. The city cross-appealed the finding that it failed to comply with the prior order.


OVERVIEW: Upon the finding of the trial court that N.Y. Tax Law § 1262-b was unconstitutional as an evasion of real estate tax limits, the city was enjoined from continuing to levy taxes pursuant to that statute and was required to reimburse the taxpayers for taxes previously paid. The trial court denied the city's motion requesting that any reimbursement of tax revenues be effected through a tax credit to be applied against taxes levied for the next year. The city reimbursed the taxes collected under § 1262-b by issuing tax credits for those amounts, which could be applied to current tax bills. The taxpayers, in an action to compel the city to comply with the trial court's order and issue cash refunds, filed a motion for summary judgment, and the city filed a cross-motion to dismiss the complaint. The trial court granted the summary judgment motion and denied the motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the order for reimbursement was unambiguous and expressly prohibited reimbursement through a tax credit against future taxes. The court found that the order called for direct and immediate repayment to the taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the taxpayers in their action to compel the city to comply with a prior order requiring the reimbursement of tax revenues.

 

606 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Anderson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


127 A.D.2d 885; 512 N.Y.S.2d 646; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 43391



February 19, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the County Court of Chemung County (New York), convicting defendant of the crime of promoting prison contraband in the first degree and sentencing him, as a second felony offender, to three and one-half to seven years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed judgment from trial court convicting defendant of promoting prison contraband in the first degree. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction. Defendant's argument that the conviction was invalid since the Commissioner of Correctional Services failed to properly file the "Standards of Inmate Behavior" rulebook with the Secretary of State as required by N.Y. Const. art. IV, § 8 had no merit. Neither did his argument that N.Y. Penal Law § 205.00(3) is unconstitutionally vague. The legislature's definition of "contraband" under N.Y. Penal Law § 205.00 did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority. The court found defendant was offered an opportunity to appear before a grand jury but refused to sign a waiver, thereby losing any right to testify. Thus, his statutory right to appear and testify was not denied. Defendant's pro se arguments were without merit because he failed to demonstrate good cause for his request to have assigned counsel replaced and venue changed. Because of this, the trial court had no duty to inquire into his request or explain to defendant his right to proceed pro se.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. His argument based on the failure of the Commissioner of Correctional Services to file a rulebook with the Secretary of State had no merit, and neither did his arguments challenging the constitutionality of two statutes. Defendant's right to appear and testify before grand jury was not denied and his pro se arguments were without merit.

 

607 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Shumaker v. Cortlandt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


124 A.D.2d 129; 511 N.Y.S.2d 351; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 40585



February 2, 1987 



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the judgment and order is reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, the town defendants-respondents are enjoined from authorizing or permitting the construction or operation of an asphalt plant on Bilotta's property and Bilotta is enjoined from constructing or operating said plant, it is declared that the decision of the Court of Appeals in Matter of Augenblick v Town of Cortlandt (66 NY2d 775, supra) should be given retroactive application, and the complaint of Bilotta and Sandport Supply Corp. in matter No. 2 is [***2] otherwise dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellant residents challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court of Westchester County (New York), which declared that a prior court decision, finding that appellee town illegally allowed for the spot zoning of an asphalt plant, was not to be given retroactive application, granted partial summary judgment to appellee buyer, and dismissed the resident's action, seeking an injunction against the buyer to build the plant.


OVERVIEW: The town adopted a list of permitted uses in M-1 light industrial districts, specifically including a certain asphalt facility. Thereafter, in a prior case, certain neighbors of the proposed asphalt plant filed an action to enjoin the building of the plant. After a holding in favor of the town and the proposed asphalt plant in the underlying case, the subject property was sold to the buyer. The buyer relied on the lower court's holding that the town had properly spot zoned the property, applied for building permits that were granted, and built an asphalt plant. During the building of the plant, the neighbors in the underlying case appealed and the decision was reversed to find that the town had illegally spot zoned the buyer's property. The court reversed the finding that the prior decision was not applicable retroactively and held that there was no sound public policy argument for not giving retroactive application to a decision of the highest court of New York State. The court noted that the non-retroactivity principles were not fairly invoked by parties, such as the buyer and the town, which were parties within the litigation leading to the reversing decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the buyer, enjoined the town from authorizing or permitting the construction or operation of the buyer's asphalt plant, and enjoined the buyer from constructing or operating the asphalt plant. The court ordered that the prior decision was to be applied retroactively.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning

After determinations of a town board and town planning board authorized adoption of resolutions permitting the manufacture of asphalt on a particular parcel located within a light industrial district, plaintiff purchased that portion of the property which was the subject of the zoning resolutions in reliance upon the Appellate Division's affirmance of Special Term's dismissal of a proceeding to annul the determinations, and obtained a building permit for the construction of an asphalt plant although aware that an appeal was pending in the Court of Appeals, following which plaintiff virtually completed construction of the plant before the Court of Appeals reversed the order of the Appellate Division and granted the petition. No sound public policy arguments can be raised for not giving retroactive application to the Court of Appeals decision (see, Matter of Augenblick v Town of Cortlandt, 104 AD2d 806, revd 66 NY2d 775). Rather than waiting for a resolution by the Court of Appeals, which he knew would be shortly forthcoming, plaintiff engaged in a reckless effort to complete the plant and then attempted to hide [***3] behind the shield of "vested rights", which cannot be condoned. Accordingly, the town defendants are enjoined from authorizing or permitting the construction or operation of an asphalt plant on plaintiff's property and plaintiff is enjoined from constructing or operating said plant.

 

608 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Kendall v. Evans


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


126 A.D.2d 703; 510 N.Y.S.2d 910; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 41849



January 26, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, state chief administrative judge, appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), which declared N.Y. Jud. Law § 39 unconstitutional insofar as it promulgated unfavorable salary differentials between a judge of a Mount Vernon city court and the judges of the White Plains and Yonkers city courts. Plaintiff retired Mount Vernon city judge sought a retroactive salary increase and a pension base adjustment.


OVERVIEW: The Unified Court Budget Act, N.Y. Jud. Law § 221-i (1985), maintained a salary disparity between the retired Mt. Vernon city judge and the judges of the nearby cities of White Plains and Yonkers. The retired judge claimed that the Act violated his equal protection rights and sought a retroactive salary increase and a pension base adjustment. In declaring the Act unconstitutional, the supreme court found that the statutorily mandated disparate treatment violated the retired judge's equal protection rights. On appeal, the court affirmed by finding that no rational basis existed for the Act's geographic salary classifications. Statistical information demonstrated the similarities in the functions, duties, and responsibilities of the judges of the three city courts, which were all located in the same county, were virtually contiguous, and had substantially the same caseloads. There was a true unity of judicial interest indistinguishable by separate geographic considerations among the three city courts. The retired judge was entitled to the differential between his salary and that of the Yonkers city judges in calculating his retroactive salary increase and pension base adjustment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the supreme court order with costs and remitted the case for further proceedings.

 

609 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Miller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


126 A.D.2d 868; 511 N.Y.S.2d 160; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 41991



January 22, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the County Court of Chemung County (New York), which convicted her on her plea of guilty to the criminal sale of a controlled substance in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold cocaine and was indicted and charged with the criminal sale of a controlled substance in the second degree, a class A-II felony. Defendant entered a plea bargain and plead guilty to criminal possession of a controlled substance in the third degree, a class B felony, on the condition that she could submit a motion asking that the sentencing court not apply the statutory mandatory prison sentence found in N.Y. Penal Law §70.00 to her case. The lower court denied defendant's motion and sentenced her to the minimum mandatory sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that defendant's sentence was not cruel and unusual. The court found that defendant admitted knowingly agreeing to participate in the drug transaction to make money. It was irrelevant that this was her first criminal offense or that she was a widow and supported her six-year old child. Moreover, N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law §§ 220.10, 220.30(3)(b)(viii) did not violate defendant's due process rights. Defendant was allowed to plea guilty to a lesser crime and was sentenced accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of the criminal sale of a controlled substance in the third degree.

 

610 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Purcell v. Regan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


126 A.D.2d 849; 510 N.Y.S.2d 772; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 41980



January 15, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which granted defendant transportation authority's motion to dismiss the county's complaint seeking to have N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 1277 declared unconstitutional and to have certain moneys withheld by the authority returned.


OVERVIEW: The transportation authority was a public benefit corporation established to ensure the efficient transportation of commuters within the metropolitan area, which included the county. Pursuant to § 1277, the authority began withholding from the county portions of certain moneys that were appropriated by the legislature for per capita assistance. Section 1277 required each county serviced by the authority to reimburse the authority for the costs incurred for the operation, maintenance and use of passenger trains within the particular county. Section 1277 also empowered the authority to recover unpaid station costs by reducing state assistance to the county by an equivalent amount from allocated state aid. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court did find that the county had standing to bring its lawsuit because it had a claimed interest in the withheld money. However, the court found that the county failed to sustained its burden in proving that § 1277 was unconstitutional. The county's argument that § 1277 violated the mandate of N.Y. Stat. Fin. Law § 43 was unpersuasive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the transportation authority's motion to dismiss the county's complaint seeking to have a public authority law declared unconstitutional and to have certain moneys withheld by the authority returned.

 

611 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Gadway


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


123 A.D.2d 83; 510 N.Y.S.2d 737; 1987 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 39804



January 8, 1987 



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed, on the facts, without costs, and petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner executor appealed the decree of the Essex County Surrogate's Court (New York), which dismissed the executor's petition to probate an instrument purporting to be the last will and testament of a decedent. Respondent devisees objected to the executor's petition contending that the estate should have been probated in Florida.


OVERVIEW: The devisees asserted that Florida was the decedent's domiciliary. The executor asserted that the decedent was domiciled in New York at the time of her death. The court found it undisputed that the decedent had homes in both Florida and New York. The court reversed the decree against the executor and granted the executor's petition to probate the decedent's will finding that the decedent in fact was domiciled in New York at the time of death. The court found that mitigating factors such as the fact that Florida law prohibited an out-of-state executor to serve, that the will was executed in New York, that the will stated that the decedent was a resident of New York and that the will was governed by New York law, as well as the fact that 10 out of 11 of the beneficiaries under the will resided in New York, all weighed toward probating the will in New York. The court also reasoned that probating the will in Florida, which would have prohibited the executor to serve, thwarted the decedent's intent to have her long-time friend and attorney serve as the executor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree that denied the executor's petition to probate the will of the decedent. The court granted the executor's petition to probate the will after the devisees objected to the executor serving in such capacity and the probating of the will in New York.


HEADNOTES

Wills -- Probate

The will of decedent, who died in Florida with residences and other assets in both Florida and New York, should have been admitted to original probate in New York. Surrogate's Court erred in summarily deciding that decedent was a Florida domiciliary since respondents failed to produce clear and convincing evidence that decedent intended to change her domicile from New York to Florida; although decedent had acquired a Florida driver's license, she also maintained her New York license, the facts that decedent registered to vote in Florida and filed tax returns as a Florida resident are not controlling, decedent had a concentration of financial operations, bank accounts and business dealings in New York, she declared in her will that she was a New York resident and she chose a burial site near her home in New York. Assuming that decedent was a Florida domiciliary at [***2] the time of her death, the will should be admitted to probate in New York because decedent had real estate in New York, her estate includes significant intangible assets in New York, the will was executed in New York in accordance with New York law with the assistance of a New York attorney and was witnessed by New York residents, there are statements in the will that decedent was a New York resident and that her residuary legatees should be determined in accordance with New York law, 10 out of 11 beneficiaries under the will reside in New York, and the beneficiaries who together receive the clear majority of the estate seek probate in New York. Further, Florida law prohibits petitioner, decedent's New York attorney who was named as executor, from serving as executor.

 

612 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


McCann v. Scaduto


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


123 A.D.2d 111; 510 N.Y.S.2d 149; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 60657



December 31, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the motion is granted to the extent that reargument is granted, upon reargument the original result is adhered to, and the motion is otherwise denied, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer filed a motion for reargument with the court, which affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the taxpayer's petition to vacate the conveyance of her property by respondent Treasurer of the County of Nassau pursuant to a tax lien. Taxpayer challenged the constitutionality of the N.Y. Nassau County Admin. Code provisions concerning enforcement of property tax collection.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer failed to pay her property taxes. The Treasurer published notice for three consecutive weeks in a newspaper of general circulation naming the properties for which the taxes were delinquent and which were subject to tax liens and sale. The taxpayer's property was on the list. Three months before the expiration of the redemption period, the purchaser of the tax lien notified the taxpayer that she must redeem her property before three months was up or lose title to her house. The taxpayer admitting receiving the notice, but did nothing. The Treasurer passed title to the purchaser. The taxpayer filed a petition to vacate the sale and to permit her to redeem her property, which the trial court denied and the court affirmed. Upon reargument, the court determined that the N.Y. Nassau County Admin. Code provisions concerning enforcement of property tax collection were not unconstitutional. Due process did not require that the taxpayer receive personal notice of the tax sale. Notification by publication was sufficient. The taxpayer did receive notice that the redemption period was expiring, but she did not act upon that notice. Her petition was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The motion for reargument was granted. The motion was denied in all other respects and the judgment dismissing the taxpayer's petition was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Tax Liens, Tax Sales and Tax Titles

The provisions of the Nassau County Administrative Code (NCAC) dealing with the enforcement of collection of real estate taxes are not unconstitutional on the ground that the NCAC does not require that actual notice of sale of the tax lien upon the owner's property be served upon the property owner. The NCAC requires that the property owner be served with actual notice, by certified mail, return receipt requested, of his right to redeem the outstanding tax lien prior to the expiration of the redemption period, after which time the lienholder is entitled to acquire absolute title to the subject premises, and this statutory scheme is constitutional. There is no constitutional requirement [***2] that the owner receive personal notice of a tax sale, notification by publication being adequate. The only practical effect of the tax lien sale is to change the entity to which the unpaid taxes are owed, since the tax lien purchaser does not obtain title to the premises on the date of the sale but merely acquires a tax lien and does not become entitled to exercise any possessory interest in the premises until the end of the statutory two-year redemption period. Due process does not require that a property owner be afforded a hearing before the divestiture of his property title to enforce the collection of real estate taxes.

 

613 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Axelrod


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


123 A.D.2d 21; 510 N.Y.S.2d 92; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 60652



December 30, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Judgment (denominated an order), Supreme Court, New York County, entered on June 30, 1986, reversed, on the law, respondent's determination overruling the Administrative Law Officer annulled, and the matter remanded to respondent for a determination either to direct the limited disclosure called for by the Administrative Law Officer, or to dismiss the charges against petitioner, without costs and without disbursements. So much of the order as granted the sealing of this file and permitted petitioner to proceed anonymously is affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner psychiatrist challenged an order of the Supreme Court of New York County (New York), which dismissed the petition that he filed under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 to vacate respondent commissioner of health's reversal of an administrative law officer's rulings in a professional misconduct proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed petitioner psychiatrist's request under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 to vacate respondent commissioner of health's reversal of an Administrative Law Officer's rulings in a professional misconduct proceeding. The court reversed that dismissal on appeal, annulled the reversal of the Administrative Law Officer's rulings, and remanded the case to respondent to either direct the limited disclosure for which the Administrative Law Officer called or to dismiss the charges against petitioner. The court found that forcing petitioner to pursue his administrative remedies without adequate discovery regarding the complaining witnesses would have arguably undermined and impaired the right of confrontation and cross-examination, and resulted in an unconstitutional deprivation of property without due process of law. The court further determined that the legislature intended that the Administrative Law Officer be independent of respondent's control in making his rulings. The court also concluded that the committee simply wanted respondent to permit the limited disclosure that was sought.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a dismissal of petitioner psychiatrist's request to vacate respondent commissioner of health's reversal of an Administrative Law Officer's rulings in a professional misconduct proceeding, annulled the reversal of those rulings, and remanded the case to respondent. The found a legislative intent that the Administrative Law Officer act independently of respondent, and that petitioner was entitled to adequate discovery.


HEADNOTES

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- When Remedy Appropriate -- Proceeding to Challenge Interlocutory Order of Commissioner of Health

1. A CPLR article 78 proceeding is appropriate to challenge an interlocutory order of respondent Commissioner of Health which [***2] reversed a ruling of the Administrative Law Officer appointed to a panel hearing professional misconduct charges against petitioner, a licensed medical practitioner, that directed the complaining witnesses to present themselves for cross-examination and directed production of documentary evidence of any prior complaints by those witnesses against petitioner. A license to practice medicine is a valuable property right which, although subject to regulation under the State's police power, may only be denied or withdrawn under procedures consonant with constitutional due process. Forcing petitioner to pursue his administrative remedies without adequate discovery regarding the complaining witnesses could arguably undermine and impair the right of confrontation and cross-examination, and result in an unconstitutional deprivation of property without due process of law. Accordingly, this proceeding is a legitimate exception to the doctrine of exhaustion of administrative remedies.

Physicians and Surgeons -- Disciplinary Proceedings -- Scope of Authority of Administrative Law Officer

2. The Administrative Law Officer appointed to a panel hearing professional misconduct charges [***3] against petitioner, a licensed medical practitioner, has exclusive and unfettered authority under Public Health Law § 230 (10) (e) to make rulings on issues of law arising during the course of proceedings, and the statute does not reserve to respondent Commissioner of Health the right of review over such matters. Accordingly, respondent Commissioner's reversal of rulings by the Administrative Law Officer, which directed the complaining witnesses to present themselves for cross-examination and directed production of documentary evidence of any prior complaints by those witnesses against petitioner, amounted to exceeding the scope of respondent's statutory authority. Respondent's attempt to reverse the Administrative Officer's ruling was an effort to redefine the parameters of the hearing, which was a usurpation of the functions specifically assigned to the Administrative Officer by the Legislature.

Physicians and Surgeons -- Disciplinary Proceedings -- Confidentiality of Reports of Medical Misconduct

3. At a hearing of charges of professional medical misconduct against petitioner psychiatrist, based upon acts of misconduct which allegedly took place 5 to 15 years prior [***4] to the charges being preferred, petitioner is entitled to cross-examine the complaining witnesses and to discover any prior complaints filed against petitioner by those witnesses, within the context of Public Health Law § 230 (11) (a), which provides confidentiality for any report of professional misconduct by a physician given to the State Board for Professional Medical Conduct. Section 230 (11) (a) does not clearly indicate that the purpose of the confidentiality referred to is to protect the complaining source; the statute can also be read as ensuring that it is the target of the investigation who is, at this stage of the proceedings, entitled to the safeguarding of his reputation. The purpose of the discovery sought by petitioner is not to disseminate any information regarding complainants, but rather to obtain information solely within the confines of the hearing. Thus, to the limited extent that the complaining witnesses have appeared and testified in petitioner's presence at the proceeding, they have waived so much of the veil of confidentiality, within the context of the hearing, as concerns prior complaints about petitioner.

 

614 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lambert


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


125 A.D.2d 495; 509 N.Y.S.2d 413; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 62801



December 15, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction in the County Court, Suffolk County (New York) for murder in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant gave statements to the police concerning her participation in the beatings of her four-year-old daughter which immediately preceded her death. Defendant was later convicted of murder in the second degree. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the "moral certainty" standard for reviewing the sufficiency of the evidence did not apply to defendant's case because defendant's confession constituted direct proof of her guilt; (2) the trial court did not err in introducing photographs of the victim because they were offered to demonstrate an element of the charged offense, a depraved indifference to human life, rather than to arouse the emotions of the jury; and (3) defendant's sentence was excessive.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment by reducing defendant's sentence from 25 years to life imprisonment to 20 years to life imprisonment. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as modified.

 

615 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Campbell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


121 A.D.2d 121; 509 N.Y.S.2d 21; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 60645



December 11, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, Bronx County, rendered on January 3, 1985, unanimously reversed, on the law and the facts, and the sentence vacated, the motion to suppress granted, and the indictment dismissed. The matter is remitted to the trial court for the purpose of entering an order in favor of the accused pursuant to CPL 160.50, not less than 30 days after service of this order upon the respondent, with leave during this 30-day period to respondent to move and seek any further stay of the implementation of CPL 160.50, as in the interest of justice is required.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction for criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree from the Supreme Court in Bronx County (New York), for which he was sentenced to an indeterminate term of 2 1/2 to 5 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for possession of a weapon in the third degree. Defendant filed a motion to suppress a gun and certain statements he gave to a police officer, on the grounds that his right to freedom from unreasonable search and seizure, under the U.S. Const. amend. IV, had been violated. The motion to suppress was denied and a conviction resulted. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction, vacated the sentence, granted defendant's motion to suppress and dismissed the indictment. The court ruled that the search of defendant's vehicle was not an administrative search, designed to produce records that are regularly kept, such as vehicle identification numbers. The search was for the purpose of uncovering evidence of a crime; hence it fell under the requirements of the Fourth Amendment. The court noted that the police officer had no reason to believe a crime had been committed when the vehicle was searched. While the court recognized that vehicles are afforded less protection than other property under the Fourth Amendment, still the protections against unreasonable search and seizure applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction in the trial court, vacated his sentence, granted the motion to suppress the product of the warrantless search, and dismissed the indictment. The matter was remitted to the trial court for the purpose of entering an order in favor of the accused.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Unlawful Search and Seizure

A judgment convicting defendant of criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree is reversed, defendant's motion to suppress statements, a gun and vehicle identification number plate (VIN) is granted, and the indictment is dismissed. The items were discovered by police during a warrantless search of a vehicle parked [***2] in the driveway outside what appeared to be an automobile repair shop which had no identifying signs or registration numbers in front, after police observed three men, including defendant, working on the car, and inquired as to the ownership of the car. The check of the vehicle and inspection for the VIN were made without any inquiry as to whether the establishment was licensed or why no registration numbers were displayed; it was a warrantless search for evidence of a crime and cannot be justified as an administrative search. The gun seized was not in public view, and there was no justification for the level of intrusion. No violation of law attributable to defendant was observed prior to the search of the automobile; his production of documents and his statements that the car belonged to his wife established sufficient dominion and control to give him standing. Finally, although defendant's statements made prior to and subsequent to Miranda warnings were voluntary, they should be suppressed as fruit of the poisonous tree since all of the statements resulted from an initial police illegality.

Keslow v. State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


125 A.D.2d 294; 508 N.Y.S.2d 578; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 62557

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action seeking, inter alia, a declaration that the statutes, rules, and regulations imposing tax liability on plaintiff taxpayers were unconstitutional, the taxpayers appealed from the order of the Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York) that denied the taxpayers' motion for a preliminary injunction and granted defendant State Tax Commission's cross motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, an individual and a corporation, initiated a declaratory action against the Commission after the Commission issued warrants to the taxpayers for failure to pay sales and use taxes due. Four years earlier the individual taxpayer had signed a consent form in which he agreed to pay taxes, penalties, and interest in connection with his personal tax liability. After the Commission issued notices demanding payment of the taxes, the taxpayers failed to seek administrative review with respect to the warrants issued thereon. The trial court dismissed the taxpayers' action holding that it was premature because of the taxpayers' failure to exhaust their administrative remedies. In affirming that order, the court held that there was no constitutional impropriety where there had been no attempt to effect a seizure of property pursuant to the warrants and the taxpayers had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the taxpayers' motion for a preliminary injunction and granting the Commission's cross motion to dismiss the complaint.

Stony Point Policemen's Benevolent Asso. v. Shankey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


125 A.D.2d 314; 508 N.Y.S.2d 597; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 62575



December 1, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a town supervisor, appealed an order of the Supreme Court, Rockland County (New York), which vacated the supervisor's appointment as police commissioner and ordered a hearing as to whether a sergeant's position in the police department was vacant. Petitioner, candidate for sergeant, sought to enjoin the supervisor from exercising the powers of police commissioner and to compel the town board to appoint him to the sergeant's position.


OVERVIEW: The supervisor was appointed as police commissioner by the town board pursuant to N.Y. Town Law § 150(2). The board later passed a resolution appointing the candidate to the sergeant's position. However, the supervisor, acting in his apparent authority as police commissioner, refused to effectuate the board's resolution. Petitioner sought to compel his appointment to sergeant and also claimed that the supervisor's appointment violated 1936 N.Y. Laws 526, which provided for the establishment, organization and operation of police departments in towns such as Stony Point, because ch. 526 did not authorized a town board to appoint a single individual to serve as the police commissioner, as was done here. The trial court held that ch. 526 was applicable, vacated the supervisor's appointment, and ordered a hearing as to the sergeant's position. The court affirmed. The supervisor's allegations that ch. 526 was unconstitutional were unsupported, a presumption of the legality of legislative acts applied, and ch. 526 had been properly published. Further, a hearing on the sergeant's position was required because there were questions of fact that could not be resolved on the pleadings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order vacating the supervisor's appointment to police commissioner and directing a hearing on the issue of the sergeant's position.

People v. Harvey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


124 A.D.2d 943; 508 N.Y.S.2d 690; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 62259



November 26, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the County Court of Albany County (New York), which found him guilty of the crime of assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant agreed to plead guilty to a reduced charge in exchange for a promised sentence of an indeterminate term of imprisonment. As part of the plea, defendant waived his right to appeal. Defendant, upon his guilty plea, was found guilty of the crime of assault in the first degree. Defendant appealed, contending that the sentence was harsh and excessive. The court dismissed the appeal. The court held that where, as part of a negotiated plea, defendant clearly waived his right to appeal from the offered sentence and the sentence was lawful, such waiver was to be given effect so long as it was knowing, voluntary, and intelligent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which found defendant guilty of the crime of assault in the first degree.

 

619 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Selkin v. Regan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


120 A.D.2d 204; 508 N.Y.S.2d 342; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 59235



November 20, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, and petition dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retiree filed a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 to review a determination of respondents, state comptroller and administrator of the New York State Employees' Retirement System, which denied the retiree's request to have his retirement lag pay included in his final average salary for purposes of calculating retirement benefits under N.Y. Retire. and Soc. Sec. Law § 2.


OVERVIEW: The retiree was a member of the New York State Employees' Retirement System. In 1982, the civil service employees association negotiated for salary increases. The retiree received an increase. In order to implement the salary increases, the state instituted a lag payroll for the first year. The result of the lag payroll was that the retiree did not receive pay for a brief work period. Payment for the period was to be paid to the retiree upon his retirement. Anticipating retirement, the retiree advised the System that he wished to have his lag payment included in the calculation of his final average salary. The System refused, stating that the subject payment had not been earned within the three-year period used to calculate his final average salary. The retiree filed a N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 proceeding and the court upheld the System's determination. The court held that because the lag pay was not earned within the previous three-year period, the application of N.Y. Retire. and Soc. Sec. Law § 431 was not necessary. A plain reading of N.Y. Retire. and Soc. Sec. Law § 2(2)(a) supported the System's interpretation that annual compensation consisted of income earned during the subject year.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the System's determination.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Retirement and Pension Benefits -- Final Average Salary -- Lag Pay

Lag pay received by petitioner, a member of the New York State Employees Retirement System, upon his retirement, but earned more than three years earlier, should not be included in computing his final average salary. Retirement and Social Security Law § 2 (2) (a) defines annual compensation as "[the] salary or wages annually earnable by a member, including maintenance, or any allowance in lieu thereof, received by the member", and section 2 (9) (b) provides that final average salary includes the "highest average annual compensation earned during any three consecutive years of member service"; the statutory language supports respondent [***2] Comptroller's interpretation that annual compensation consists of income earned during the subject year. Although Retirement and Social Security Law § 431 prohibits including lump-sum payments for deferred compensation in any form of termination pay in the salary base for the computation of retirement benefits, and has been held unconstitutional as applied retroactively to employees who were members of the System prior to the effective date of the statute, respondent's determination did not indicate any reliance upon section 431. Finally, including the lag pay of System members who retired within three years of the deferred pay period in their final average salary presents no injustice.

 

620 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rotunno v. Rochester


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


120 A.D.2d 160; 507 N.Y.S.2d 924; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 59229



November 10, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment unanimously modified, on the law, and, as modified, affirmed, with costs to plaintiffs, in accordance with opinion by Dillon, P. J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, New York State Liquor Authority (SLA), appealed a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Monroe County (New York), which found that the SLA exceeded its powers in promulgating N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 9, § 100.1(c), which prohibited plaintiff police officers from working in certain establishments were liquor was sold.


OVERVIEW: In promulgating N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 9, § 100.1(c), the SLA prohibited police officers from being employed in any premises licensed to sell alcoholic beverages. When defendant police chief accordingly refused the officers permission to work at a baseball stadium and other venues, they sued. In affirming the judgment, the court held that neither N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law §§ 128 nor 128a gave the SLA the authority to proscribe any form of conduct. The court noted that § 128, which generally prohibited police from being interested in the manufacturing or sale of alcoholic beverages, was silent as to the SLA's authority to promulgate rules. The court further noted that § 128-a, which authorized the SLA to promulgate rules, was designed to permit police officers to work in or for certain establishments that sold liquor, and that it authorized the SLA to promote its ends, not trammel them. The court held that absent some legislative delegation of authority, the rule was void, and further noted that the SLA had no constitutional criminalize any behavior.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, as modified, for the police officers in their action to have a rule prohibiting them from working in establishments were liquor was sold declared void.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating Liquors -- Employment of Police Officer at Premises Licensed to Sell Alcoholic Beverages

The State Liquor Authority (SLA) exceeded its powers in promulgating 9 NYCRR 100.1 (c), pursuant to which no police officer shall be employed by, or work in, any premises licensed to sell alcoholic beverages. The SLA is not, pursuant to Alcoholic Beverage Control [***2] Law § 128 which provides that it shall be unlawful for police officers "to be either directly or indirectly interested in the manufacture or sale of alcoholic beverages", empowered to promulgate rules defining what conduct of a police officer shall be unlawful under the statute and thus 9 NYCRR 100.1 (c) was not promulgated to implement and amplify section 128. Alcoholic Beverage Control Law § 128-a, which provides that "Notwithstanding any inconsistent provision of law to the contrary, the authority shall promulgate * * * regulations * * * to provide that it shall not be unlawful for a police officer * * * to work in a premises licensed to sell beer", directs the SLA to promulgate rules relating to lawful, rather than unlawful, conduct and the subject regulation is wholly unnecessary to accomplish the legislative directive and thus exceeds its scope; if such employment or activity is to be proscribed, it is for the Legislature to do so.

Commissioner of Labor v. Chudzik


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


124 A.D.2d 1035; 508 N.Y.S.2d 760; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 62387



November 10, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Order unanimously reversed on the law without costs, motion to vacate orders granted, motion to extend levy granted and Labor Law § 573 (2) declared constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commissioner of labor, as judgment creditor of an unemployment insurance tax debt, sought review of an order from the Supreme Court, Cattaraugas County (New York), which denied a motion to vacate three orders that denied applications to extend a levy upon the personal property of respondent judgment debtor.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner of labor, as judgment creditor of an unemployment insurance tax debt, applied to extend a levy upon the personal property of the judgment debtor. The trial court denied the commissioner of labor's motion to vacate three orders that denied the applications to extend a levy upon the personal property of the judgment debtor. The trial court's order was based on its prior decisions that declared N.Y. Lab. Law § 573(2) unconstitutional. The court held that: (1) the trial court erred when it declared N.Y. Lab. Law § 573(2) unconstitutional; and (2) because notice of exempt property had to be given to a judgment debtor pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5222(d) and 5232(c), the failure of N.Y. Labor Law § 573(2) to require such notice did not render the statute unconstitutional because the two statutes, which covered the same general subject matter, were to be construed together and applied harmoniously and consistently.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court.

 

622 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Edward R.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


123 A.D.2d 866; 507 N.Y.S.2d 647; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 60982



October 27, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 384-b to terminate appellant mother's parental rights by reason of mental illness, the mother sought review of an order of the Family Court of Dutchess County (New York) that allowed respondent Dutchess County Department of Social Services (department) to proceed with the child's adoption without the consent of the mother.


OVERVIEW: The family court allowed the department to proceed with the subject child's adoption without the consent of the mother. The mother sought review, alleging N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 384-b(6)(e) violated procedural due process because it provided that parental rights could be permanently terminated by reason of a parent's mental illness on the basis of only one psychiatrist's testimony, rather than on the basis of the opinion of at least two psychiatrists as required in certain other types of criminal and civil proceedings. Upon review, the court affirmed. It noted that § 384-b(6)(e) specifically authorized the parent, as well as the petitioning agency, to submit other psychiatric, psychological or medical evidence relevant to the case. Moreover, the parent was free to cross-examine the court-appointed psychiatrist at the hearing. Therefore, rather than restricting the proof to the testimony of one witness, the statute set forth a minimum requirement of testimony by a psychiatric expert in order to terminate parental rights.


OUTCOME: The decision of the family court that allowed the department to proceed with the subject child's adoption without the consent of the mother was affirmed.

 

623 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rochester Gas & Electric Corp. v. Public Service Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


119 A.D.2d 353; 507 N.Y.S.2d 305; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 60632



October 23, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Order modified, on the law, without costs, by reversing so much thereof as dismissed the complaint; it is declared that defendant's Opinion No. 85-6 is not violative of the United States Constitution or the New York State Constitution or in any other manner unlawful; and, as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff gas and electric corporation appealed the decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, the Public Service Commission (commission), in the corporation's declaratory judgment action regarding N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 66d(2).


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 66d(2), which required gas corporations to transport customer-owned gas and directed gas distribution corporations to file tariff leave amendments in accordance with the guidelines of the commission. The gas and electric corporation sought a declaratory judgment that § 66d(2) violated its right to due process by converting it into a common carrier, by interfering with its facilities, and by establishing transportation rates that were not just and reasonable. The lower court granted the commission's motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint. The corporation appealed. The court found that the law did convert the corporation to a common carrier of customer-owned natural gas by requiring the corporation when it had excess transportation capacity; however, that requirement did not violate the corporation's due process rights because it was not arbitrary or capricious. It merely extended the corporation's service to an area that it was already committed to serve. The court reversed the lower court's order and modified it by issuing a declaration in the commission's favor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court, which had granted summary judgment in the commission's favor in the corporation's declaratory judgment action. The court held that the lower court should not have dismissed the complaint, and modified the order by issuing a declaration in the commission's favor.


HEADNOTES

Public Utilities -- Transportation Services for Customer-Owned Gas

1. Although Public Service Law § 66-d (2), in requiring regulated gas corporations with excess transportation capacity to deliver customer-owned natural gas to all those who seek their services within their franchise territory to the extent of their capabilities, converts such corporations, including plaintiff, to a common carrier, there is no violation of plaintiff's due process rights; defendant Public Service Commission's order requiring plaintiff to file tariffs for the transportation of customer-owned gas amounts to nothing more [***2] than extending plaintiff's service to an area that it is already committed to serve. Plaintiff has not proved the statute unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt; development of in-State natural gas supplies will be stimulated and the natural gas market in the State will be more competitive to the benefit of consumers; with respect to constitutional due process, a State is free to adopt whatever economic policy will promote the public welfare. Finally, there is a rational basis for requiring plaintiff to provide the service of delivering customer-owned natural gas and it is entirely rational for defendant to only permit plaintiff to recover the cost of providing the expanded transportation and delivery duties; there has been no taking without just compensation.

Declaratory Judgments -- Form of Relief

2. In a declaratory judgment action, it was error to dismiss the complaint, and accordingly, the order of Special Term is modified by issuing a declaration in defendant's favor.

People v. Reynolds


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


124 A.D.2d 356; 507 N.Y.S.2d 295; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 61378



October 23, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the County Court of Columbia County (New York) convicting her, upon a plea of guilty, of criminal possession of marihuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of her conviction for criminal possession of marihuana, contending she was improperly charged and that the search of her property was illegal. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that defendant was properly charged under N.Y. Penal Law § 221.30, based upon the definition of marihuana for purposes of that statute as set forth in N.Y. Pub. Health Law §3302 (20). The court further concluded that both the aerial and foot searches of defendant's property prior to obtaining a search warrant were not improper. The court found that the aerial observation could form the basis for a search warrant, as there was no expectation of privacy from such observation. The court also concluded that the foot searches were a proper basis upon which to obtain a search warrant. The court found that the items seized from defendant's property not specifically identified in the search warrant were in compliance with the "plain view" doctrine as the officer was in a lawful position to observe the items, his observation was inadvertent rather that anticipated, and the incriminating character of the items was immediately apparent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

625 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Thomas & Betts Corp. v. State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


124 A.D.2d 334; 508 N.Y.S.2d 111; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 61363



October 16, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, sought to review a determination of respondent State Tax Commission (commission) (New York), which sustained a corporate franchise tax assessment imposed under N.Y. Tax Law art. 9-A, and concluded that a sales manager's rented room constituted an office maintained by the taxpayer in the state, thus subjecting it to payment of corporate franchise taxes under N.Y. Tax Law § 209(1).


OVERVIEW: The petition was dismissed on the ground that the proceeding was barred by statute of limitations because the proceeding was not commenced within four months of the date that the commission's decision was mailed to the taxpayer, as required by N.Y. Tax Law § 1090(e). The taxpayer served an amended petition alleging that the commission's decision violated constitutional and jurisdictional laws. The court confirmed the commission's determination and dismissed the amended petition. The taxpayer contended that the limitations period was inapplicable to its petition because a statutory exclusive remedy provision was inapplicable where a petition in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding claimed that an administrative agency acted unconstitutionally or lacked jurisdiction. The court did not agree that the fact that the taxpayer asserted such claims in its amended petition ousted the provisions of N.Y. Tax Law § 1090. Where the taxpayer sought the very kind of judicial review authorized by § 1090, the provision of that statute that a decision by the commission was deemed final for statute of limitations purposes, should not have been negated by the assertion of certain claims.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the commission's determination that sustained a corporate franchise tax assessment imposed on the taxpayer.

 

626 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


McDermott v. McDermott


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


119 A.D.2d 370; 507 N.Y.S.2d 390; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 58992



October 14, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the order of the Supreme Court, Richmond County, dated April 16, 1984, is reversed, an the proposed intervenor's application for leave to intervene is granted, and it is further

Ordered that the judgment of the same court, dated April 16, 1984, is modified, on the facts, by reducing the award of counsel fees from $ 7,500 to $ 7,000. As so modified, the judgment is affirmed, and it is further

Ordered that the plaintiff is awarded one bill of costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former husband appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term of Richmond County (New York), which granted plaintiff former wife a divorce on the ground of abandonment, distributed marital assets, and awarded the wife maintenance and attorney fees. A motion to intervene by proposed intervenor pension fund was denied.


OVERVIEW: After 33 years of marriage, the wife was granted a divorce on the ground of abandonment, under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(2). A substantial portion of the marital property was attributed to the husband's pension fund. He worked for the fire department throughout the entire marriage, and she was a housewife. The special term court directed the husband to select a pension plan payment option that did not limit the wife's survivorship benefits. The pension fund sought to intervene under N.Y. C.P.L.R. Law §§ 1012(a)(2), 1013 for the purpose of rearguing the pension distribution determination on constitutional and statutory grounds. The court held that the special term court erred in refusing the intervention because the pension fund had a real and substantial interest in the proceedings. The court held that the special term court had the authority under the 1980 Equitable Distribution Law, N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 281, to decree that there were two owners of the pension contract and to adopt appropriate measures to protect the ownership interests of both the husband and wife. The limitation of the husband's choices of pension plan payment options protected the wife's co-ownership rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed all provisions of the divorce and distribution of the marital property, including the directives regarding the husband's pension fund payment options. However, the order denying the pension fund leave to intervene was reversed because the pension fund had a real and substantial interest in the proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Parties -- Intervention

1. In distributing the pension rights of defendant husband, a public employee, in a divorce action, the court awarded [***2] plaintiff wife a one-half interest and to insure her ability to receive that interest, it restricted defendant's choice among the payment options. Although Special Term properly denied the pension fund leave to intervene as of right since the standards of CPLR 1012 (a) (2) were not met, it was error to refuse permission to intervene under CPLR 1013. The fund, which sought to intervene, after Special Term's decision but before entry of judgment for the purpose of rearguing the pension distribution determination on constitutional and statutory grounds, had a real and substantial interest in the proceedings. The error is curable without a remittitur since by the Appellate Division's exercise of discretion to permit intervention on appeal, it will entertain the same argument that would have been made at Special Term.

Husband and Wife -- Divorce -- Abandonment -- Equitable Distribution

2. In an action for divorce brought by a 58-year-old housewife married for 33 years to a 62-year-old fire department employee, plaintiff's testimony was sufficient to establish the unjustified and nonconsensual departure which constitutes abandonment. It was not improper for the court to divide [***3] the husband's pension rights, which constituted the major marital asset, equally; the maintenance award of $ 225 per week was not excessive and the argument that it should not have been permitted to continue indefinitely is meritless because the payments were to terminate upon defendant's retirement, a matter of three years; it was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to require defendant to maintain the existing medical coverage or its equivalent for plaintiff's benefit and, under the circumstances, there is no reason to insert a termination date for that obligation. Finally, the award of attorney's fees reflected no abuse of discretion.

Husband and Wife -- Equitable Distribution -- Pension Rights

3. In distributing the pension rights of defendant husband, a public employee, in a divorce action, the court properly awarded plaintiff wife a one-half interest and to insure her ability to receive that interest, it properly restricted defendant's choice among the payment options to permit plaintiff to share in the payments as made and in any further distribution after her husband's death. The method of distribution is discretionary and must be contoured to suit [***4] the particular circumstances, needs and means of the parties in the case. Restrictive terminology created to protect pensions against judicial process invoked by creditors and assignees (see, Administrative Code of City of New York § B19-7.941) cannot be read as prohibiting the use of judicial power to protect an award of pension rights to a spouse, and although NY Constitution, article V, § 7 prevents reduction by the public employer of the financial benefits promised in the pension contract, an equitable distribution court's award of an interest in a pension contract to a nonmember spouse does not unconstitutionally diminish or impair the plan member's pension or the contractual rights to it; judicial restriction of option or beneficiary choices does not diminish a pension in the sense that a lesser amount will be paid. The judiciary may constitutionally and legally determine and decree that there are two owners of the pension contract and it has the discretion to constitutionally and legally adopt appropriate measures to protect the ownership interests of both.

 

627 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


123 A.D.2d 473; 506 N.Y.S.2d 483; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 60228



September 18, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the County Court of Chemung County (New York), which convicted him of attempted promoting prison contraband in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted and charged with the crime of promoting prison contraband in the first degree based upon his alleged possession of a 12-inch sharpened piece of metal with a cloth handle. He pleaded guilty to attempted promoting prison contraband in the first degree. He appealed, contending that the statute under which he was convicted, N.Y. Penal Law § 205.25, was unconstitutionally vague because there was no duly promulgated rule prohibiting possession of the sharpened piece of metal. The court rejected his argument and found that at the time of defendant's offense, statutory and duly filed regulatory provisions prohibited inmate possession of various articles and validly made possession thereof a criminal offense under N.Y. Penal Law § 205.00(3). The court therefore concluded that the definition of the crime of promoting prison contraband was not incomplete and was valid on its face. The court further concluded that defendant forfeited his objections by his guilty plea. Defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel argument was rejected because counsel obtained an advantageous plea bargain.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted promoting prison contraband in the first degree.

People v. Young


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


123 A.D.2d 366; 506 N.Y.S.2d 376; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 60141



September 15, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which convicted him of burglary in the second degree, robbery in the first degree, and robbery in the second degree. The People also appealed from so much of the judgment as failed to adjudicate defendant a second felony offender and imposed a sentence accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted upon a jury verdict of burglary in the first degree and of robbery in the first and second degree. The People filed a felony statement at the sentencing hearing for the purpose of having him sentenced as a second felony offender pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06 and N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 400.21. Defendant argued successfully that the 1974 and 1975 felonies could not be used as predicate felonies because he had not been advised of the constitutional rights that he was waiving as a result of those guilty pleas. Defendant appealed his conviction and the People appealed the denial of their request that defendant be adjudicated a second felony offender. The court found that defendant's argument of prosecutorial misconduct had not been preserved for review because defendant failed to object at trial to the prosecutrix's summation statement. The court found that defendant was sentenced as a second felony offender on the 1975 conviction and that the 1974 conviction had served as the predicate felony for that sentence. The court found that defendant had not challenged the validity of that second felony offender determination, therefore, it was binding upon him.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court by vacating the sentence imposed on defendant and remitted the matter to the lower court for resentencing of defendant as a second felony offender. The court affirmed the judgment as modified.

Abwilda v. v. Thomas W.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


122 A.D.2d 950; 505 N.Y.S.2d 969; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 59439



August 25, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the Family Court, Queens County (New York), which dismissed her petition seeking to establish that respondent ex-boyfriend was the father of her child.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a petition with the family court seeking to establish that her ex-boyfriend was the father of her child. The family court dismissed the petition based upon human leucocyte antigen (HLA) testing that showed that there was no probability that the ex-boyfriend was the father. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal finding that the mother failed to meet her burden of showing that N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 532(a) was unconstitutional or that the family court erred in admitting the results of the HLA test. The court found that the HLA test was reliable in paternity actions and it was reasonable for the family court to rely upon the test results because a qualified expert testified with personal knowledge that the tests were prepared and kept in the regular course of business. The court found that although HLA test results were not definitive or conclusive of paternity, the family court, as the trier of fact, properly made its own assessment of the weight to be accorded to the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the mother's paternity petition.

Rubinstein v. Board of Elections


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

Therefore, the designating petition was not in compliance with § 6-134(2). The court also held that the statute was constitutional because the state had a compelling interest in preserving the integrity of their electoral process.
