Smith v. Anchorage Associates


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


122 A.D.2d 788; 505 N.Y.S.2d 673; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 59303



August 4, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff floating home owners challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County (New York), which dismissed their complaint against defendants, the marina owner and the town, that sought to declare Babylon, N.Y., Town Code § 213-107 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The owners floating homes were harbored at the marina. Section 213-107 restricted the mooring or docking of vessels designed for or occupied as dwelling units. Shortly after the ordinance was adopted, the marina owner filed a condominium offering plan expressly excluding parties who intended to dock floating homes. On appeal, the owners argued that they were entitled as a matter of law to purchase slips at the marina because they were tenants in occupancy on the date the condominium offering plan was accepted for filing. The court affirmed the dismissal of the owners' action because the marina owner extended exclusive purchase period rights and other incentives only to tenants possessing written occupancy agreements, which the owners did not possess. The offer was not extended to parties intending to dock floating homes and that restriction was reinforced through a restrictive covenant incorporated into the deeds to the slip units. Therefore, regardless of the ordinance, the owners are not entitled to remain at the marina.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the owners' action against the marina owner and the town that sought a declaration that an ordinance was unconstitutional.

 

632 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


N.Y. State Club Ass'n v. City of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


118 A.D.2d 392; 505 N.Y.S.2d 152; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 55168



July 31, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on November 22, 1985, affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court (New York) which denied a motion by the association for summary judgment and granted a cross motion by respondents, city and associated individuals, for summary judgment in an action to find that a local law violated the equal protection clause.


OVERVIEW: The association brought an action against respondents claiming that a certain local law violated the equal protection clause by defining what were "distinctly private" clubs within its compass. The association filed a motion for summary judgment and respondents filed a cross motion for summary judgment. The trial court granted respondents cross motion and the association appealed. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding that the local law did not violate the equal protection clause. The court found that the classification and exemptions were related to a permissible public purpose. The court held that the association's contention that the law was not one of general applicability and was unduly burdensome to those affected, was without basis. The legislative purpose of curtailing discriminatory practice in clubs whose character and operation made them public accommodations by clearly defined standards did not violate due process or the equal protection of the law, because the definition excluded other clubs. The court determined that the exemptions served a proper legislative purpose and that no unconstitutional burden was imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that denied the association's motion for summary judgment and granted respondents' motion for summary judgment in an action to find that a local law violated the equal protection clause.


HEADNOTES

Civil Rights -- Discrimination in Public Accommodation

In amending New York City's prohibition against invidious discrimination by clubs which are not "distinctly private", Local Laws, 1984, No. 63 of City of New York, which provides that any private exclusion will not apply for private clubs if they have more than 400 members and provide for regular meal service and regularly receive payment on behalf of a nonmember for furtherance of trade or business, but exempts from coverage private corporations incorporated under, or referred to in, the Benevolent Orders Law, the Education Law or the Religious Corporations Law, is constitutional. The purpose of Local Law No. 63 is to bring public organizations within the ambit of the City Human Rights Law, and there is no equal protection or due process violation in excluding [***2] benevolent orders which, by definition, are not public since their purpose is to benefit their members, or in excluding religious corporations, which are patently not engaged in commercial activity for the benefit of nonmembers. The legislative purpose of curtailing discriminatory practice in clubs whose character and operation make them public accommodations by clearly defined standards does not violate due process or the equal protection of the laws, because the definition excludes other clubs; the exemptions serve a proper legislative purpose and there is no unconstitutional burden imposed.

 

633 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Herzog Bros. Trucking, Inc. v. State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


122 A.D.2d 518; 504 N.Y.S.2d 878; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 59787



July 31, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state tax commission (the commission) sought review from the Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department (New York), which issued a preliminary injunction restraining the commission from taking any action in regard to imposing or collecting the taxes against appellee fuel supplier.


OVERVIEW: The fuel supplier provided gas to retail establishments within Indian reservations and a tax was assessed on the sale. Due to the lower cost, customers, other than those actually living on the reservations, came to buy the gas at lower prices avoiding taxation. The tax collecting authority desired to remedy the situation and amended the tax laws. The commission then attempted to retroactively collect taxes from the fuel supplier and an injunction was sought and obtained. From this, the commission sought review. On appeal, the court found that the amended laws did not appear unconstitutional. The court found that a main issue was whether the commission imposed a burden on the fuel supplier that exceeded the permissible "minimal burden of collection" standard and that this was in fact lacking. The court surmised that the fuel supplier failed to establish the clear likelihood of success on the merits required for a showing of their entitlement to a preliminary injunction. Therefore, the injunction was issued in error and the order was reversed.


OUTCOME: The preliminary injunction restraining the commission from taking any action in regard to imposing or collecting the taxes against the fuel supplier was reversed.

People v. Valdelamar


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


122 A.D.2d 289; 505 N.Y.S.2d 192; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 59636



July 28, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the sentences imposed by the Supreme Court, Queens County (New York), which convicted him on two counts of robbery in the first degree, grand larceny in the third degree, and attempted sodomy in the first degree, upon his pleas of guilty.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court affirmed the sentences for the convictions for robbery, but modified the sentences for the convictions for grand larceny and attempted sodomy. The court found that because the crimes for which defendant was convicted of grand larceny and attempted sodomy were committed prior to the effective date of the mandatory penalty assessment statute, the imposition of such assessments constituted an unconstitutional ex post facto penalty.


OUTCOME: The sentences imposed for the robbery in the first degree convictions were affirmed. The sentences imposed for the grand larceny in the third degree and attempted sodomy in the first degree convictions were modified by vacating the mandatory penalty assessments imposed. As so modified, the sentences were affirmed.

F. L. D. Constr. Corp. v. Williams


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


122 A.D.2d 189; 504 N.Y.S.2d 726; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 59522



July 21, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation and respondent Commissioner appealed the decision of the Supreme Court, Richmond County (New York), which partly affirmed and partly annulled the commissioner's decision regarding disputed property. The court held that the property was not subject to wetland regulation under N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law art. 25 and that the DEC had arbitrarily exerted jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Conservation (DEC) issued a tidal wetlands permit and a State Pollution Discharge Elimination System (SPEDES) permit to a corporation upon certain conditions and sought to dismantle a sewage plant on the corporation's property. The trial court affirmed in part and annulled in part the commissioner's decision, but the court reinstated the commissioner's decision and remitted the matter for a determination of constitutional issues related to the taking. Although the trial court found that the disputed property was not subject to wetland regulation under N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law art. 25, the court found that the commissioner's decision that the property was subject to such regulation was supported by substantial evidence and was neither arbitrary nor capricious. Further, the court found that the conditions that the commissioner placed upon granting of the SPEDES permit were reasonable and that the sewage plant was located within wetlands and subject to the authority of the DEC. Finally, the court noted that the trial court was obligated to consider the corporation's constitutional claims under N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law § 25-0404.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's decision to the extent that it annulled the commissioner's original directions. The court also remitted the matter for a determination regarding related constitutional issues.

 

636 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Nole v. Passidomo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


118 A.D.2d 326; 504 N.Y.S.2d 809; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 55156



July 17, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, on the law, without costs, motion granted, complaint dismissed and it is declared that Vehicle and Traffic Law § 318 is not unconstitutional as a violation of plaintiff's due process rights.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles of the State of New York and the Department of Motor Vehicles, appealed the decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which denied defendants' motion for summary judgement, in plaintiff registrant's declaratory judgment action challenging the suspension of her registration under N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 318 and alleging that § 318 violated the registrant's due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 318(1)(a), defendants suspended the registration of the registrant's vehicle for period of time representing the period of lapsed coverage in the registrant's insurance. The registrant filed a declaratory judgment, alleging that the suspension was issued in the absence of any evidence of legal termination of insurance or of lapse of insurance coverage, that § 318 did not permit a suspension of registration for lapsed insurance coverage when the registrant has re-obtained coverage at the time of the suspension, and that § 318 was unconstitutional in authorizing the suspension without affording the registrant a prior adversarial, evidentiary hearing. The trial court denied defendants' summary judgment motion. On review, the court reversed, ordering the dismissal of the action and declaring that §318 was constitutional. The registrant was precluded from pursuing the instant action to resolve factual issues involving the claims when she failed to pursue available administrative remedies. Also, defendants' actions were consistent with the statutory framework and the procedures applied to the registrant under § 318 satisfied the requirements of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment denying defendants' summary judgment motion, ordered the dismissal of the declaratory action filed by the registrant challenging the suspension of a vehicle registration, and declared that the statute under which the suspension was ordered did not violate the registrant's due process.


HEADNOTES

Declaratory Judgments -- When Remedy Appropriate

1. In a declaratory judgment action challenging the suspension of the registration of plaintiff's vehicle pursuant to Vehicle and Traffic Law § 318 for a period representing the number of days of lapsed insurance coverage, defendants' motion for summary judgment should have been granted. To the extent that summary judgment was denied on the ground that a proper determination of the complaint requires resolution of the outstanding issues of fact described in plaintiff's opposing papers, a declaratory judgment action was an inappropriate method to review defendants' administrative actions. Plaintiff is precluded from basing her suit on claims that there was in fact no lapse in coverage or that her insurer's notice of termination was improper;  [***2] there is no proof that plaintiff submitted evidence at the administrative level to support these claims or that she pursued her administrative remedies to show that she had valid, continuous insurance coverage, as she was invited to do in two letters from defendants.

Motor Vehicles -- Suspension of Registration Due to Lapsed Insurance Coverage

2. In an action wherein plaintiff challenged the suspension of the registration of her vehicle pursuant to Vehicle and Traffic Law § 318 for a period representing the number of days of lapsed insurance coverage, defendants' motion for summary judgment should have been granted. In ordering suspension on the basis of plaintiff's insurer's notification that the proof of insurance was no longer in effect and in extending that suspension for the period during which, on the basis of the available evidence, there was a lapse in coverage, defendants' actions were completely consistent with the statutory framework (see, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 312 [1] [a]; § 318 [1-a] [a]), and there is no basis upon which an estoppel can be applied against defendants.

Motor Vehicles -- Suspension of Registration Due to Lapsed Insurance  [***3] Coverage

3. In an action wherein plaintiff challenged the suspension of the registration of her vehicle pursuant to Vehicle and Traffic Law § 318 for a period representing the number of days of lapsed insurance coverage, defendants' motion for summary judgment should have been granted. The issue of the existence of coverage and proper termination thereof is one of relative simplicity, largely determinable on the basis of documentary evidence; a registrant can be relieved of any suspension imposed for lapse of coverage merely by paying a civil penalty of $ 4 for each day during which no insurance was in effect (Vehicle and Traffic Law § 318 [1-a] [b]); judicial review is available through a CPLR article 78 proceeding; and the burden and delay in having to hold a full, evidentiary hearing before suspension in every case would largely thwart the strong State policy to bar uninsured vehicles from the public highways. Minimal due process requirements of notice and an opportunity to be heard were complied with, since plaintiff received advance notification of the proposed suspension and the basis therefor and was invited to submit proof of continued, valid coverage; accordingly,  [***4] Vehicle and Traffic Law § 318 is not unconstitutional as a violation of plaintiff's due process rights.

Leemhuis v. New York State Public Employees Federation


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


121 A.D.2d 796; 504 N.Y.S.2d 248; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 58763



June 19, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee and defendant union cross appealed from the decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which granted the union's motion to dismiss the employee's amended complaint for failure to exhaust administrative remedies and declared a portion of the union's agency shop fee rebate procedure improper.


OVERVIEW: The union represented the employee's division. He was not a union member but agency shop fees equal to membership dues were deducted from his salary pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 208(3)(a). In 1982 and 1983 the employee timely requested the return of that portion of his fees that was used to support ideological causes not germane to collective bargaining activities. He received small refunds for both years. The employee filed suit, alleging that N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 208(3) violated U.S. Constitution amends. I, XIV and sought, among other things, an injunction to prevent the union from spending agency shop fees on impermissible services. The union filed a motion to dismiss, which the lower court granted. The parties cross-appealed and the court reversed only that part of the lower court's order that granted the union's motion to dismiss. The court held that the lower court erred in granting the motion because the employee's objection to the assessment of agency shop fees was timely filed and because his argument was primarily a challenge to the constitutionality of the union's procedures, he had not needed to demonstrate an exhaustion of his administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court modified the decision of the lower court by reversing that part of the order that granted the union's motion to dismiss the amended complaint for failure to exhaust administrative remedies, but otherwise affirmed the decision of the lower court.

 

641 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


McCain v. Koch


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


117 A.D.2d 198; 502 N.Y.S.2d 720; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 52475



May 13, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on June 27, 1984, which granted plaintiffs' (McCain et al.) motion for a preliminary injunction, unanimously modified, on the law, the motion for a preliminary injunction denied and the injunction vacated, and as so modified, otherwise affirmed, without costs and without disbursements; the order of said court entered on June 27, 1984, which denied the municipal defendants' motion to vacate the temporary restraining order is unanimously reversed, on the law, and the motion to vacate is granted, without costs and without disbursements; and the order of said court entered on November 9, 1984, is unanimously affirmed, without costs and without disbursements; the order of said court entered on May 30, 1985, is unanimously reversed, on the law, the facts, and in the exercise of discretion, and the motion for intervention, class action status and a [***3] preliminary injunction is granted, without costs and without disbursements; and the order of said court entered on June 29, 1984, is unanimously modified, on the law, the motion for class certification is denied, the cross motion of the respondent State Commissioner to dismiss the petition is granted and the proceeding is dismissed against him, and, as so modified, the order is affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeless families sought review of orders issued by the Supreme Court at Special Term, New York County (New York) in the consolidated cases brought against defendants, mayor and city and state social service agency officials, to obtain suitable emergency housing, due process rights upon transfer from emergency housing, and funds for the transportation of school children.


OVERVIEW: In the two consolidated cases plaintiff homeless families sought injunctive relief requiring defendants, mayor and city and state social services officials, to provide plaintiff with suitable emergency shelter, school transportation allowances, and notice and hearing prior to termination of emergency shelter. On appeal from lower court orders, the court first prohibited defendants from denying emergency shelter to plaintiff, citing the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, social services statutes, and N.Y. Const. art. XVII, § 1. The court then concluded that N.Y Const. art. XVII, § 1 did not entitle plaintiff to any standard of suitability with regard to emergency shelter. Additionally, the court held that emergency shelter residents had no due process right upon transfer and that the assignment of families to mass shelters was permissible. Finally, the court required plaintiff's automatic entitlement to a school transportation allowance when residing in emergency shelter. The court reversed the orders involving the provision of emergency shelter and due process rights, modified the transportation allowance ruling, and affirmed the mass shelter order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed orders in plaintiff homeless families' case against defendants, mayor and city and state social services agency officials, and thereby required that emergency shelter be provided to plaintiff and denied due process rights upon transfer. The court modified the transportation allowance order to make funds available automatically, and affirmed the order permitting plaintiff's placement in mass shelters.


HEADNOTES

Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families

1. An order which denied a motion by proposed plaintiffs-intervenors, homeless families who allegedly had unsuccessfully requested emergency shelter from defendants, to intervene in an action commenced against defendants by other homeless families concerning their entitlement to emergency shelter, and for a preliminary injunction barring defendants from denying shelter to eligible families is reversed. The provision of emergency housing to the proposed intervenors did not moot their claims; the questions presented are of public importance and significance, likely to recur and yet evade review; thus, a preliminary injunction barring denial of emergency shelter to homeless families is granted.

 [***4] Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families -- Preliminary Injunction

2. Plaintiffs, homeless families with children, are entitled to a preliminary injunction barring State and municipal defendants who are charged with the administration of programs to assist homeless families in locating housing, from denying emergency shelter to homeless families. The irreparable injury to be sustained by homeless families clearly outweighs the burden that providing temporary emergency shelter imposes upon defendants, and plaintiffs have demonstrated a high probability of success on the merits. Further, public interest strongly favors an injunction pending a final determination on the merits.

Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families -- State Plan for Emergency Assistance to Needy Families with Children

3. In an action seeking a preliminary injunction barring State and municipal defendants who are charged with the administration of programs to assist homeless families in locating housing, from denying emergency shelter to homeless families, plaintiffs have a high probability of establishing that defendant City of New York is mandated to provide [***5] emergency shelter to eligible families for 30 days in one 12-month period pursuant to the State Plan for Emergency Assistance to Needy Families with Children (EAF). The State's participation in the EAF program obligates the New York City Department of Social Services (City DSS), budgetary constraints notwithstanding, to secure the amount of emergency shelter necessary for homeless families found within the City's borders; the duty to provide emergency assistance is not limited to the provision of cash benefits and ancillary services. Moreover, plaintiffs have a high probability of establishing that in failing to assure emergency shelter for all eligible homeless families, both the State and City DSS have violated the Social Security Act requirement of mandatory enforcement of the State Plan (42 USC § 602 [a] [1]).

Constitutional Law -- Equal Protection of Laws -- Denial of Emergency Shelter to Homeless Families

4. Under the equal protection guarantees of the State and Federal Constitutions, any classification which denies to one class of needy persons public assistance which is available to all others, cannot be justified unless it is rationally related to a legitimate [***6] State interest. Thus, since defendant City of New York makes emergency shelter available to homeless single men, there is no apparent reasonable basis for the City's denial of emergency shelter to plaintiffs, homeless families with children; the needs of plaintiffs are greater than those of single adults, and defendants' less than equal treatment of plaintiffs is plainly irrational.

Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families -- Duty of State to Aid Needy

5. The policy of defendant New York City Department of Social Services in administering the State Plan for Emergency Assistance to Needy Families with Children to only provide cash allowances and information concerning housing availability rather than to provide emergency shelter for homeless families contravenes both the letter and spirit of the State's affirmative obligation to aid all its needy residents under NY Constitution, article XVII, § 1. Article XVII was intended to require the State to take positive steps to assist the needy, and the provision for assistance is a positive duty, not a matter of legislative grace. In view of the scarcity of decent low-income housing, the City's policy simply [***7] ignores the brutal realities of plaintiffs' situation and amounts to a denial of aid to homeless families.

Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families -- Minimal Standards for Housing

6. It was error to compel the State and municipal defendants to comply with reasonable, minimal standards of cleanliness, warmth, space and rudimentary conveniences in providing emergency shelter to plaintiffs, homeless families with children. The adequacy of the level of welfare benefits is a matter committed to the discretion of the Legislature. Although plaintiffs have documented the unsafe and squalid conditions prevalent in welfare hotel accommodations, the emergency housing provided by defendants is more than token, and is genuine and meaningful. Thus, in light of the Legislature's broad discretion, plaintiffs are not likely to prove that NY Constitution article XVII substantively guarantees minimal physical standards in emergency shelter.

Injunctions -- When Injunctive Relief Appropriate

7. The codification of more extensive minimal standards for emergency shelter for homeless families with children in 18 NYCRR 352.3 than those contained in an interim order [***8] granted in an action by plaintiffs, homeless families with children, against the State and municipal defendants who administer programs to assist homeless families in locating housing, did not render partially moot defendants' challenge to a preliminary injunction, which compelled defendants to comply with the minimal standards contained in the interim order. The issuance of the regulations obviated the need for injunctive relief essentially duplicative in nature. Moreover, since the system of procedural safeguards for such homeless families delineated in the interim order duplicates those already set forth more extensively in social services regulations, and only isolated instances of violations of those safeguards exist, injunctive relief compelling defendants to comply with the safeguards contained in the order was unwarranted.

Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families -- Hearing before Transfer to Alternate Facility -- Due Process

8. In an action by plaintiffs, homeless families with children, against municipal defendants who administer programs to assist homeless families in locating housing, an order which denied defendants' motion to vacate a temporary [***9] restraining order prohibiting transfer of emergency shelter recipients to alternate facilities until notice and an opportunity to be heard were given is reversed. The requirement for a hearing before transfer interferes with the newly established State inspection procedures for hotel and motel facilities set forth in 18 NYCRR 352.3 (h) and would often effectively preclude relocation since alternative placements would become unavailable pending a hearing. Moreover, emergency shelter residents do not have a due process right to be housed in any particular neighborhood or type of housing.

Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families - Mass Shelters

9. In an action by plaintiffs, homeless families with children, against the State and municipal defendants who administer programs to assist homeless families in locating housing, the closing of mass shelters for homeless families will not be compelled in light of the broad discretion vested in the Legislature regarding the adequacy of the level of welfare benefits. While mass shelters are not good environments, they afford families food, security, outdoor recreational space, and social services which do not exist [***10] at emergency hotel placements.

Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families -- Responsibility of State Commissioner of Social Services

10. A proceeding against respondent Commissioners of the State Department of Social Services (DSS) and the New York City Department of Social Services seeking a preliminary injunction requiring respondent Commissioners to provide emergency housing to petitioners, homeless families with children, within the area where their minor children attend school or to provide transportation allowances based on actual costs where necessary, is dismissed as to respondent State Commissioner. Social Services Law § 62 places primary responsibility upon the local social services agencies for the delivery of services and assistance to needy families; only the City DSS is the relevant party because it alone is accountable for the direct payment of actual transportation expenses incurred by or for relocation of homeless families.

Social Services -- Emergency Housing for Homeless Families -- School Transportation Allowance

11. Under NY Constitution, article XI, § 1 and Education Law article 65, the State must provide free education [***11] to all children over age five; moreover, Education Law § 3209 squarely places responsibility upon public welfare officials in local social services districts to provide indigent children with the necessaries to enable them to attend school, which include funds for school transportation. Accordingly, respondent New York City Department of Social Services policy of providing a flat travel allowance of $ 18 per week to eligible homeless families residing in emergency shelters whose children must commute to school is inadequate and is unconstitutional in that it deprives indigent children of the right to free education and amounts to a refusal to aid needy children; respondent is obligated to provide actual transportation expenses, both for children until they obtain transportation passes from the Board of Education, and for the parents of young children who must be accompanies to school. Moreover, Social Services Law § 350-j and 18 NYCRR 372.4 (d) also mandate payment of such transportation expenses; homeless families who are eligible for emergency shelter under the program for Emergency Assistance to Needy Families with Children are automatically entitled to a transportation allowance [***12] if they have been relocated at a distance from their former communities and their children's schools.

Actions -- Class Actions

12. A determination granting class action certification in a proceeding seeking to compel respondent Commissioner of the Department of Social Services of the City of New York to provide emergency housing to petitioners within the area where their minor children attend school or to provide transportation allowances based on actual costs for children and for their parents where necessary is reversed; class certification is superfluous where there is no evidence of unwillingness on the part of respondent government official to comply with and apply court rulings equally to all persons similarly situated.

Velasquez v. Perales


No. 25349


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 49989



May 6, 1986 



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Judgment of Supreme Court, New York County (Allen Murray Myers, J.), entered February 15, 1984, holding that Social Services Law §131-a(10) which denied eligibility for home relief to persons whose gross income exceeded 150% of the State standard of need was unconstitutional, certifying a class and granting a permanent injunction against enforcement of the statute with retroactive relief from its limits, unanimously reversed on the law, the complaint is dismissed and the class certification vacated as moot, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commissioner appealed from a Judgment of Supreme Court, New York County (New York) holding that N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 131-a(10) was unconstitutional and granting plaintiff class members a permanent injunction against enforcement of the statute with retroactive relief from its limits.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 131-a(10) denied eligibility for home relief to persons whose gross income exceeded 150% of the state standard of need. The parties agreed to hold the appeal in abeyance pending the outcome of a related appeal addressing the same issues. The statute was upheld as constitutional in the related appeal and the court reversed the judgment. The court also concluded that it was improper to certify the action as a class action and vacated the class certification as moot. The court held that stare decisis was sufficient to protect all similarly situated class members because government action was involved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment finding the statute unconstitutional and the class certification was vacated as moot.

 

643 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Goodwin v. Perales


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


120 A.D.2d 527; 501 N.Y.S.2d 1007; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 56595



May 5, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner recipients appealed a judgment from the Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York), which dismissed their consolidated petitions to review determinations of respondent commissioner of social services (commissioner) affirming the local agency determination deducting the full amount of the interim Home Relief grants from their Supplemental Security grants.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the recipients' consolidated petitions to review determinations of the commissioner affirming the local agency determination deducting the full amount of interim Home Relief grants from their Supplemental Security grants. On appeal, the recipients contended that the state irrationally discriminated against Home Relief recipients who had become eligible for Federal Supplemental Security Income grants. The trial court's judgment was affirmed. The court held that during the interim assistance period the recipients' were not eligible for Supplemental Security Income grants. The uncontroverted facts amply demonstrated that the recipients' actual benefit receipts never fell below their state needs standard for any month within the interim assistance period. Thus, the recoupment did not irrationally discriminate against Home Relief recipients who had become eligible for Federal Supplemental Security Income grants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment dismissing the recipients' consolidated petitions to review the commissioner's determination that the full amount of the recipients' interim Home Relief grants could be deducted from their Supplemental Security Income grants.

 

644 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Leichter v. Barber


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


120 A.D.2d 776; 501 N.Y.S.2d 925; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 56914



May 1, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), that granted partial summary judgment in favor of defendant New York State Job Incentive Board in the taxpayer's declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer sought declaratory and injunctive relief concerning the board's procedure in determining eligibility for tax credits against corporate franchise taxes. The trial court granted the board's cross motion for partial summary judgment dismissing the first three causes of action in the complaint. The court affirmed on the merits. The board was not required to formally promulgate, in accordance with the State Administrative Procedure Act, its policy regarding the calculation of jobs created by expanding an existing corporation because the policy did not constitute a rule or regulation. Rather, the guideline was an interpretive statement that in itself had no legal effect, but was merely explanatory. The policy was drafted in response to staff requests for guidelines to aid them in giving advice and assistance to applicants. Although the guideline was developed when the board was attempting to establish a set of objective criteria to be determinative in each case, during the period the board did not consider the policy either fixed or determinative. When the board finally developed fixed, determinative standards, it formally promulgated rules and regulations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the board's partial summary judgment motion in the taxpayer's declaratory judgment action.

 

645 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


County of Rensselaer v. Troy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


120 A.D.2d 796; 501 N.Y.S.2d 534; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 56927



May 1, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which granted summary judgment for plaintiff county and ordered the city to pay the entire amount of taxes which the county levied upon the city pursuant to 1918 N.Y. Laws 209, § 9 (Law), and prior to the effective date of the amendment to the city charter, which repealed the Law.


OVERVIEW: The county levied taxes upon the city pursuant to the Law. While the city had the power to repeal the Law, the city failed to specifically identify its intent to do so when it adopted its new city charter. The city then amended its charter to specifically and expressly repeal the Law. Subsequently, the city did not pay the entire amount of taxes which the county levied. The county commenced an action to recover the deficiency, and was awarded summary judgment for the unpaid amount by the special term. In affirming summary judgment for the county, the court held that the amendment that repealed the law could not have been given retroactive effect. The court held that the city incurred the obligation to pay, and the county acquired a vested property right in the taxes levied when the final levy was in place, and the subsequent amendment could not have prevented the county from obtaining the second half of the entire amount of the levy from the city. Further, the court held that retroactive application in that situation was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for the county against the city.

 

646 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Burns v. Egan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


117 A.D.2d 38; 501 N.Y.S.2d 742; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51042



April 24, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which granted a motion for summary judgment by respondents, tax commissioner and associated individuals, in an action initiated by appellants challenging their right to vote under N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 11 and the constitutionality of the Prison Construction Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers initiated action against respondents, tax commissioner and associated individuals, challenging their right to vote under N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 11 and the constitutionality of the Prison Construction Act, which authorized respondents to finance and develop prisons. The trial court granted respondents' motion for summary judgment, and appellants sought review. The court found that neglect in asserting a right for an unreasonable length of time might have barred an action pursuant to the doctrine of laches. The court held that the essential element of laches was delay prejudicial to the opposing party. In this case, the action was barred by laches because adverse judicial action would have caused unacceptable disorder and confusion. The court held that the doctrine of res judicata was also applicable because it had been previously determined that appellants lacked standing on the merits. The court affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which dismissed appellant taxpayers' action against respondents, tax commissioner and associated individuals, in action challenging the constitutionality of the Prison Construction Act. The court held that the action was barred by laches because delay was prejudicial to respondents. Res judicata was applicable because it had previously been determined that appellants lacked standing.


HEADNOTES

Equity -- Laches -- Res Judicata

The doctrine of laches bars an action by five individual plaintiffs challenging, as citizens, taxpayers and voters, the constitutionality of the Prison Construction Act (L 1983, ch 56, as amended by L 1983, chs 712, 713), which authorized defendant Urban Development Corporation (UDC) to finance and develop prisons using $ 380 million to be raised by the issuance of bonds and notes, as violative of their rights to vote under NY Constitution, article VII, § 11, which mandates a public referendum before the State undertakes to incur a long-term debt. The original complaint, identifying plaintiffs as residents, citizens and taxpayers, served more than four months after the effective date of the Act, both could, and should have, asserted the individual plaintiffs'  [***2] claims as voters and it was not until some 16 months later, after dismissal of that first action was affirmed by the Court of Appeals on the ground that plaintiffs had no standing as citizen taxpayers (see, New York State Coalition for Criminal Justice v Coughlin, 103 AD2d 40, affd 64 NY2d 660), that plaintiffs commenced the instant action, finally pleading their status as voters; additionally, since defendants waited almost two years while plaintiffs exhausted all appeals in their citizen-taxpayer action before the sale of bonds by UDC, and in the meantime, have commenced construction of correctional facilities and sold bonds for approximately $ 294 million, adverse judicial action at this juncture would cause unacceptable disorder and confusion. Alternatively, relitigation of the standing issue is barred by the doctrine of res judicata, since plaintiffs' present challenge emanates from the same factual source as the earlier litigation and centers around the exact same issue and at the time of the initial lawsuit plaintiffs were voters and had the opportunity to sue in that capacity; the previous determination that plaintiffs lacked standing was on the merits insofar as the [***3] standing issue is concerned and res judicata pertains not only to matters actually litigated, but also to any which might readily have been litigated.

Cosmo Realty Corp. v. Scruggs-Leftwich


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


118 A.D.2d 826; 500 N.Y.S.2d 538; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 54676



March 31, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a judgment of the Supreme Court in Westchester County (New York), which denied their motion for summary judgment and granted a motion filed by defendant, the New York State Division of Housing and Community Renewal, for summary judgment in plaintiffs' action seeking a declaration that the Laws of 1983 and the Mount Vernon resolution of July 15, 1983, which reestablished rent control, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The statute was enacted in order to deal with the emergency created by plaintiffs' demands for dramatic rent increases. In response, plaintiffs filed an action seeking to have the statute declared unconstitutional. The court held that plaintiffs failed to meet their burden of proof. Although the legislature's method of dealing with the crisis may not have been the only one possible, and may not even have been the best solution, the legislature's response to the crisis was neither irrational nor unreasonable, and therefore was constitutional. The Division was entitled to have its interpretation of the regulating statute upheld because that construction was not irrational.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment and granting the Division's motion for summary judgment.

McNulty v. New York State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


118 A.D.2d 1041; 500 N.Y.S.2d 415; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 54825



March 27, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which dismissed the taxpayers' application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to review a determination of respondent, the New York State Tax Commission, which sustained a personal income tax assessment imposed pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 22 by the Audit Division of the Department of Taxation and Finance.


OVERVIEW: Until the taxpayers moved from New York to New Jersey, one had been a partner in a New York City law firm, and his distributive share of the partnership income was the taxpayers' principal source of income. Pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 654(a), petitioners properly filed a resident and a nonresident return for the year at issue, prorating their income, exemptions, and deductions over the two periods as required by § 654(a). After an audit, the Division assessed additional income tax, finding that all the partnership income belonged on the nonresident return, and the taxpayers complained that they thus received no benefit from the exemptions and deductions prorated to the resident period. The Commission sustained the assessment, the trial court dismissed the taxpayers' petition for review on the merits, and the court affirmed. Since gain or loss could not be determined until the end of the taxable year under N.Y. Tax Law § 364, it was plainly required that the entire partnership income be included on the nonresident return. It was the taxpayers' own change of residency that caused the result of which they complained, and they should have been aware of the problem when they moved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the taxpayers' petition for review of the Commission's determination that sustained the Department's assessment of additional tax.

Carlino v. Albany


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


118 A.D.2d 928; 499 N.Y.S.2d 814; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 54763



March 6, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured motorist appealed from an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which, upon reargument, dismissed his complaint against defendants, City of Albany and County of Albany (county), in his action charging that each municipality had breached a duty to maintain a road. The county appealed from the earlier denial of its cross motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint against it.


OVERVIEW: The injured motorist brought an action against defendants charging that each municipality had breached a duty to maintain the road upon which he was injured. Upon reargument, the supreme court dismissed the complaint against defendants, and the injured motorist appealed. The county also appealed from the supreme court's earlier order denying its cross motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed the supreme court's dismissal of the insured motorist's complaint, holding that no conflict existed between the City of Albany, N.Y., Local Laws, No. 1, § 1 (1953) and N.Y. Second Class Cities Law § 244 because the dictates of the Second Class Cities Law only applied by the statute's own terms, until superseded pursuant to the municipal home rule law. The City of Albany's local law was superseding; hence it was enforceable. With regard to the county's cross appeal, the court reversed so much of the supreme court's order as granted the county's motion for summary judgment, denied the motion, and as so modified affirmed. The court held that whether the county did have constructive notice of the defect in the road was a contested fact issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the supreme court's order, which denied the injured motorist's motion for partial summary judgment against the City of Albany and the county and the county's cross motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint against it. The court modified the supreme court's subsequent order by reversing so much thereof as granted the county's motion for summary judgment, denied the motion, and so modified, affirmed.

Memorial Hospital v. Axelrod


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


118 A.D.2d 938; 499 N.Y.S.2d 505; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 54768



March 6, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, dismissed the hospital's petition to annul a determination of respondent, Commissioner of the New York State Department of Health (commissioner), that found the hospital in violation of N.Y. Pub. Health Law §§ 206, 2803.


OVERVIEW: An administrative law judge found the hospital in violation of N.Y. Pub. Health Law §§ 206, 2803, and fined the hospital $ 4,000 for the hospital's refusal to allow the department of health access to examine certain patients. The commissioner sustained the charges and the fine. The supreme court at special term confirmed the determination and dismissed the hospital's petition to annul the commissioner's determination. On review, the court modified the judgment by reversing the $ 4,000 fine and reducing it to $ 1,000, and as modified, affirmed. The court ruled that the 1981 amendment to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2803(1)(a), adding specific language authorizing patient observation in inspections of residential health care facilities, did not evince a legislative intent to take away the commissioner's concomitant right to inspect hospitals. The court ruled that the legislature intended that the amendment be cumulative, not exclusive. Thus, the department of health was authorized to observe and examine patients in the hospital and the hospital's refusal to allow such inspection was a violation of the statute. The court found, however, that there was only one instance of refusal.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the supreme court at special term, which confirmed the commissioner's determination and dismissed the hospital's petition, by reversing the $ 4,000 fine and reducing it to $ 1,000, and as modified, affirmed.

Gimbel Bros., Inc. v. Brook Shopping Centers, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


118 A.D.2d 532; 499 N.Y.S.2d 435; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 54401



March 3, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessee filed suit against defendants, a lessor and its agent (lessor), seeking a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief. The Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), entered judgment for the lessee, finding that the lessee had no duty to pay Sunday charges under the lease but denying the lessee the right to set off past charges against future rent payments. The lessor appealed, and the lessee cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lessee had entered into the lease in question in 1955. The lease contained no reference to Sunday openings, but state law, N.Y. Bus. Law § 9, prohibited such openings. In 1976, § 9 was held to be unconstitutional. The lessee opened on Sunday for the first time in 1976 and paid $ 10 per Sunday to the former landlord. The current lessor increased the charge, which was paid by the lessee until 1978. The court held that (1) the trial court properly found that the lessee had no duty to pay Sunday charges under the lease and that the lessor was not entitled to reformation of the lease; (2) the lessee was properly denied restitution of the Sunday charges it had pervasively paid when such payments were made voluntarily and the lessee was not operating under a mistake of law or fact; and (3) the trial court's injunctive declaration was erroneous when the injunction did little more than compel the lessor to respect the lessee's rights under the lease and did not clearly apprise the lessor as to what actions were enjoined.


OUTCOME: The court deleted the grant of injunctive relief from the judgment under review but otherwise affirmed the judgment.

People v. Snow


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

117 A.D.2d 1019; 499 N.Y.S.2d 562; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 53280



February 21, 1986 

 

653 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. Regan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


114 A.D.2d 187; 498 N.Y.S.2d 557; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 49968



February 13, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed, on the law, without costs, and petitions dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant comptroller sought review of seven judgments from the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which, in proceedings pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, annulled the comptroller's decisions to suspend the payment of retirement benefits to respondent employees.


OVERVIEW: The employees filed for retirement between the date of reelection to their judicial offices in November and the following January, when their reelection terms commenced. Each employee received retirement benefits in addition to a judicial salary under a procedure sanctioned by custom under N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 150. After § 150 was amended, the comptroller notified the employees that the retirement benefits would be suspended. They instituted N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 proceedings on the ground that the action violated N.Y. Const. art. V, § 7. The trial court held that amended N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 150 could not be constitutionally applied to those who retired before its effective date and directed payment to the employees. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the intention of the legislature when it enacted § 150 was to encourage retirees to run for public office, but it was not applicable to employees who filed for retirement from their judicial offices after their reelection to such offices and before the commencement of their new terms. The amendment to § 150, which amplified that intent, was not a change in the law; thus, there was no constitutional impairment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and dismissed the employees' petitions.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Retirement and Pension Benefits

1. Judgments annulling a determination of respondent Comptroller suspending the payment of retirement benefits to petitioners are reversed and the petitions dismissed, petitioners having filed for retirement benefits between the date of reelection to their respective judicial offices in November and the following January 1, when their reelection terms commenced; after commencement of their new terms, each petitioner began receiving retirement benefits in addition to a full judicial salary pursuant to respondents' interpretation of the "elective public office" exception contained in Civil Service Law § 150, which generally suspends the retirement benefits of persons who, subsequent to their retirement [***2] from State service, accept public office, but following the effective date of a 1984 amendment to section 150 providing that any person who, subsequent to his retirement from an elective public office, is reelected, shall have his retirement allowance suspended, petitioners were notified that their retirement benefits would be suspended immediately. The "elective public office" exception contained in Civil Service Law § 150 prior to the amendment did not apply to petitioners, all of whom filed for retirement from their judicial offices after their reelection to such offices and before the commencement of their new terms in such offices; the purpose of the statute was to encourage retired public officers to run for elective public office, and since the amendment did not effect a substantive change in Civil Service Law § 150 as to petitioners, there has been no unconstitutional impairment of their retirement benefits or vested contractual rights; further, the doctrine of estoppel is not applicable to create rights to retirement benefits to which there is no entitlement.

Appeal -- Matters Reviewable

2. Although generally an appellate court will not review any issue not [***3] raised in the pleadings or at Special Term, an exception to this rule exists when the particular matter involves something undeniable, or which in any event would not generate factual issues needing trial-level resolution; accordingly, the issue of legislative intent, which does not present factual issues, may be raised at the appellate level for the first time.

 

654 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Standard Mfg. Co. v. Tax Com. of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


114 A.D.2d 138; 498 N.Y.S.2d 724; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 49854



January 30, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, and petition dismissed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought review of the decision from respondent Tax Commission of the State of New York (Commissioner), which sustained notices of deficiency issued to the taxpayer for its failure to file a franchise tax report for a corporation located in Puerto Rico that was under the same ownership as the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer and a Puerto Rican company were both owned by the same three stockholders and had the same board of directors. The Puerto Rican company sold 90 percent of its product to the taxpayer and did no advertising for other sales. The state issued a notice of deficiency to the taxpayer for failure to file a franchise report for the Puerto Rican company and the taxpayer filed a petition for redetermination. The commissioner denied the petition and the taxpayer challenged the decision. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the franchise report was necessary under N.Y. Tax Law § 211(4) to properly reflect the taxpayer's tax liability. The undisputed facts showed that the two companies were engaged in a unitary business, had substantial inter-corporate transactions, and were under the same ownership. Thus, a combined report fulfilled the statutory purpose of more realistically portraying true income. The tax did not conflict with federal legislation granting a tax credit for investment in companies located in United States territories because Congress did not clearly manifest an intention to preempt state police powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax deficiencies levied against the taxpayer.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Franchise Tax on Business Corporations

A determination of the State Tax Commission sustaining a franchise tax assessment imposed upon petitioner, a New York corporation engaged in the manufacture, purchase and sale of outerwear clothing, in connection with its failure to file a franchise tax report for its wholly owned subsidiary, a Delaware corporation with its principal place of business in Puerto Rico engaged in the manufacture and sale of "activewear", is confirmed. There was ample evidence to support the Commission's conclusion that petitioner and its subsidiary were engaged in a unitary business and had substantial intercorporate transactions; under all the circumstances, combined reporting fulfills the purpose of Tax Law § 211 (4) of avoiding distortion [***2] of and more realistically portraying true income; requiring petitioner to file a combined tax return is not preempted by the supremacy clause (US Const, art VI, § 2), since Federal legislation providing a tax credit for taxable income received from sources outside the United States attributable to the conduct of a business within a United States possession is not at variance with the New York statute (Tax Law § 209 [1]) in that the power to tax exists independently of the Federal Constitution and a State's power to tax can coexist with a predominantly Federal power such as the regulation of commerce. Finally, New York net income is to be computed without deducting the amount of a tax credit permitted under Federal law and since there is clearly provision for inclusion of the amount of a tax credit, there is no usurpation of a legislative function.

Murphy v. Kelley


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


116 A.D.2d 967; 498 N.Y.S.2d 537; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51735



January 30, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a juvenile criminal defendant, sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court at Special Term for Clinton County (New York), which dismissed his application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to compel respondent district attorney to consent to the removal of the criminal action against petitioner to the Family Court of Clinton County and/or to declare N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 210.43(1)(b) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed petitioner's application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to compel respondent district attorney to consent to the removal of the criminal action against petitioner to the Family Court of Clinton County and/or to declare N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 210.43(1)(b) unconstitutional. Upon review, the court affirmed, holding that a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 was not the proper method to obtain mandamus in this case. The court held that because the demand concerned a judgmental act as opposed to a clerical or ministerial act, the application was properly dismissed. The court held that the petition was also properly dismissed because it was not filed within the four-month statute of limitation period as provided in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 217.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Cavaioli v. Board of Trustees


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


116 A.D.2d 689; 498 N.Y.S.2d 7; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51544



January 27, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York), which granted defendant trustees' motion to dismiss the employees' complaint as to the constitutionality of N.Y. Educ. Law § 355-a, which delegated the task of salary determination to the trustees.


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose between the employees and the trustees as to whether the authority delegated to them by § 355-a was constitutional. The employees sought a declaration that it was not. The lower court granted the trustees' motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court modified the lower court's judgment by declaring that § 355-a was constitutional and otherwise affirmed the judgment. The trustees were properly delegated the task of determining a salary schedule for a state university system's professional employees. That determination was not susceptible to rigid formulas. Nevertheless, the enabling legislation was constitutional because it provided sufficient guidelines for the trustees. Nor was the schedule unconstitutional or arbitrary and unreasonable based on its distinction between employees of two and four-year colleges. As to the employees' claim for back pay, they failed even though the lower court should have retained jurisdiction over them. That was so because the claims were based on the premise that the salary schedule was arbitrary, which the court rejected.


OUTCOME: The court modified the lower court's judgment by declaring that the delegation of salary determination to the trustees was constitutional. The judgment dismissing the employees' complaint was otherwise affirmed.

 

657 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Alweis v. Evans


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


114 A.D.2d 85; 497 N.Y.S.2d 800; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 49844



January 24, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously reversed on the law with costs to plaintiffs and judgment granted, in accordance with opinion by Boomer, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant administrative judges challenged the order of the Supreme Court of Monroe County (New York), which awarded summary judgment to plaintiff court reporters, declared that N.Y. Jud. Law §299 and N.Y. Jud. Law § 302 were not in conflict, and declared null and void administrative directives that compelled trial judges to order transcripts pursuant to a particular section of the N.Y. Judiciary Law.


OVERVIEW: The court reporters brought an action against the administrative judges seeking relief against directives requiring them to furnish transcripts free of charge upon request and declaring that N.Y. Jud. Law §299 was void. The trial court declared that N.Y. Jud. Law §§ 299, 302, were not in conflict, and that those sections empowered the trial court, in its sole discretion, to determine if transcripts should be ordered under N.Y. Jud. Law § 299 free of charge, or under N.Y. Jud. Law § 302 whereby the stenographer was to be paid. The trial court also declared null and void directives that compelled trial judges to order a transcript pursuant to a particular section of the Judiciary Law. The court held that N.Y. Jud. Law § 299 and N.Y. Jud. Law § 302 could not be reconciled and that N.Y. Jud. Law § 299 had been repealed by implication. The court ruled that the trial judges did not have the authority to determine whether a court reporter would be paid for transcripts. The court declared that § 299 had been repealed by the 1936 amendment to N.Y. Jud. Law § 302.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- Court Reporters -- Payment for Furnishing Transcript upon Request of Judge

 Judiciary Law § 299, which provides that the trial court may order transcripts from stenographers free of charge, and Judiciary Law § 302, which provides that stenographers are to be paid for such transcripts, cannot be reconciled and, inasmuch as section 302 embodies the latest expression of legislative intent, section 299 has been repealed by implication. Nothing in the language of these sections indicates [***2] a legislative intent to permit the Trial Judge to decide whether a court reporter should be paid for transcripts ordered by him; moreover, such a construction would be unreasonable; the Legislature has provided no standards for the exercise of such discretion; nor do these sections delegate authority to the Office of Court Administration to make the choice.

Home Office Reference Lab. v. Axelrod


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


116 A.D.2d 858; 498 N.Y.S.2d 181; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51675



January 16, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Commissioner of Health of the State of New York appealed from the order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which granted petitioner corporation's application to review a determination of the commissioner subjecting the corporation to the licensing and assessment provisions of N.Y. Pub. Health Law. The trial court held that the corporation was not subject to those provisions and ordered the refund of fees it paid.


OVERVIEW: The corporation performed laboratory tests on the blood and urine samples of applicants for life insurance policies. Pursuant to N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10, § 58-3.1, the commissioner assessed the corporation for laboratory and reference fees, the payment of which was a prerequisite for a permit. The corporation paid the assessment under protest and brought an action against the commissioner, contending that it was not a clinical laboratory within the meaning of N.Y. Pub. Health Law. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court noted that N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 570 declared that it sought to regulate the performance of clinical laboratories in the furnishing of information invaluable to the diagnosis and treatment of disease to the medical practitioner, and that N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 580(2) stated that the only activities regulated were those constituting patient services or services provided to health officers or their agents for sanitary purposes. The court concluded that none of the corporation's activities fell within those listed by the statute, and that it was entitled to a refund of the fees that it paid under protest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

659 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Greco Bros. Amusement Co. v. Chu


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


113 A.D.2d 622; 497 N.Y.S.2d 206; 1986 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 49759



January 2, 1986 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, without costs, determination confirmed, and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state tax commission and its officers, sought review of an order of the Supreme Court of Albany County (New York), which annulled a determination of the state tax commission sustaining a sales and use tax assessment imposed under N.Y. Tax Law arts. 28-29 against respondent taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The state tax commission contended the trial court erred in annulling the determination assessing sales and use taxes on the taxpayer for the full value of its replacement vending machines. The court agreed and reversed, holding that: (1) any ambiguity in a statutory exclusion from taxation must be construed against the government; (2) the transactions at issue were fully taxable under N.Y. Tax Law § 1110; (3) underscored words of the statute were clearly designed to exclude the value of trade-ins taken as partial compensation during a sale; (4) the taxpayer simply replaced its own used machines with new machines taken from its own inventory; (5) no transfer of title to the machines was made, nor was there an exchange of money or other consideration, or any type of payment from any person or entity to another; (6) as such, there were no transactions within the scope of the statutory exclusion; (7) it was the form of the transaction, not the substance, that controlled; and (8) there was nothing irrational about the tax commission's determination that effectively bound the taxpayer to the form of business chosen by it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that had annulled a determination of the state tax commission imposing a sales and use tax on the taxpayer, confirmed the determination, and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes

1. The State Tax Commission properly assessed against petitioner, a distributor of vending machines and amusement devices and the operator of a vending route consisting of the same types of machines at various locations, a compensating use tax based on the full value of the new machines petitioner took from its inventory and utilized as replacements on the vending route; petitioner was not entitled to deduct the value of used machines from the taxable price of the new machines as a "trade-in" value, since Tax Law § 1110 specifically excludes "any credit for tangible personal property accepted in part payment and intended for resale". Although petitioner could have conducted its business in another manner which would satisfy the statute [***2] and qualify the used machines for the exclusion, it did not do so, and it is the form of the transaction, not the substance, which controls; further, petitioner's equal protection claims are without merit.

Administrative Law -- Timeliness of Administrative Actions and Proceedings

2. In a proceeding to annul a determination of the State Tax Commission sustaining a sales and use tax assessment, the determination need not be nullified for failure to comply with the time requirements of 20 NYCRR 601.8 and Tax Law § 171; although Tax Law § 171 requires a determination within nine months after submission of briefs, it also provides that the remedy is to compel issuance of a determination through an application pursuant to CPLR article 78 for an order compelling issuance. Nor does failure to comply with the 90-day time limit in 20 NYCRR 601.8 require nullification.

 

660 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hodges


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


113 A.D.2d 514; 496 N.Y.S.2d 771; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 56606



December 30, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Queens County, rendered March 12, 1982, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for second degree robbery obtained by plaintiff state in the Supreme Court of New York, Queens County.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he was entitled to assert a claim of right defense under N.Y. Penal Law § 155.15 (1) to a robbery charge when he allegedly used force to recover money spent on contraband that he purchased. He asserted on appeal that he was denied due process of law and a fair trial when the trial court declined to charge the jury on the alleged claim of right defense. The court held that defendant was, by his own admission, involved in an illegal purchase of marijuana and has absolutely no legally cognizable right to recoup expenditures made in an illegal transaction, much less through the use of force. The court held that the claim of right defense was only available in a larceny prosecution, not a robbery prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the state and affirmed defendant's conviction for second degree robbery.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Robbery -- Claim of Right as Defense

A defendant who purchased contraband is not entitled to assert a claim of right defense ( Penal Law § 155.15 [1]) to a robbery charge when he allegedly used force to recover money spent in the purchase and, therefore, it was not error to decline to instruct the jury on a claim of right defense in the prosecution of defendant for robbery; by the specific terms of section 155.15 (1), the claim of right defense is only available in a larceny prosecution, not a robbery prosecution; moreover, since defendant was, by his own admission, involved in an illegal purchase of marihuana, he had absolutely no legally cognizable right to recoup expenditures made in such an illegal transaction, much less through the use of force.
