688 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Davis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


111 A.D.2d 945; 489 N.Y.S.2d 936; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 50223



June 24, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the County Court, Chemung County (New York), which convicted defendant of first degree attempted promoting prison contraband.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an inmate, was caught with a razor blade and lost "good time" that he had earned while incarcerated. Defendant was then criminally prosecuted for promoting prison contraband and pled guilty. Defendant was sentenced as a second felony offender. Defendant sought review and argued that the prosecution of his razor blade possession was a violation of his constitutional right against double jeopardy because he had already been punished with the loss of his good time, and that N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06, under which defendant was sentenced as a second felony offender, was a violation of defendant's state and federal constitutional right to due process. The court found that the loss of good time did not bar defendant's criminal prosecution for a crime based on the same act and that the second felony offender statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

689 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. New York State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


108 A.D.2d 488; 489 N.Y.S.2d 787; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 47912



June 6, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, without costs, and motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court of Albany County (New York), which granted a motion by respondent state tax commissioner to dismiss the petition for failure to exhaust administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that because the returns filed for the periods under review were essentially correct and sufficient, the state tax commissioner had no authority under N.Y. Tax Law § 1138(a)(1) to conduct administrative hearings to recover any tax due, but rather, had to request the Attorney-General to bring an action to enforce payment pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 1141(a). The taxpayer further argued that under N.Y. Tax Law § 1147(b), the state tax commissioner had no authority to assess any taxes due more than three years before the date of the notices of determination and demand for payment of the taxes due. The court reversed the decision of the lower court and denied the state tax commissioner's motion to dismiss. The court held that the notices of determination and demand for payment of taxes due were dated December 29, 1982, and, accordingly, in the absence of any hint of fraud, there could not be any assessment of taxes for periods ending three years prior to that date unless no return therefor was filed. The court held that N.Y. Tax Law § 1138 did not confer administrative jurisdiction on the state tax commissioner to recover unpaid taxes where correct returns were filed.


OUTCOME: The court denied the state tax commissioner's motion to dismiss the taxpayer's petition and reversed the lower court's judgment, on the law and without costs.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes -- Manner of Challenging Jurisdiction of State Tax Commission

1. A taxpayer may challenge the taxing authority's jurisdiction as unconstitutional or inapplicable in a manner other than that prescribed in the Tax Law; thus, a CPLR article 78 proceeding was properly commenced by petitioner to challenge respondent New York State Tax Commission's authority to hold a hearing pursuant to Tax Law § 1138 (a) (1) on the redetermination of deficiency of sales and use taxes and revision of the determination of sales and use taxes due.

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes -- Timeliness of Assessment of Additional Tax

2. Pursuant to Tax Law § 1147 (b), in the absence of fraud, no assessment of additional tax shall be made after the expiration of more than three years from the date of the filing [***2] of a return, provided that, where no return has been filed, the tax may be assessed at anytime; accordingly, where notices of determination and demand for payment of sales and use taxes due from petitioner for periods beginning with the period ending February 29, 1976, were dated December 29, 1982, and there was no hint of fraud, there cannot be any assessment for those periods ending prior to December 29, 1979, except for the period ending May 31, 1978, for which no return was filed.

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes -- Authority of State Tax Commission to Hold Assessment Hearing

3. Respondent New York State Tax Commission has authority under Tax Law § 1138 (a) (1) to hold hearings concerning the assessment of sales and use taxes due from petitioner for periods for which no tax returns were filed and for the period for which the return filed was incorrect or insufficient.

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes -- Jurisdiction of State Tax Commission to Recover Unpaid Taxes

4. Respondent New York State Tax Commission does not have authority under Tax Law § 1138 (a) (1) to hold hearings concerning the assessment of sales and use taxes due from petitioner for a period [***3] for which a correct and sufficient return was filed but no payment made; section 1138 does not confer jurisdiction on respondent to recover unpaid taxes where correct returns have been filed; moreover, such jurisdiction is not conferred by Tax Law § 171 (21), which requires respondent to provide a hearing as a matter of right to any taxpayer who requests a hearing, notwithstanding that petitioner sought a hearing pursuant to section 1138 (a) (1); the fact that petitioner reserved his rights by seeking administrative review should not prevent him from pursuing a CPLR article 78 proceeding to challenge respondent's jurisdiction. Accordingly, a motion by respondent to dismiss the petition challenging respondent's jurisdiction to conduct such hearing for failure to exhaust administrative remedies is denied.

Cibro Petroleum Products, Inc. v. Chu


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


111 A.D.2d 962; 490 N.Y.S.2d 59; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 50234



June 6, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Commissioner of the New York State Department of Taxation and Finance and President of the New York State Tax Commission, challenged an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York), which declared that the application of N.Y. Tax Law art. 13-A to respondent refinery's sale of military jet fuel to the federal government violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8(3).


OVERVIEW: Under N.Y. Tax Law § 301(a), a petroleum business was taxed the sum of 3 1/4 percent of its gross receipts from sales of petroleum where shipments were made to points within the state, for the privilege of doing business in state. The court maintained that before a state tax could be held to violate the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const., art I, § 8(3), on discrimination grounds, a plaintiff was required to show that it was discriminatory in favor of local business entities in purpose or effect. The court noted that the refinery did not cite any evidence that the purpose of § 301(a) was to discourage or otherwise penalize interstate petroleum suppliers. The court also noted that the legislative history and wording of the statute clearly dispelled such a purpose. The court found that the tax itself was fairly apportioned to intrastate activities, as its incidence was dependent upon delivery to the purchaser in state. Therefore, the court concluded the tax was constitutionally imposed, irrespective of whether the transportation of the fuel itself from its originating point to its ultimate destination entailed crossing state borders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the supreme court's order.

 

691 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


D'Angelo v. Cole


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


108 A.D.2d 541; 489 N.Y.S.2d 807; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 47917



June 4, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously reversed, on the law, with costs, counterclaim dismissed, and ordinance declared unconstitutional, in accordance with Per Curiam opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Livingston County (New York), which granted judgment in favor of respondents, the Village of Avon and the Village Board, and held that the Village's ordinance governing the maintenance of private roads was constitutional by implication.


OVERVIEW: The landowner initiated an action against the Village contending that the Village's ordinance governing the maintenance of private roads was unconstitutional. The trial court granted judgment in favor of the Village and held that such ordinance was constitutional by implication. The landowner sought review. The court held that an enactment which deprived a citizen of his right to use his property as he choose could not have been sustained under the police power if there was no reasonable relation between the end sought to be achieved by the regulation and the means used to achieve that end. The court found that an ordinance which purported to legislate for public safety must have tended in some appreciable way to that end. The court determined that there was not a substantial connection between the purpose of the ordinance and the end to be accomplished. The court determined that the ordinance was unconstitutional and reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment of the trial court, granted judgment in favor of the landowner, and held that the Village's ordinance governing the maintenance of private roads was unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Ordinance Establishing Maintenance Standards for Private Roads

An enactment which deprives a citizen of his right to use his property as he chooses cannot be sustained under the police power if there is no reasonable relationship between the end sought to be achieved by the regulation and the means used to achieve that end. Thus, a village ordinance which establishes standards for the maintenance of private roads is unconstitutional where at least two of the standards exceed what is necessary to achieve the stated purpose of the ordinance, i.e., to protect the public from unwarranted dangers and hazards in said roads; for the ordinance maintenance standards to be imposed on a private road owner against his will, it must appear that the standards are [***2] reasonably necessary to assure the public safety.

People v. Williams


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


111 A.D.2d 359; 489 N.Y.S.2d 331; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51458

Board of Educ. v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


111 A.D.2d 505; 488 N.Y.S.2d 887; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51573



May 9, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, board of education and taxpayers, sought review of a decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which granted a motion to dismiss plaintiffs' complaint brought by defendants, state and town. Plaintiffs had filed a declaratory judgment action to declare unconstitutional 1983 N.Y. Laws 1018, which changed how excess school taxes were to have been refunded.


OVERVIEW: 1983 N.Y. Laws 1018 changed how excess school taxes were to have been refunded. If a nuclear power plant in the county were to get its assessment reduced, the school district in which the plant was located would have been responsible for refunding the school taxes paid as a result of the initial over-assessment. Plaintiffs' declaratory judgment action sought to have 1983 N.Y. Laws 1018 declared unconstitutional. The complaint was dismissed on defendants' motion because they lacked standing, the complaint failed to state a cause of action, and the proceeding was premature. The court affirmed the dismissal, but for different reasons. The court found that the board of education lacked standing, but that while the taxpayers lacked standing under the state finance law, they had standing under the common law. However, the court held that the taxpayers' complaint did not present a justiciable controversy because the future event was beyond the control of the parties and might never have occurred. The court noted that dismissal of the complaint was not on the merits; consequently, the dismissal did not bar a subsequent action for the same relief if there ever was an actual controversy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of defendants' motion to dismiss the plaintiffs' complaint in its declaratory judgment action against defendants.

 

694 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Under 21 v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


108 A.D.2d 250; 488 N.Y.S.2d 669; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 48383; 37 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P35,378



May 7, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by Under 21, Catholic Home Bureau for Dependent Children v. New York, 65 N.Y.2d 344, 482 N.E.2d 1, 1985 N.Y. LEXIS 15387, 492 N.Y.S.2d 522 (1985)
Appeal dismissed by Agudath Israel of Am. v. New York, 65 N.Y.2d 924, 1985 N.Y. LEXIS 15223 (1985)
Appeal dismissed by Salvation Army v. Koch, 65 N.Y.2d 924, 1985 N.Y. LEXIS 15224 (1985)
Appeal dismissed by Under 21, Catholic Home Bur. for Dependent Children v. New York, 65 N.Y.2d 924, 1985 N.Y. LEXIS 15225 (1985)



DISPOSITION: Three orders and judgments (three papers), Supreme Court, New York County, one of which was entered on October 4, 1984, and the other two entered on October 5, 1984, modified, on the law, without costs and without disbursements, the motions for summary judgment denied, and upon search of the record ( CPLR 3212 [b]), summary judgment granted to defendants declaring that Mayoral Executive Order No. 50 and regulations promulgated thereunder are constitutional and valid, and otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the mayor, the city, and city officials, challenged decisions from the Supreme Court at Special Term, New York County (New York), which granted plaintiff non-profit organizations (organizations) summary judgment in their challenges to the validity of an executive order that prohibited those with city contracts from refusing to hire people on the basis of sexual orientation or affectional preference.


OVERVIEW: The mayor issued an executive order that prohibited those who secured contracts with the city from refusing to hire people simply on the basis of "sexual orientation or affectional preference" even if they were able perform the job in a satisfactory manner. The organizations challenged the validity of the executive order. The trial court granted summary judgment to the organizations because the mayor's action was ultra vires, unlawfully usurped the legislative power, and violated the New York State Constitution. The court reversed and upheld the validity of the executive order on the basis of due process and equal protection principals that barred arbitrary and invidious discrimination. The court held that the mayor did not exercise legislative authority. The court determined that the mayor validly exercised his charter powers under the federal and state constitutions because agencies, which stood in the shoes of the state, were not permitted to prohibit the employment of individuals on the basis of personal proclivities which had nothing to do with whether they were able to perform the job adequately. The mayor was obligated to enforce those rights under his oath of office.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the organizations, granted summary judgment to the mayor and city officials, and declared that the executive order and regulations promulgated there under were constitutional and valid.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Executive Power of Mayor -- Order Prohibiting Discrimination in Employment Based on Sexual Orientation

Executive Order No. 50 of the Mayor of the City of New York, which forbids those who secure contracts with New York City from [***2] refusing to hire people simply on the basis of sexual orientation or affectional preference even if they can perform the job in a satisfactory manner, and regulations promulgated thereunder, are constitutional and valid, and the Mayor did not encroach on the legislative prerogative in issuing the order. Under US Constitution 14th Amendment and NY Constitution, article I, § 11, the City of New York is prohibited from engaging in discrimination on the basis of sexual orientation or affectional preference; in promulgating Executive Order No. 50, the Mayor, as chief executive officer of the City of New York, had authority to assure that the city did not discriminate against any of its citizens; the Mayor was obligated to enforce the fundamental constitutional principles. Thus, the executive order represents a valid exercise of his charter powers in fulfillment of his responsibility to prevent invidious discrimination in employment by the city and those who contract to perform city services; the source of the Mayor's authority rests in constitutional due process and equal protection rather than an assertion of legislative authority.

 

695 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Pauk v. Board of Trustees


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


111 A.D.2d 17; 488 N.Y.S.2d 685; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51172



May 7, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, New York County, New York, entered judgment in favor of defendant university trustees that dismissed plaintiff professor's action that alleged violation of N.Y. Const. art. V, § 6 and N.Y. Educ. Law § 6212, and violation of the state constitution for keeping tenure votes secret. The trial court allowed the professor's breach of contract action. The trustees appealed.


OVERVIEW: A state college professor, who was denied tenure, claimed that the faculty made its adverse decision based on his union activities. The court found that the trial court correctly dismissed the cause of action based on a violation of N.Y. Const. art. V, § 6 and N.Y. Educ. Law § 6212 because the controversy was res judicata. The court held that the allegation that the faculty violated the state constitution by keeping tenure votes secret was properly dismissed under res judicata. The court held that the trial court's decision to allow the breach of contract action to go forward was erroneous. The court held that the transactional analysis approach to res judicata required the court to determine whether the breach of contract allegation arose from the same core facts. The court found the same facts controlled and that the contract claim had to be dismissed under res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that allowed the breach of contract action to go forward and affirmed the judgment that dismissed the other two causes of action.

 

696 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ramos


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


108 A.D.2d 209; 488 N.Y.S.2d 762; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 42956



May 6, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Motion, insofar as it is for reargument, denied.

Motion, insofar as it seeks leave to appeal from the order dated June 13, 1984, granted by Justice Titone, and order of the Supreme Court, Kings County, dated June 13, 1984 reversed, as a matter of discretion in the interest of justice, and matter remitted to the Supreme Court, Kings County, for further proceedings, in accordance with the opinion herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, acting pro se, moved for reargument of his appeal of a judgment of the Supreme Court in Kings County (New York) that was entered upon a verdict finding him guilty of manslaughter and assault and that had been affirmed by the appellate division. In the alternative, defendant moved for leave to appeal denial of his motion to the supreme court to vacate the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion for leave to appeal an order of the trial court was granted. The court held that the proper procedure for determining ineffective assistance of appellate counsel was through a motion to vacate the judgment pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.10. In reaching this conclusion, the court held that defendant was constitutionally entitled to effective assistance of counsel on any appeal that could be taken as of right. The court held that a broad reading of § 440.10(1)(h), which authorized the vacatur of a judgment obtained in violation of a right of the defendant under the constitution of the state or of the United States, encompassed ineffective assistance of appellate counsel claims concerning representation in intermediate appellate courts. According to the court, in determining whether appellate counsel was effective, the trial court passed not on the court's decision, but only on the conduct of the counsel who presented the appeal on a new record established in an evidentiary hearing, a record not before the reviewing court on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion for leave to appeal and reversed the judgment of conviction, holding that the proper procedure for determining ineffective assistance of counsel was through a motion to vacate the judgment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Right to Counsel -- Effective Representation -- Appellate Counsel -- Motion to Vacate Judgment

A claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel should be pursued in postjudgment proceedings [***2] commenced pursuant to CPL article 440; accordingly, where defendant, contending that he was denied effective assistance of appellate counsel, seeks reargument of an appeal from a judgment of conviction which was affirmed by the Appellate Division and, alternatively, leave to appeal from an order of Supreme Court which denied his application to vacate the judgment pursuant to CPL article 440, leave to appeal from said order is granted and the matter is reversed and remitted to Supreme Court for determination of the application on the merits, and the motion for reargument is denied. Although the alleged error could have been asserted at the time of the original appeal, CPL 440.10 (2) (c) is not a bar; it is not the alleged error alone, but an unjustified, unconstitutional failure of appellate counsel to raise the claim, that calls for relief; inasmuch as a judgment of conviction is reviewable as of right at the intermediate appellate court level, a broad reading of CPL 440.10 (1) (h) would encompass ineffective assistance of appellate counsel claims concerning representation in intermediate appellate courts. Moreover, a motion to vacate a judgment does not impose any additional burdens [***3] upon the trial courts and, in those instances in which it is necessary, the trial court is the best forum for an evidentiary hearing.

 

697 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


PEOPLE v. RAMOS


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 44101



May 6, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [*1] The motion insofar as it was for leave to appeal should be granted, the order dated June 13, 1984, reversed, and the case remitted to Criminal Term. The motion insorfar as it was for reargument should be denied

MOLLEN, P.J. and LAZER, J., concur


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought reargument of an appeal from a judgment of conviction for manslaughter in the first degree and assault in the first degree that was affirmed by the court. Defendant alternatively sought leave to appeal from an order of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York) that denied his application to vacate the judgment pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree and assault in the first degree in connection with a stabbing at a social club. Defendant asserted a justification defense. On appeal, counsel raised an argument that defendant's constitutional right to counsel was violated by alleged premature deliberations conducted by the jury during the course of trial. The appellate court found that defendant could raise no arguably meritorious challenge to the conduct of his trial. Defendant then made application to vacate the judgment, contending that he was denied effective assistance of appellate counsel. The trial court held that nisi prius was an improper forum for the review of the effectiveness of appellate counsel. Defendant sought reargument or leave to appeal. The court found that the trial court did not pass on the merits of the claim, and remitted the case to give the trial court the opportunity to do so. In the event that ineffective assistance of appellate counsel was found, the proper procedure was to vacate the judgment and resentence defendant to allow a new appeal to be taken. The motion for reargument was denied.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion for leave to appeal, reversed the order that denied defendant's application to vacate the judgment of conviction for manslaughter in the first degree and assault in the first degree, and remitted the case. The motion for reargument was denied.

 

698 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Terrell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


111 A.D.2d 1; 488 N.Y.S.2d 660; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51157



May 2, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court of New York, New York County, which convicted defendant of two counts of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first-degree and sentenced him to concurrent prison terms of three years to life. The state challenged the legality of the sentence.


OVERVIEW: After defendant refused a plea bargain and he was convicted, the state requested that the trial court impose a sentence within the range of 15 years to life as authorized by N.Y. Penal Law § 70.00(3)(a)(i). Defendant maintained that in view of his minor criminal record, the nature of the offense, and the great disparity between the plea offer and the mandatory sentence, the statutory sentence would be unconstitutional as applied to him. The trial court agreed. Upon review, the court found that the crimes at issue were committed prior to the effective date of the amendment, which increased the amount of drugs necessary for a class A-I felony of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first-degree. Defendant was subject to the old sentencing scheme. Instead, the trial court found that his was a rare case where the narcotics statute, while otherwise valid, would have been unconstitutional as applied to him. The court found that defendant was a principal actor in an ongoing cocaine business, and his was not the sort of peripheral association with narcotics activity that provided extremely compelling circumstances for not applying the sentencing guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for two counts of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first-degree. The court reversed the judgment by vacating defendant's sentence of concurrent prison terms of three years to life. The court remanded the matter for resentencing.

 

699 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ramos


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


111 A.D.2d 424; 488 N.Y.S.2d 489; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 51519



May 2, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the County Court of Chemung County (New York), which convicted defendant of attempted assault in the second degree, following his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted and charged with two counts of second degree assault. Defendant pleaded guilty to attempted assault in the second degree in full satisfaction of the indictment and was sentenced to an indeterminate term of imprisonment of 1 1/2 to 3 years, to run consecutive to the sentence he was then serving. Defendant claimed that the statute pursuant to which he was sentenced was unconstitutional. The court held that defendant was indicted pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law §120.05 (7) which, in effect, raised conduct which would constitute third degree assault to second degree assault where the actor committed the act while imprisoned pursuant to a criminal charge or judgment of conviction. The court noted that a conviction pursuant to this provision carries a sentence consecutive to the term defendant was serving unless the trial court provides otherwise in the interest of justice. The court affirmed because the court held that defendant waived this challenge because he did not raise this challenge before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of attempted assault in the second degree.

 

700 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rochester Gas & Electric Corp. v. Public Service Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


108 A.D.2d 35; 488 N.Y.S.2d 303; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 48377



April 25, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, and petition dismissed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner company brought a proceeding, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, to review so much of a determination of respondent Public Service Commission (Commission) as denied the company's requested increase in steam rates.


OVERVIEW: The company provided gas, electric, and steam services to various customers. Its steam sales had been steadily declining to the point that the Department of Public Service recommended that the company review the economic feasibility of its steam system. In conjunction with its filing for increased gas and electric rates, the company requested an increase in steam rates. It later submitted its report regarding the practicality of its steam department to the Commission and all of its steam customers. The Commission later established a temporary steam rate increase of nine percent. It also granted additional rate relief sufficient to avoid a negative return on the common stock investment. The Commission then made permanent the temporary, noncompensatory rate, and permitted a revenue increase sufficient only to enable the company to recover its out-of-pocket expenses. The court confirmed the determination, by holding that N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 85, suggested no absolute guarantee of steam rates that yielded a profit, and there was no error in the Commission's determination that the company's customers should not bear the burden of transforming its failing business into a success.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the determination, which denied the company's requested increase in steam rates. The court also dismissed the company's petition to review such determination.


HEADNOTES

Public Utilities -- Rate Making -- Steam Rates

A determination by respondent Public Service Commission which denied petitioner's requested increase in steam rates, being supported by substantial evidence, is confirmed. Respondent did not act unconstitutionally in fixing the steam rates for the years in issue at a level designed only to enable petitioner to recover its operating expenses; neither justice nor the Constitution obliges consumers to ensure a profitable return on an unprofitable enterprise such as petitioner's steam business; moreover, the language of Public Service Law § 85 does not suggest an absolute guarantee of steam rates yielding a profit, but rather reflects a constitutional principle which requires a balancing of the interests of the consumer against the interests of the regulated [***2] company's shareholders.

 

701 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Brooklyn Union Gas Co. v. Commissioner of Dep't of Finance


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


108 A.D.2d 74; 487 N.Y.S.2d 762; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 48362



April 16, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Determinations of the respondent Finance Department, dated March 15, 1984, annulled and vacated and the matter remanded to the Finance Commissioner of the City of New York for the purpose of determining whether all or any portion of the claimed refund is barred by reason of the failure of petitioner to make its claim for refund within the time limited by law, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner public utility sought review of final determinations of the Commissioner of the Department of Finance that denied its applications for refunds of the utility taxes paid to the City of New York pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law §§ 1201 and 1221(a)(3).


OVERVIEW: The public utility was subject to both state and New York City taxes pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 1201. For the period in question, it paid to the City of New York 2.35 percent on the gross income reported as taxable. The public utility sought a refund of taxes paid, arguing that it should only have paid 1.00 percent of its gross income. The referee concluded that the higher rate was proper. The court held that N.Y. Tax Law § 1221(a)(3) required that taxes upon utilities such as the public utility should be in accord with N.Y. Gen. City Law § 20-b, which limited the tax to 1.00 percent of gross income or gross operating income. The court held that the tax was not a nullity, and the public utility would only be entitled to recover the excess if paid in taxes over the appropriate amount. The court granted the public utility's petition for review.


OUTCOME: The court granted the public utility's petition to review the denial of its request for a refund of overpaid taxes.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- New York City Utility Tax -- Rate of Tax

1. A utility tax at the rate of 2.35% on gross income, fixed in Administrative Code of the City of New York § QQ46-2.0, imposed on petitioner, a public utility subject to both State and New York City taxes as provided in Tax Law § 186-a, for the period May 1980 through November 1982 is in excess of the rate limited by law. The [***2] City of New York may impose a tax on section 186-a utilities but, pursuant to Tax Law § 1221 (a) (3), the tax must be in accordance with the provisions of General City Law § 20-b which limits the tax to 1% of gross income or gross operating income; inasmuch as the city had the power to levy the tax, but erroneously imposed a rate in excess of that limited by law, petitioner may recover only the amount by which the tax, as levied, exceeded the amount authorized by Tax Law §§ 1201 and 1221 and General City Law § 20-b.

Taxation -- Refund of Tax Erroneously Collected -- One-Year Limitation Period

2. Where petitioner submitted applications to the New York City Department of Finance in January and June of 1983 seeking a refund for New York City utility taxes paid for the period May 1980 through November 1982, and said tax was determined to have been levied at a rate in excess of that limited by law, a portion of the refund claimed may be time barred; Administrative Code of the City of New York § QQ46-7.0 (a) provides that the Director of Finance shall refund or credit without interest any tax erroneously, illegally or unconstitutionally collected or paid, if application for [***3] such refund shall be made within one year from the payment thereof. Accordingly, the matter is remanded to determine whether all or any portion of the claimed refund is time barred.

 

702 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Joyce v. Ortiz


No. 22637


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 43686



April 12, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Order filed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner deputy fire chiefs sought review of the decision of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which dismissed their application filed against respondent government officials to declare the officials' actions regarding the filling of positions arbitrary and unlawful and request for a mandate for a test for chief of the department and an eligibles list based thereon and to enjoin appointments to that position except from such list.


OVERVIEW: According to the government officials, the personnel director of the department of personnel had adopted a resolution, which eliminated the position of chief of the department. The officials argued that the deputy chiefs' petition had been rendered moot by the resolution. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss the petition as moot. It further determined that the reclassification at issue did not offend the relevant portions of the New York State Constitution or the New York City Administrative Code. The court disagreed and held that even if the officers were genuinely re-evaluating the organizational structure within the fire department, they were still not authorized to suspend their compliance with the dictates of N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 65. The officials failed to comply with the procedural prescriptions outlined in § 65 and the New York City Charter. No notice, hearing, review, or approval by the state civil service commission either preceded or followed the promulgation of the resolution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the deputy chiefs' petition and granted the petition.

 

703 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Joyce v. Ortiz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


108 A.D.2d 158; 487 N.Y.S.2d 746; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 42954



April 11, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Judgment (denominated an order), Supreme Court, New York County, entered on March 16, 1984, unanimously reversed, on the law, and the petition granted, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner deputy fire chiefs (deputies) challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which dismissed the deputies' request for declaratory and injunctive relief which arose out of respondent personnel director's purported reclassification of the deputies.


OVERVIEW: Although the title of chief of the fire department belonged in the competitive civil service class, the position had for years been filled by extended provisional appointments. The deputies unsuccessfully requested that a competitive promotional examination be slated. When the deputies sought declaratory relief, the personnel director reclassified all deputy chiefs to a new civil service title without necessity of another examination and provided that the duties of the office of the chief would be exercised by a permanent incumbent in the competitive civil service with a new title. The trial court held that the actions constituted managerial discretion but the court reversed, because the personnel actions violated N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 65, which limited the duration of provisional appointments, and N.Y. Const. art. V, § 6, which required that appointments and promotions in civil service be made according to merit and fitness upon competitive examination. The personnel director's actions resulted in a reclassification of the title of chief of the department from the competitive to the noncompetitive class without compliance with N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 20.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the supreme court, which dismissed the deputies' request for declaratory and injunctive relief.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Appointment and Promotion -- Provisional Appointments

1. Provisional appointments allowed by Civil Service Law § 65 are subject to the mandatory requirements that an examination be ordered for any position held by provisional appointment for a period of one month and that the examination be held as soon as practicable in order to prevent the provisional appointment from continuing for a period in excess of nine months; an agency has no discretion to determine whether an examination will be ordered and conducted. Thus, respondents violated the provisions of section 65 when they filled the title of Chief of the Fire Department of the City of New York by successive provisional appointments, one for nearly three years and the next for about two and one-half years;  [***2] even if respondents were genuinely reevaluating the organizational structure within the Fire Department, and not simply endeavoring to evade the Civil Service Law, they were still not authorized to suspend compliance with the dictates of the statute.

Civil Service -- Appointment and Promotion -- Chief of Fire Department of City of New York

2. Resolutions promulgated by respondent Personnel Director of the City of New York which would eliminate the need for a competitive examination to effect the promotion of any person having the title of Deputy Chief (Fire) to the position of Chief of the Department contravenes NY Constitution, art V, § 6, which provides that appointments and promotions in the civil service be made according to merit and fitness based upon competitive examination, and Administrative Code of the City of New York § 487a-9.0, which requires that promotions within the Fire Department be the result of "seniority, meritorious service * * * and * * * competitive examination"; respondents may not circumvent the legal imperatives merely by endeavoring to abolish a title and designate an employee in a subordinate position to perform its former duties.

 [***3] Civil Service -- Appointment and Promotion -- Chief of Fire Department of City of New York

3. In enacting, respectively, New York City Charter § 494 and Administrative Code of the City of New York § 487a-20.0, the State Legislature and the New York City Council have explicitly limited the Fire Commissioner's discretion in the selection of the Chief of the Department; thus, to the extent that resolutions promulgated by respondent Personnel Director of the City of New York represent an encroachment upon legislative authority by eliminating the Chief of the Department as a separate and independent entity and investing the Fire Commissioner with the power to designate and remove the Chief of the Department at will, the law is clear that if an office is created by statute or ordinance, it can only be abolished by statute or ordinance and not by resolution.

Civil Service -- Classification -- Reclassification by Resolution

4. Resolutions purporting to reclassify civil service titles are invalid where they are not adopted in accordance with statutory requirements; thus, resolutions promulgated by respondent Personnel Director of the City of New York, which maintain the [***4] position of Deputy Chief (Fire) as a tenured, competitive civil service title but direct that appointment to the Chief of the Department detail will be made from among the Deputy Chief (Fire) incumbents solely by designation of the Fire Commissioner and will serve at his pleasure, are invalid. In effect, such actions have resulted in a reclassification of the title of Chief of the Department from the competitive to the noncompetitive, or exempt, class without compliance with the procedural prescriptions outlined in Civil Service Law § 20 and New York City Charter § 1105; no notice, no hearings, and no review or approval by the State Civil Service Commission either preceded or followed the promulgation of the resolutions. Moreover, City Charter § 1105 (g), in conjunction with Civil Service Law § 20 (1), do not exempt respondents from the procedural mandates contained in section 20.

 

704 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Herald Co. v. Roy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


107 A.D.2d 515; 487 N.Y.S.2d 435; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 48368



April 5, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Application unanimously denied and petition dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspaper filed a petition for a writ of prohibition to vacate and prohibit enforcement of respondent trial judge's order to prevent the disclosure by respondent, county commissioner of jurors (commissioner), of jurors' identities and addresses in a murder trial.


OVERVIEW: The newspaper claimed that the judge's order to prevent the commissioner's disclosure of the juror's identities and addresses in a murder trial was unconstitutional. The court dismissed the newspaper's petition for a writ of prohibition. The newspaper could have obtained the jurors' identities at the voir dire proceedings. Also, there was a dispute whether the judge issued any orders regarding the non-disclosure of the jurors' names and addresses or non-disclosure of the court minute books. Until the factual issue was determined, the petition was improper. Neither the commissioner nor the trial court clerks were obligated to orally provide the names and addresses of the jurors. Also, the newspaper was not entitled to the answers to the potential jurors' questionnaires because they had confidential information. To the extent that the newspaper sought access to public records and minute books, a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 7803(1), proceeding against the commissioner and trial court clerks in the supreme court, special term, in the nature of mandamus was the proper vehicle to obtain this relief.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the newspaper's petition against the trial judge and the commissioner to obtain the disclosure of the jurors' identities and addresses in a murder trial.


HEADNOTES

Newspapers -- Right of Access to Criminal Trials -- Closure of Trial Proceedings

1. In a CPLR article 78 proceeding wherein petitioner newspaper publisher seeks a judgment vacating and prohibiting enforcement of alleged oral orders of respondent Administrative Judge which prevent respondent County Commissioner of Jurors and others from disclosing to the public and media the identities of jurors selected to hear criminal charges in Onondaga County, petitioner's right to access to criminal trials has not been unconstitutionally restrained nor does the failure to provide the information it seeks constitute a form of closure of trial proceedings; even assuming the existence of the oral orders, there is no doubt that the entire criminal proceedings, including the voir dire, are open to the public; any newspaper reporter attending the voir dire proceeding could ascertain the identity of the jurors.

Proceeding against  [***2] Body or Officer -- Prohibition -- Order Preventing Disclosure of Identities of Jurors

2. The petition is dismissed in a CPLR article 78 proceeding wherein petitioner newspaper publisher seeks a judgment vacating and prohibiting enforcement of alleged oral orders of respondent Administrative Judge which prevent respondent County Commissioner of Jurors and others from disclosing to the public and media the identities of jurors selected to hear criminal charges in Onondaga County; inasmuch as petitioner ultimately seeks the identity of jurors sitting at criminal trials, relief by way of prohibition would not provide it with any remedy; moreover, there is no duty imposed on respondent Commissioner and court clerks to orally provide anyone with the names and addresses of the jurors and the court is not empowered to order these public officials to answer petitioner's question and divulge the information it seeks. Thus, to the extent that petitioner seeks access to public records and minute books, an article 78 proceeding in the nature of mandamus is the proper vehicle to endeavor to obtain such relief against respondent Commissioner and the court clerks ( CPLR 7803 [1]), and such proceeding [***3] must properly be brought in Supreme Court, Special Term ( CPLR 7804 [b]), not in the Appellate Division in the first instance.

Jury -- Disclosure of Juror Qualification Questionnaire -- Access to Criminal Part Minute Books

3. The protection offered by Judiciary Law § 509 (a), which provides that "[such] [juror qualification] questionnaires and records shall be considered confidential and shall not be disclosed except to the county jury board or as permitted by the appellate division" extends to the information contained in the juror qualification questionnaire and to records maintained by the Commissioner of Jurors to which such information may be transposed; moreover, access to the minute books maintained by the clerks of Criminal Parts may be obtained not by virtue of the provisions of Judiciary Law § 255-b but because the books must be kept pursuant to CPLR 9702 (5) and searched and certified by the court clerks pursuant to Judiciary Law § 255.

People v. Baynard

April 1, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgments by the Supreme Court, Queens County (New York), which convicted him of two counts of attempted robbery in the first degree upon his pleas of guilty and sentenced him as a second felony offender to two concurrent terms of four to eight years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was not advised that he had the right to cross-examine the State's witnesses prior to the taking if his pleas of guilty. Italiano v. Harrison


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


110 A.D.2d 684; 488 N.Y.S.2d 13; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 48578



April 1, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town challenged an order of the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York) that declared its resolution that prohibited parking and standing of vehicles on a certain designated roadway to be unconstitutional and denied its cross motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that appellee, a licensed peddler, was denied his property rights without due process of law by the town's adoption of a resolution that restricted all parking and standing along the thoroughfare where appellee operated a mobile frankfurter stand. Appellee asserted that the resolution was designed for purposes other than public health, safety, or welfare and that there was no record of any increased risks as a result of the presence of peddlers at the location to serve as a rational basis for its imposition. The trial court properly found that appellee's claim was a justiciable controversy. The town could only pass legislation, which prohibited peddling in certain streets if such action was reasonably calculated to achieve the valid public purposes of maintaining its busiest streets free from congestion and preserving them for the primary purpose of public travel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

708 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Dupont v. Joedon & Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


107 A.D.2d 369; 486 N.Y.S.2d 946; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 48244; 40 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 1022



March 26, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on May 24, 1983, unanimously modified, on the law, to the extent only of denying summary judgment as to late charges and moving expenses subsequent to January 15, 1979, and the action is remanded for an assessment as to the above charges, and striking Caffrey as a party to the motion, and otherwise affirmed, without costs and without disbursements. It is further ordered that the judgment of said court entered on June 14, 1983, is reversed, on the law and the facts, and the judgment vacated with leave to settle and enter an interlocutory judgment reflecting the liability of Joedon and Zucker for all other charges,  [***2] and the order entered on September 26, 1984, is modified, as aforesaid, and otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant filed an action for damages against defendant storage company for wrongful eviction and related causes of action. The storage company asserted a cross claim against defendant landlords for moving and storage charges. The Supreme Court, New York County (New York) dismissed the tenant's complaint and granted the storage company summary judgment on its crossclaim against the landlords. The landlords appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the tenant was evicted from the premises owned by the landlords, its equipment was placed in the premises of the storage company. The equipment was ultimately sold at public auction. The landlords argued that the moving and storage charges were due to the storage company's conduct in canceling a scheduled public auction. The storage company asserted that the sale was canceled due to the tenant's claim of ownership of the goods and questions as to the constitutionality of the statute permitting an ex parte sale of bailed goods. The landlords were notified of the cancellation of the warehousemen's lien sale and advised that such cancellation had no effect on their right to conduct a sale as judgment creditor. The court agreed with the storage company and held that the parties' writings contradicted any contention that the landlords were liable only for the original three-month storage fee. The storage company had no obligation to sell the goods at any specific time to satisfy the warehouseman's lien or to mitigate damages. The bailment contract, which was terminable at will, was a continuing contract until it was terminated and was not a contract only for a reasonable time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as modified the grant of summary judgment for the storage company. The court remanded for an assessment as to the late charges and moving charges. The court ordered the lower court to strike the principal shareholder of the storage company as a party to the motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Warehousemen -- Warehouseman's Lien -- Remedy Not Exclusive

The warehouseman's lien remedy under UCC 7-209 and 7-210 is not exclusive, nor does it have the effect of relinquishing the warehouseman's right of action against the person liable for storage charges. Accordingly, where plaintiff commercial tenant was evicted from defendant landlords' premises and plaintiff's equipment was removed by defendant moving company and placed in the warehouse of defendant storage company, remaining there until nearly four years later when it was sold at public auction and purchased by defendant moving and storage companies, Special Term properly granted defendant moving and storage companies summary judgment on their cross claim against defendant landlords for storage charges at the monthly rate agreed to in the storage contract for a period of 47 months; however, since there was no agreement as to late charges, an assessment is required as to those charges and also as to six moving charges which are unexplained.

 

709 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Perrotta v. New York


No. 22396


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


107 A.D.2d 320; 486 N.Y.S.2d 941; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 42510



March 21, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on March 18, 1984, unanimously reversed, on the law, the judgment vacated, the petition pursuant to CPLR article 78 denied and respondents' determination reinstated, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner building permit applicant filed a proceeding, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78(1), to direct respondent New York City Department of Buildings to rescind its revocation of applicant's building plans. The Supreme Court at Special Term (New York) annulled Department's revocation of the permits and directed Department to reinstate the permit. Department sought review.


OVERVIEW: Department approved applicant's request for a permit to build a single-family, two-story house. Neighbors discovered that toilets and bathtubs were being placed on all floors, that the building was three stories, and that partitions for separate entrances were being built. Department revoked applicant's permit. Applicant filed two sets of amended plants, which were both rejected. Finally, applicant submitted an amended plant that removed several bathtubs and toilets. Department advised applicant that the amended plans were acceptable, but applicant did not apply for a new permit. In annulling the revocation of the permit and the approval of the amended plan, the trial court held that applicant had a vested right to complete the building, as he had performed substantial work in good-faith reliance upon the legally issued permit. The court held that the trial court erred in annulling the revocation, as even though the building was substantially constructed at the time the permit was revoked, it was not the same building as that which had appeared in the permit application. Applicant did not acquire vested rights because he relied on an invalid permit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and reinstated Department's determination.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning -- Revocation of Building Permit

Petitioner is precluded from bringing a CPLR article 78 proceeding to annul a determination of the New York City Buildings Department revoking his permit to build a two-story, single-family house in a neighborhood zoned for single-family residences, since he failed to appeal the revocation to the Board of Standards and Appeals (NY City Charter § 666 [7] [a]), where petitioner alleges that respondents' interference [***2] with his "vested right" to complete a nonconforming building after substantial work was performed and obligations were assumed in good-faith reliance upon a legally issued permit was an unconstitutional taking. Further, the permit was not valid in the first instance, since the Buildings Department approved petitioner's proposals based upon its initial failure to perceive that the design submitted by him represented plans for a two-family residence; vested rights are not acquired where there is reliance upon an invalid permit. In any event, by erecting an aboveground basement, making the building a three-story structure, petitioner was not in compliance with the design which had been accepted or with the relevant zoning ordinances (Administrative Code of City of New York § C26-20.0).

 

710 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dupont


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


107 A.D.2d 247; 486 N.Y.S.2d 169; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 48427



March 7, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, New York County, rendered on June 16, 1982, unanimously modified, by reversing the conviction only to the extent of dismissing count 10 of the indictment and vacating the sentence imposed thereon, and otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with aggravated harassment, attempted grand larceny in the third degree, tampering with a witness, falsely reporting an incident, and harassment. The Supreme Court of New York County (New York) convicted defendant and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant distributed a magazine, which contained cartoons that depicted his previous attorney in an uncomplimentary light, portrayed him as a homosexual, and referenced previous real estate dealings. The defendant was convicted for aggravated harassment under N.Y. Penal Law § 240.30, and he appealed. The court stated that as offensive as the defendant's activities may have been they did not violate § 240.30. The court stated that § 240.30, was not designed to prevent dissemination or publication of vexatious material about an individual and that it was not meant as a substitute for defamation laws. The court stated that the statute on its face was vague and overbroad and that it was unconstitutional as it applied to the defendant. The court stated this was an overly broad effort to apply § 240.30, to a constitutionally protected activity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and dismissed the defendant's conviction for aggravated harassment and vacated his sentence for that conviction. The court affirmed the rest of the defendant's convictions.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Harassment -- Distribution of Offensive and Vexatious Material

1. Defendant's conviction for aggravated harassment (Penal Law § 240.30), arising out of his distribution of offensive and vexatious printed material with intent to harass and annoy the complainant, is reversed; the harassment statute does not appear to have been relied upon as the basis for punishing any but annoying and harassing communications transmitted directly to the complainant and was not designed to prevent dissemination of such material. Moreover, the statute is vague, at least as [***2] applied to defendant, since it is not clear what is meant by communication "in a manner likely to cause annoyance or alarm" to another; on the face of the statute it would be difficult for one to know that criminal sanctions were applicable to the distribution of the instant material, which accused the complainant of homosexuality and of sharp or dishonest dealing.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Standing

2. A defendant, who was convicted of aggravated harassment based on his distributing of offensive and vexatious printed material accusing complainant of homosexuality and sharp or dishonest dealing, has standing to challenge the harassment statute (Penal Law § 240.30) for overbreadth since the distinct possibility exists that the statute might again be similarly applied in the future, thereby forcing others to refrain from engaging in constitutionally protected speech or expression; defendant's conviction violated his 1st Amendment rights in that he was punished for exercising his right to free speech. It cannot be said that such State interest as there may be in protecting individuals against criticism of their sexual habits or financial dealings can justify [***3] prosecuting defendant.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Vexatious and Offensive Material

3. A statute drawn in so narrow a form as to criminally punish one who describes another as a homosexual or as one who engages in sharp or dishonest dealing (see, Penal Law § 240.30), is unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, at least as applied to defendant who was charged with distributing vexatious and offensive material which was neither obscene nor otherwise unprotected by the 1st Amendment (the "fighting words" exception, Chaplinsky v New Hampshire, 315 U.S. 586, being inapplicable since the distribution was neither a violent nor a potentially violent act); the statute was so vague and indefinite, in form and as interpreted, as to permit within the scope of its language the punishment of incidents fairly within the protection of the guarantee of free speech, and, consequently, is void on its face, as contrary to the 14th Amendment. The fact that certain modes of expression may be "annoying" to others does not require an individual to forfeit his 1st Amendment rights to make those expressions.

 

711 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Amerada Hess Corp. v. Acampora


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


109 A.D.2d 719; 486 N.Y.S.2d 38; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 47198



March 4, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed an action for a judgment declaring defendant board members' denial of the corporation's application to change the zoning classification of certain parcels of real property was confiscatory and unconstitutional. The board members filed a motion to dismiss the complaint as time barred. The Supreme Court, Suffolk County (New York) denied the motion to dismiss, and the board members appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the declaratory judgment action, the corporation sought to have the board members' denial of its application for a change of zone declared unconstitutional and void, and a judgment directing the board members to grant a change of zone for two parcels. In their motion to dismiss, the board members asserted the corporation's cause of action accrued approximately nine years prior to the commencement of the action, when the town board originally denied the application for a change of zone and the action was time barred by the six-year statute of limitations contained in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 213(1). In denying the motion to dismiss, the trial court held the corporation's declaratory judgment action was commenced some four years after it had accrued. On appeal, the court affirmed, even though it rejected the trial court's reasoning, because the statute of limitations did not bar the constitutional attack raised in the corporation's declaratory judgment action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied the board members' motion to dismiss the corporation's declaratory judgment action as time barred.

People v. Towns


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


109 A.D.2d 764; 486 N.Y.S.2d 81; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 47250



March 4, 1985 

 

713 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Savings Bank of Utica v. New York State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


107 A.D.2d 205; 485 N.Y.S.2d 903; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 48420



March 1, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment unanimously affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank appealed the summary judgment of the Supreme Court, Oneida County (New York), which was entered in favor of defendant New York State Tax Commission (commission), in the bank's action that challenged the constitutionality of New York's franchise tax scheme with respect to savings and commercial banks.


OVERVIEW: Under the New York franchise tax scheme, the formula for computing the alternative minimum tax was not the same for savings banks as for commercial banks. The bank, which was a savings bank, brought an action against the commission to challenge the way in which it was taxed. The trial court granted a summary judgment for the commission, which the court affirmed. The court held that, because of the differences between the types of banks, one tax formula was unable to produce an equitable tax for both. The attributes justifying different tax treatment were that commercial banks continued to show a net profit and thus paid the basic tax, while savings banks had actually shown a net loss. Savings banks remained mutual institutions that handled savings accounts and provided money for long-term residential real estate mortgages. Commercial banks, conversely, derived a much lower proportionate share of their revenue from such sources and paid out a much smaller proportion of interest. The franchise tax scheme did not violate N.Y. Const. art. XVI, § 4 because the two types of banks did not exercise substantially similar functions or engage in substantially similar business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment in favor of the commission.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Franchise Tax on Banking Corporations -- Equal Protection -- Different Alternative Minimum Tax for Savings and Commercial Banks

1. The different alternative minimum franchise tax treatment accorded savings banks and commercial banks pursuant to the classification set forth in Tax Law § 1455 (b), wherein the alternative minimum for savings banks is based on a percentage of interest or dividends credited to depositors or shareholders, while the minimum for commercial banks is based on an assessment of an institution's par value of stock, does not violate the State Constitution since the different treatment has a rational basis [***2] and achieves the legislative goal of imposing a tax for the privilege of doing business in the State as a corporate entity. The statutory scheme recognizes the inherent differences in the two types of institutions and results in the collection of franchise taxes from each type of bank in proportion to its share of assets.

Taxation -- Franchise Tax on Banking Corporations -- Different Treatment for Savings and Commercial Banks

2. The State's method of imposing different alternative minimum franchise taxes on savings banks and commercial banks does not violate NY Constitution, article XVI, § 4, which provides that there shall be no discrimination in the rates and method of taxation between corporations incorporated under the laws of the United States and other corporations exercising substantially similar functions, since commercial banks and savings banks do not in fact perform substantially similar functions or engage in substantially similar business; moreover, inasmuch as Federally chartered and State-chartered commercial banks are treated identically, and Federally chartered and State-chartered savings banks are treated identically, the franchise tax scheme does not [***3] violate the aforementioned constitutional provision.

 

714 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. New York State Teachers' Retirement System


No. 48843


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


107 A.D.2d 103; 485 N.Y.S.2d 871; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 42507



February 28, 1985 



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified, on the law, without costs, by deleting the second, third, fourth and fifth decretal paragraphs and substituting therefor a paragraph providing that Retirement and Social Security Law §§ 211 and 213 are not applicable to plaintiff, and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory action to determine entitlement to pension benefits, plaintiff retiree appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which (1) granted motions by defendants, teachers' retirement system and others (retirement funds), for summary judgment, and (2) declared that the actions taken by the retirement funds regarding the retiree's retirement benefits did not violate any of his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: After retiring from his job with the New York City Police Department the retiree worked as a faculty member of the State University of New York (SUNY). During that time he was drawing a pension form the police department. As a result of the retiree's inquiry concerning his rights upon retirement from his position with SUNY, the police pension fund advised him that he had not been entitled to receive benefits from the fund during the period that he was employed by SUNY. He was notified that his police pension benefits would be suspended and the pension benefits received would have to be repaid. He brought the instant declaratory action to determine his entitlement to the pension benefits paid to him by the police pension fund. The court affirmed the finding that the retiree's employment by SUNY was subject to the conditions and limitations in the former statute N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law §§ 150, 151, and that pursuant to N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 214, he was not entitled to the benefits received from the police pension fund during his employment with SUNY.


OUTCOME: In a declaratory action to determine entitlement to pension benefits, the judgment providing that sections of the retirement and social security law were not applicable to the retiree was modified, and, as so modified, was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Retirement and Pension Benefits -- Suspension of Benefits during Public Reemployment

1. Plaintiff, who retired from the New York City Police Department in July 1962, was not entitled to pension benefits he received from the New York City Police Pension Fund during the period that he was employed as a faculty member of the State University of New York (SUNY). Plaintiff's membership in the Teachers' Retirement System, which predated the enactment of Retirement and Social Security Law article 7 in 1964, is protected by the NY Constitution,  [***2] article V, § 7 and cannot be impaired by Retirement and Social Security Law § 213, which prohibits a public retiree who is reemployed pursuant to article 7 from becoming a member of a public retirement system; however, since Retirement and Social Security Law § 211, which extends to public pensioners the privilege to undertake limited public employment without affecting their retirement allowances, and section 213 cannot be considered separate and apart from one another and since section 213 cannot be applied to plaintiff, plaintiff may not take advantage of the privilege established by section 211. Accordingly, pursuant to Retirement and Social Security Law § 214, plaintiff was not entitled to the benefits received from the Police Pension Fund since 1962; section 214 provides that a retired person may be similarly employed during the effective period of article 7 subject to the same conditions and limitations as were applicable to his employment pursuant to the statutes under which he was originally employed; plaintiff's employment by SUNY in 1962 was subject to Civil Service Law (former) §§ 150, 151, under which plaintiff was not entitled to receive such benefits during his [***3] employment with SUNY.

Civil Service -- Retirement and Pension Benefits -- Suspension of Benefits during Public Reemployment -- Due Process -- Equal Protection

2. The due process rights of plaintiff, who retired from the New York City Police Department in 1962 and was not entitled to pension benefits he received from the New York City Police Pension Fund during the period that he was employed as a faculty member of the State University of New York (SUNY), were not violated by the actions of the Police Pension Fund in notifying plaintiff by letter that his pension benefits would be suspended, that benefits received since 1962 would have to be repaid, and that he had 10 days to challenge the repayment calculation. Plaintiff's entitlement to continued receipt of pension benefits from the pension fund is something less than an unrestricted property right subject to the full panoply of due process protections; the pension fund's letter met the minimum requirements of notice and an opportunity to be heard; inasmuch as no factual dispute existed, plaintiff was not entitled to a full hearing. Moreover, plaintiff's assertions that he was denied equal protection since public pensioners [***4] who undertake private employment are not subject to the same statutory conditions and limitations as those who return to public employment are inadequate to overcome the dual presumption of constitutionality and that the Legislature investigated and found such facts as were necessary to support the legislation.

Civil Service -- Retirement and Pension Benefits -- Suspension of Benefits during Public Reemployment -- Estoppel

3. Generally, the doctrine of estoppel is not applicable to agencies of the State acting in a governmental capacity; accordingly, where plaintiff, who retired from the New York City Police Department in 1962, was not entitled to pension benefits he received from the New York City Police Pension Fund during the period that he was employed as a faculty member of the State University of New York (SUNY), the Police Pension Fund should not be estopped from terminating plaintiff's benefits and seeking to recover benefits paid since 1962 because it knew or should have known of plaintiff's reemployment with SUNY.

 

715 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Lakeview Apartments of Hunns Lake, Inc. v. Stanford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


108 A.D.2d 914; 485 N.Y.S.2d 801; 1985 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 43246



February 25, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, apartment company and others (apartment company), appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Dutchess County (New York), which favored defendants, the town and others (town), and dismissed the proceeding challenging Town of Stanford, N.Y., Local Law No. 2 (1982).


OVERVIEW: In 1977, the town, which had no zoning ordinance, enacted a moratorium law which prohibited multifamily dwellings and industrial and commercial establishments, except upon a variance issued by the town board on recommendation by the planning board. Each succeeding year, the moratorium law was reenacted. It remained in effect in 1982 when the apartment company made their application for a variance. The town argued that progress had been in the adoption of a comprehensive zoning plan, including the adoption of a master plan in 1980, and the completion of a preliminary draft of a zoning ordinance in December 1983 (one month after the apartment company's application for a variance was denied). However, the court found the justifications asserted for the delay were without merit. It held that the stop-gap legislation had been in effect for an excessive amount of time without the enactment of a comprehensive zoning ordinance, and that the limitation upon the use of property was unconstitutional and void. Thus, it reversed the judgment, and found the local law ultra vires and void.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the town was reversed, judgment was granted in favor of the apartment company declaring the temporary local zoning law ultra vires and void, and the town was directed to issue the permit applied for by the apartment company.
