770 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lord


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


103 A.D.2d 1032; 478 N.Y.S.2d 425; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19733



July 13, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Monroe County Court (New York), which convicted defendant of attempted murder in the second degree and sentenced him as a persistent felony offender to an indeterminate term of imprisonment of 20 years to life.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed the victim more than 40 times with an ice pick. The victim testified that an associate with whom defendant had committed a bank robbery had told the victim to leave town, so as to avoid the victim's being questioned by police about the robbery. Such testimony supported the prosecution's theory that defendant attempted to kill the victim in order to prevent him from revealing defendant's participation in the robbery. Defendant was convicted of attempted murder in the second degree and sentenced as a persistent felony offender. Defendant appealed, contending that the trial court erred in allowing the victim to testify as to what defendant's associate said to the victim. The court disagreed and held that the testimony was properly received under the rule of admission by silence as probative of defendant's state of mind and motive. Defendant, who was present when his associate spoke to the victim about the potential for the police questioning about the robbery, could have denied the statements if he considered them untrue. Because defendant made no such denial, the inference was justifiable that defendant acquiesced in his associate's statements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of attempted murder in the second degree and sentenced him as a persistent felony offender to an indeterminate term of imprisonment of 20 years to life.

 

771 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Meegan "S" v. Donald "T"


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


103 A.D.2d 913; 478 N.Y.S.2d 150; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19580



July 12, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent putative father appealed from an order of the Family Court of Essex County (New York), which denied the putative father's motion to dismiss a second paternity petition. The father argued that the second petition should have been dismissed on the ground that the amendment extending the statute of limitations was not intended to have retroactive consequences and that res judicata barred the proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner mother filed in a paternity proceeding on behalf of her child, born in 1980. In 1983, that petition was dismissed as untimely because the proceeding had not been commenced within two years of the child's birth as required by § 517 of the Family Court Act. No appeal was taken. Later that year, § 517 was amended to extend the limitations period to five years from the child's birth. In light of the amendment, the mother filed a new paternity petition. The putative father's motion to dismiss the second petition was denied. The court reversed the judgment and held, first, that the amendment was to have been retroactively applied. The extension of the limitations period to five years was calculated to cure the statute of its perceived constitutional infirmity. Remedial legislation was generally afforded retrospective treatment. However, res judicata prohibited consideration of the second petition. The precise issue decided in the first proceeding was that the mother was precluded by the statute of limitations. As she did not appeal that ruling, that determination was conclusive on the parties notwithstanding the subsequent change in the law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying dismissal of the mother's paternity petition, and it dismissed the petition.

 

772 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Dougal v. County of Suffolk


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


102 A.D.2d 531; 477 N.Y.S.2d 381; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18816



July 9, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, dated January 11, 1983, affirmed, with one bill of costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff merchants challenged the judgment from the Supreme Court at Special Term, Suffolk County (New York), which declared County of Suffolk, N.Y., Local Law No. 42-1981 and Town of Islip, N.Y., Local Law No. 4 (1981), preempted by state legislation. They filed an action against defendant county to declare both laws, which forbade the sale of merchandise characterized as drug paraphernalia, unconstitutional and unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: The merchants owned and operated retail establishments. They claimed that state legislation was preemptive and that the local ordinances were void for vagueness and violated their rights of free speech, due process, and equal protection. The court initially directed the issuance of a preliminary injunction and a trial of the factual issues raised in the complaint against the county. However, a later judgment declared the local ordinances to be preempted by state legislation. The court held that: (1) although the county and the town had broad powers to enact local legislation concerning the health, safety, welfare, and morals of their residents, pursuant to N.Y. Const. art IX, § 2, and N.Y. Mun. Home Rule Law § 10(1), they were precluded from adopting local laws that were preempted by state legislation; (2) the legislature evinced an intention to occupy the entire field of "drug-related paraphernalia," marked by a pervasive scheme of state legislation; and (3) the local enactments expressly conflicted with the state legislation and their different standards, definitions, and penalties would lead to confused and inconsistent enforcement. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, with one bill of costs, the judgment rendered by the trial court, which declared the county and town local laws preempted by state legislation in the merchants' action against the county to declare the laws forbidding the sale of drug paraphernalia unconstitutional and unenforceable.


HEADNOTES

Local Laws -- Preemption by State -- Sale of Drug Paraphernalia

Local laws which forbid the sale of certain merchandise characterized as drug paraphernalia are preempted by State legislation, since the State Legislature has enacted a comprehensive and detailed regulatory scheme in the field of drug-related paraphernalia.

 

773 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Zoepy Marie, Inc. v. Greenburgh


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


103 A.D.2d 776; 477 N.Y.S.2d 411; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19392



July 9, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), which denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment and granted defendant town's cross motion for summary judgment dismissing the action as premature upon the ground that plaintiffs failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. Plaintiffs had filed an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 to declare certain sections of the town's law unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a cause of action against the town to have its Sign and Illumination Law and Gasoline Service Station Law unconstitutional. The trial court granted the town's cross-motion for summary judgment holding that plaintiffs failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. Reversing the trial court's judgment, the court noted that plaintiffs were not required to exhaust their administrative remedies by seeking variances before commencing the instant action. They were not claiming that the statutes in issue were creating a unique hardship for them. Rather than asking for the relaxation of an assumedly valid regulation, plaintiffs were asserting that they were entitled to a declaration of the unconstitutionality of the statutes because as applied to them the statutes improperly restricted their freedom of speech. Under these circumstances, the court held that they were entitled to make a direct attack upon these statutes. The court concluded that the restrictions on the dissemination of truthful commercial speech were violative of plaintiffs' rights under the U.S. Const. amend. I because they restricted speech solely on the basis of content.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment denying plaintiffs' motion for summery judgment and granting the towns cross-motion for summary judgment.

 

774 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Schultz Mgmt. v. Bd. of Stds. & Appeals


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


103 A.D.2d 687; 477 N.Y.S.2d 351; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19302



July 5, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, New York County (New York) ordered a new hearing for petitioner mortgagees in their N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding which sought, citing N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 301(5), annulment of the order of respondent Board of Standards and Appeals of the City of New York (board), revoking the certificate of occupancy of the mortgaged building because of misrepresentations in an alteration permit application.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing on the application of the Buildings Commissioner, the board revoked the building's certificate of occupancy because it was issued on misrepresentations made in an application for an alteration permit. The application represented that the premises consisted of two buildings, each with a lot coverage of less than 5,000 square feet and therefore convertible, as of right, into loft dwellings under the zoning regulations. But the property was one building with a lot coverage of 12,472 and therefore not eligible for conversion. Reversing the decision, the court explained that the mortgagees were not entitled under N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 301(5) to notice of the hearing concerning continuation of the certificate of occupancy where the dwelling did not conform to all other applicable law. The court added that not only did the mortgagees have actual notice of the revocation proceeding, they participated in the hearings by submitting affidavits opposing the revocation. The court rejected the mortgagees' claims that they were denied their constitutionally protected due process right to notice and an opportunity to have been heard as without merit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order giving the mortgagees a new hearing on the board's revocation of the certificate of occupancy for the mortgaged building and dismissed the petition.

 

775 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Commissioner of Labor v. Hinman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


103 A.D.2d 886; 478 N.Y.S.2d 116; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19553



July 5, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff labor commissioner challenged the order from the Supreme Court at Special Term, Madison County (New York), which denied his motion to hold defendant employer in contempt of court for failing to comply with a subpoena, and granted the employer's cross motion to vacate a judgment entered against her.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner claimed that the relief sought in the employer's cross motion was precluded by her failure to exhaust her administrative remedies. The court held that: (1) the exhaustion rule was not inflexible; rather, it was subject to important qualifications; (2) notwithstanding the rule against collateral attack, the commissioner's administrative determination was subject to such attack if it was absolutely void as for want of jurisdiction; (3) because the judgment was not obtained in the traditional method of a lawsuit or under conditions, N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5015 was intended to preclude relief from the trial court; (4) the commissioner had achieved an acceptable balance between the purposes of his enabling legislation and the protection of individual due process through his procedure that provided an opportunity for both a meaningful hearing and judicial review; and (5) the employer's failure to comply with a duly issued subpoena constituted contempt of court, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5251.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, granted the commissioner's motion for contempt, denied the employer's cross motion, and remitted the matter to the trial court.

 

776 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Haverstraw


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


102 A.D.2d 451; 479 N.Y.S.2d 42; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18806



July 2, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Cross appeal dismissed (see Parochial Bus Systems v Board of Educ., 60 NY2d 539).

Judgments dated June 26, 1980 and July 6, 1981 reversed, on the law and the facts, and proceedings remitted to Special Term for a new determination on the evidence heretofore presented, in accordance with the opinion herewith.

Petitioners are awarded one bill of costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court at Special Term, Rockland County (New York) dismissed plaintiff taxpayers' petitions pursuant to N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 7 to review assessments for the years 1974 through 1978. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers alleged over valuation, illegality, and inequality in the tax assessments on their real property and attempted to prove the inequality of the assessments with the "justification" requirement of a prior decision. They served notice on defendant town to admit ratio pursuant to N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 716. The town's response was that it denied to admit the ratio on the grounds that the town did not understand the taxpayers' demand to admit. The trial court held that the taxpayers failed to prove ratio and inequality. The court reversed and held that the evidence established the taxpayers' prima facie case that the use of the state rates was justified and that the taxpayers proved ratio and inequality. The town failed to meet its burden of proving that the state rates were inappropriate. The town's response to the taxpayers' demand for admissions did not comply with the provisions of N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 716. The town's failure to properly deny the ratio was equivalent to a stipulation of the previous judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the taxpayers' petitions to review real estate tax assessments for the years 1974 through 1978. The court remitted to the trial court for a new determination on the evidence.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Assessment -- Evidence of Inequality -- State Equalization Rate

In proceedings pursuant to article 7 of the Real Property Tax Law to review assessments for the years 1974 through 1978 on certain real property located in the Town of Haverstraw, which property is improved with buildings containing 390 [***2] single-family condominium dwelling units, petitioners have established ratio in their effort to prove inequality of their assessments, where they presented State Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA) certificates of State equalization rates for the years in question and SBEA backup materials for those years and this documentary evidence was supported by the testimony of the town's appraiser, the Town Attorney and the SBEA director of research and statistics. In any event, the town's failure to "specifically" deny the ratios set forth in notices to admit ratio served by petitioners for the years 1974 through 1977 must be deemed an admission of the ratios set forth therein for those years (Real Property Tax Law, § 716). Accordingly, inasmuch as the town is not a special assessing unit with a population of one million or more and State equalization rates may therefore be used to prove inequality (Real Property Tax Law, § 720, subd 3, as amd by L 1981, ch 1057, § 7), petitioners must be deemed to have established ratio for the years 1974 through 1978 and are entitled to a determination by the trial court on the issue of the fair market value of the subject property.

 

777 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Franza v. Carey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


102 A.D.2d 780; 478 N.Y.S.2d 873; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18951



June 28, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State Attorney General and plaintiff shop owners challenged the decision of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which held that N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law art. 39 was not impermissibly vague on its face, but, with respect to the sale and display of multiuse items, granted the shop owners' application for a preliminary injunction and directed a hearing to determine as to such items the constitutionality of article 39.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed with the trial court that article 39 was not impermissibly vague and that a violation of article 39 occurred only if the violator was shown to have a culpable intent. As applied to retailers, possession of drug paraphernalia did not give rise to a violation unless the retailer intended to sell the drug paraphernalia to those who would use it in a prohibited manner. The court found no basis for the trial court's conclusion that a hearing was required prior to enforcement of the statute to determine the constitutionality of its application to one or another of the so-called multiple-use items that the shop owners possessed. The court held that the trial court correctly concluded that the omission of a specific requirement of probable cause in N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 852(2) was not reasonably interpreted as diluting the requirement that there be probable cause prior to any search or seizure undertaken pursuant to the subdivision. The court held that the omission from § 852(2) of any right to at least a postseizure hearing prior to forfeiture violated the Due Process Clause of the Constitution. The court severed the invalid section from the rest of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's order by declaring one subsection of the statute to be unconstitutional and severing that section, vacating the preliminary injunction, and dismissing the complaint. The court affirmed the trial court's order as modified.

 

778 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Pepsico, Inc. v. Bouchard


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


102 A.D.2d 1000; 477 N.Y.S.2d 892; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19237



June 28, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner owner appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which sustained a sales and use tax assessment by respondent Tax Commission of the State of New York imposed pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 1136(b).


OVERVIEW: The owner purchased an aircraft out of state, paying a sales and use tax on it in that state. The owner later hangared the airplane in New York. The state tax department sent the owner a notice demanding payment of sales and use taxes on the airplane. After a formal hearing, the assessment was modified in several respects, but the owner's main arguments were rejected. The owner brought a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 to review the tax commission's determination. The court rejected the owner's argument that the assessment was barred by the three-year statute of limitations in N.Y. Tax Law § 1147(b). The owner's argument was grounded on the fact that the assessment notice had the wrong taxable quarter listed as the assessment period and no assessment was proposed for the correct quarter; therefore, it contended, the assessment for the proper quarter was time-bared. The court found that the owner had adequate notice of the taxes due within the three-year time period as evidenced by the very fact of its timely challenge to the assessment. The court confirmed the tax determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining the sales and use tax imposed by the tax commission on the owner's aircraft.

 

779 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Methodist Hospital of Brooklyn v. State Ins. Fund


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


102 A.D.2d 367; 479 N.Y.S.2d 11; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18795



June 26, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on February 24, 1983, affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employers filed a declaratory judgment action against respondents, state insurance fund and state, for a determination of the constitutionality of the Workers' Compensation Law, as amended by 1982 N.Y. Laws 55, 404. The Supreme Court, New York County (New York) granted the state's cross-motion for summary judgment for a declaration that 1982 N.Y. Laws 55, 404 was constitutional. The employers appealed.


OVERVIEW: 1982 N.Y. Laws 55 was enacted as an amendment to the Workers' Compensation Law (WCL) and mandated the transfer of monies from the state insurance fund to the general state fund. 1982 N.Y. Laws 404 provided for an appropriation to the state insurance fund. Some employers filed a declaratory judgment action against the state insurance fund and state that challenged the constitutionality of 1982 N.Y. Laws 55, 404. The trial court granted the state's cross-motion for summary judgment. The employers appealed and asserted that 1982 N.Y. Laws 55, 404 infringed on their property interest in the state insurance funds in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 6. The court held that 1982 N.Y. Laws 55, 404 were constitutional under the U.S. Constitution and the New York constitution because the state properly exercised its sovereign power over the state insurance fund as a state agency, the legislature had power to enact laws concerning workers' compensation under N.Y. Const. art. I, § 18, and the employers failed to show that they had any constitutionally protected contractual or property rights in the state insurance fund under the WCL.


OUTCOME: The judgment that granted the state's cross-motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Workers' Compensation -- State Insurance Fund as State Agency

1. In a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of chapter 55 of the Laws of 1982 which amended the Workers' Compensation Law to mandate that the State Insurance Fund (SIF) transfer $ 190 million to the general fund of the State by March 1, 1983, and to provide for future transfers, and chapter 404 of the Laws of 1982 which provided for the first $ 190 million appropriation, the SIF must be considered a State agency for purposes of the litigation. The SIF is a State agency subject to the broad scope of the Legislature's power to enact laws concerning workers'  [***2] compensation (NY Const, art I, § 18) notwithstanding that for "insurance purposes" or "in litigation" as the owner of a subrogated claim it may be treated as a private entity.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Appropriation from State Insurance Fund

2. Chapter 55 of the Laws of 1982, which amended the Workers' Compensation Law to mandate that the State Insurance Fund (SIF) transfer $ 190 million to the general fund of the State by March 1, 1983, and to provide for future transfers, which sum would be appropriated for the SIF in the State budget, but none of which would be actually paid unless the following year's State budget failed to make the same appropriation, and chapter 404 of the Laws of 1982, which provided for the first $ 190 million appropriation, are not unconstitutional on the ground that they implicitly create a loan or gift of the State's credit in violation of article VII (§ 8, subd 1) of the New York Constitution. The SIF is not an individual or public or private corporation or association or private undertaking within the meaning of article VII (§ 8, subd 1); the SIF is itself a State agency and, therefore, the constitutional provision does [***3] not apply to it.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Appropriation from State Insurance Fund

3. Chapter 55 of the Laws of 1982, which amended the Workers' Compensation Law to mandate that the State Insurance Fund (SIF) transfer $ 190 million to the general fund of the State which sum would be appropriated for the SIF in the State budget, but none of which would be actually paid unless the following year's State budget failed to make the same appropriation, is not unconstitutional on the ground that it creates a debt from the State to the SIF in violation of sections 9 and 11 of article VII of the New York Constitution. The provision for the annual appropriation of $ 190 million to insure the solvency of the SIF following the transfer of a like sum to the State's general fund cannot be equated with the incurring of long-term debt for capital improvement as proscribed by those constitutional provisions. Moreover, chapter 55 and chapter 404 of the Laws of 1982, which provides for the first $ 190 million appropriation under chapter 55, do not create an appropriation scheme in violation of section 7 of article VII; if no appropriation is passed in any future year,  [***4] the amount appropriated for and encumbered during the preceding fiscal year is to be paid forthwith and, therefore, any moneys paid under any such appropriation must be paid, if at all, within two years next after the passage of such appropriation action within the mandate of section 7 of article VII.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Appropriation from State Insurance Fund

4. Chapter 55 of the Laws of 1982, which amended the Workers' Compensation Law to mandate that the State Insurance Fund (SIF) transfer $ 190 million to the general fund of the State, does not constitute an unconstitutional legislative incursion upon the discretionary powers of State officials with responsibility for the SIF. Chapter 55 does not deal with the investment discretion of the SIF; rather, it merely directs the transfer of funds internally within the State's financial structure.

Constitutional Law -- Due Process -- Appropriation from State Insurance Fund

5. Chapter 55 of the Laws of 1982, which amended the Workers' Compensation Law to mandate that the State Insurance Fund (SIF) transfer $ 190 million to the general fund of the State by March 1, 1983, and to provide for [***5] future transfers, and chapter 404 of the Laws of 1982, which provided for the first $ 190 million appropriation, are not unconstitutional on the ground that they provide for the taking of private property from plaintiffs, employers insured by SIF under workers' compensation policies, without due process of law. The SIF funds are State funds and plaintiffs have no constitutionally protected property interests therein. No such property rights derive from any promises or guarantees contained in the insurance policies or any provision of the Workers' Compensation Law; the insurance policies cannot be fairly interpreted as conferring any such contractual rights and the language of the applicable provisions of the Workers' Compensation Law is clearly permissive and does not evince a legislative intent to create private contractual or vested rights.

Constitutional Law -- Impairment of Contract -- Appropriation from State Insurance Fund

6. Chapter 55 of the Laws of 1982, which amended the Workers' Compensation Law to mandate that the State Insurance fund (SIF) transfer $ 190 million to the general fund of the State by March 1, 1983, and to provide for future transfers, and chapter [***6] 404 of the Laws of 1982, which provided for the first $ 190 million appropriation, are not unconstitutional on the ground that they constitute an impairment of the contractual obligations of plaintiffs, employers insured by SIF under workers' compensation policies. Inasmuch as plaintiffs were operating in a heavily regulated industry, they knew that their contractual rights were subject to alteration by legislative amendments and, therefore, their reasonable expectations have not been impaired; moreover, any impairment that might exist is not substantial since there is no evidence of any retroactive impact of the challenged legislation on any contract rights plaintiffs may possess nor does it appear that the SIF will raise its premiums as a result of said legislation.

American Ins. Asso. v. Bouchard


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


102 A.D.2d 775; 479 N.Y.S.2d 23; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18940



June 26, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants insurers sought review of the decision of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which granted respondent state officials' cross motion for summary judgment that dismissed the complaint in which the insurers sought a declaration that 1982 N.Y. Laws 55 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The insurers filed an action against the state officials and sought a declaratory judgment that 1982 N.Y. Laws 55 was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the state officials' cross motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint but the court reversed. The court found that the insurers did not lack standing because a justiciable controversy existed as the insurers had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute. The court found that the assets of the trust funds were intended to secure the obligations of insurers to policyholders and beneficiaries in case of insolvency and were supplied by the insurers who filed the action. The court also found that 1982 N.Y. Laws 55 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court that granted the state officials' cross motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint and determined that the statute in question was constitutional.

 

781 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fagan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


102 A.D.2d 744; 477 N.Y.S.2d 12; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18912



June 21, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which convicted defendant, following his guilty plea, of two counts of attempted robbery in the second degree and sentenced him as a persistent violent felony offender to two concurrent sentences of six years to life.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the state's persistent violent felony offender law, N.Y. Penal Law § 70.08, violated the state constitution's ex post facto prohibition. The court held that the statute's reclassification of prior felony convictions as violent felonies did not violate the restriction against ex post facto legislation because § 70.08 imposed a more severe punishment for the latest crime for which an accused was sentenced but did not impose any additional penalty for the prior crimes. However, the court then held that the trial court erred in calculating defendant's prior felonies. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that two or more predicate violent felony convictions were required to be committed sequentially, so that the second offense, to be counted as a predicate, was required to be committed after sentencing of the first offense. Thus, the court held that the three prior convictions in which concurrent sentences were imposed within a three-month period were considered as only one prior offense. Thus, the court modified the judgment by vacating the sentence and remanding the case for sentencing of defendant as a second violent felony offender.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment by vacating defendant's sentence and remanding the case to the trial court for sentencing of defendant as a second violent felony offender. The court otherwise affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of two counts of attempted robbery in the second degree.

 

782 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Taylor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


102 A.D.2d 944; 477 N.Y.S.2d 805; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19197



June 21, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the County Court of Chemung County (New York), which convicted him of forgery in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of forgery. Defendant appealed, arguing that the prosecution was precluded from submitting certain evidence because it failed to demonstrate the good cause necessary to excuse its failure to give the statutory notice of its intention to offer potentially suppressible evidence at trial within 15 days after arraignment as required by N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 710.30 (2). The court ruled that the statutory requirements could be dispensed with whenever the statute's goal, to afford defendant adequate time in preparing his case, was accomplished by some substitute procedure. The court held that the statutory goal of adequate preparation was accomplished since defendant was notified that the prosecution intended to offer suppressible evidence at a hearing two months prior to defendant's trial. Further, the court concluded that a photographic array was not unconstitutionally suggestive because defendant's contention of unconstitutionality was based on the fact that defendant's photograph had not been trimmed to fit in the police identification book, yet the witnesses did not recall noticing this difference when they made their identifications.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was affirmed where the prosecution's failure to give statutory notice of its intention to offer potentially suppressible evidence did not warrant reversal of the conviction because the statutory goal of adequate preparation was accomplished when defendant was notified of the intent to offer suppressible evidence two months prior to defendant's trial and a photographic array was not unconstitutionally suggestive.

 

783 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Empire State Pharmaceutical Soc. v. New York State Dep't of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


102 A.D.2d 964; 477 N.Y.S.2d 832; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19213



June 21, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent New York State Department of Education challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), that granted the application to enjoin the Department's use of certain procedures for pharmacy inspection and penalty assessment. Petitioners, the pharmacists' association, the individual pharmacists, and pharmacy corporations, brought the initial proceeding pursuant to N.Y.C.P.L.R. art. 78.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners initiated the art. 78 proceeding to enjoin the Department's use of certain expedited procedures to inspect pharmacies and assess penalties. Petitioners also sought a declaration that the procedures, as set forth in N.Y. Educ. Law § 65102)(c), were unconstitutional. The supreme court held that the expedited procedure was an unconstitutional deprivation of due process because a specific penalty was assessed before the licensee had an opportunity to appear before the relevant committee. The supreme court also directed the Department to issue warnings without penalties or giving notice of charges and reference to a committee panel. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, analogizing the procedure to the criminal plea bargaining process. The letter constituted the charge and the acceptance of the proposed fine was, in effect, a plea of guilty. The court also held that the guilty plea properly was encouraged by offering benefits and that the Department did not exceed its authority under the statute. The Department's procedures for inspection and assessment of penalties constituted reasonable acts designed to further the regulatory scheme.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and dismissed the petition.

 

784 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Lock v. New York State Education Dep't


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


102 A.D.2d 979; 477 N.Y.S.2d 783; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19223



June 21, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner doctor appealed from an order and judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which dismissed his application under N.Y. C.P.L.R. article 78 to annul a determination of the State Education Department (department) denying the doctor a license to practice medicine in New York, and granted the department's motion to dismiss the doctor's complaint.


OVERVIEW: The doctor, who also held a graduate degree in physics from an American university, graduated from a 24-month medical school in Mexico. N.Y. Educ. Law § 6524 required completion of education in accordance with regulations requiring completion of a curriculum of not less than 32 months. The trial court dismissed the doctor's application to annul the department's refusal to license him to practice medicine in New York. The court affirmed. The reasons for the department's refusal to waive the doctor's conceded noncompliance with the regulation, including his failure to demonstrate that the doctorate in physics was equivalent to a year of medical school, the lack of accreditation of the Mexican medical school, and the failure of the Mexican school to respond to inquiries made by the department, afforded substantial evidence to support the determination which was not arbitrary or capricious. Similarly, the department's refusal to recognize the validity of the doctor's four years of postgraduate medical residences and fellowships in New York hospitals, or to give him an opportunity to demonstrate that the four years complied with New York standards, was not irrational or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

785 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Baird v. Axelrod


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


102 A.D.2d 972; 477 N.Y.S.2d 845; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19219



June 12, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nursing home owner appealed the decision of respondent Commissioner of Health of the State of New York, pursuant to an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), in the owner's N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding that sought permission to construct two additional nursing home beds.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that the commissioner lacked authority to prohibit the proposed construction on the basis of public need as he did not receive government funds and the finding of a lack of public need for the additional beds was not supported by substantial evidence. In rejecting both arguments, the court found that the commissioner's decision was not irrational and held that N.Y. Pub. Health § 2802 clearly and specifically provided that the construction of a hospital required the commissioner's approval, and the commissioner was required to base such approval on his satisfaction as to a public need for the construction. Further, the court found that the public need requirement was applicable to the owner's facility because it applied to all hospitals, irrespective of the nature of their funding. Moreover, the formula utilized to predict public need was properly designed to provide flexibility between the levels of care provided by health-related facilities and skilled nursing facilities. Finally, the commissioner's rejection due to the owner's nonacceptance of Medicaid patients was properly based on greater need for facilities who accepted such patients in view of their numbers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commissioner's decision and dismissed the owner's petition without costs.

 

786 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Brooklyn Union Gas Co. v. Public Service Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


101 A.D.2d 453; 478 N.Y.S.2d 78; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17841



May 24, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, and petition dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Natural Gas Utility appealed pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 from the order of the New York Public Service Commission. The utility contended that the order and rate increase imposed by the commission was improper because it was not introduced into evidence, it was not supported by substantial evidence, it was unauthorized, arbitrary and capricious, and it was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The utility sought a two-tier rate increase and the commission imposed an order that granted a single rate increase. The court held that it was unnecessary for the specific rate plan adopted to be introduced into evidence because the commission was not bound by any specific rate proposal offered by a party. The court held that the rate proposal arrived at by the commission was supported by substantial evidence and it was not arbitrary or capricious. The court held that the commission's allowance for certain advertising expenses was supported by substantial evidence. The court held that the commission had authority under N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 66(12)(a) to require a disclaimer in the utility's advertisements. The court held that the disclaimer did not violate the First Amendment because it was a valid regulation of commercial speech and it was narrowly drawn. The court held that because the disclaimer was narrowly drawn it was not arbitrary or capricious. The court held that the utility's equal protection rights were not violated because equal protection did not require the universal application of a remedy.


OUTCOME: The commission's rate determination was affirmed and the utility's petition was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Public Utilities -- Rate Making -- Across-the-Board Increase

1. The Public Service Commission (PSC) is charged with the responsibility of setting reasonable rates and, in doing so, it is not bound by the specific rate proposals offered by the parties, so long as its ultimate determination is supported by substantial evidence in the record; simply because petitioner, a utility which provides gas service to customers within a portion of the City of New York, sought a two-stage rate increase, which request was supported by the staff of the Department of Public Service (department), the PSC was not bound to give petitioner some form [***2] of a two-stage rate increase. The PSC's decision to adopt a specific rate design proposed by the Consumer Protection Board in a reply brief did not deny petitioner its right to cross-examine or respond to such proposal; the decision of the PSC to reject a two-stage rate increase due to lack of a decremental cost study was not irrational or arbitrary and capricious. There is substantial evidence in the record to support the ultimate across-the-board rate increase arrived at by the PSC, and there is no requirement that the PSC accept the testimony of, or evidence presented by, any one particular witness, even if that witness is a member of the staff of the department.

Public Utilities -- Rate Making -- Promotional Advertising Expenses

2. A decision of the Public Service Commission (PSC) to limit the allowance for promotional advertising expenses for petitioner, a utility which provides gas service, to .08% of revenues, or $ 751,000, rather than the $ 1.6 million requested by petitioner, is supported by substantial evidence; such a matter rests within the the discretion and expertise of the PSC.

Public Utilities -- Promotional Advertising -- Disclaimer Requirement

 [***3] 3. The Public Service Commission (PSC) has the statutory authority to require petitioner, a utility which provides gas service, in advertising based on the price advantage of natural gas, to include a disclaimer that any such advantage might dissipate as a result of deregulation and to provide a phone number to solicit further information, since subdivision 12-a of section 66 of the Public Service Law provides that the commission shall ensure periodic explanation of applicable rates and rate schedules for the purpose of assisting customers in making the most efficient use of energy. The disclaimer requirement did not infringe upon petitioner's constitutional right of expression, since the State has a substantial interest in requiring a utility to provide complete information to consumers if it chooses to advertise the price advantages of its service, the disclaimer directly advances that interest and it is specific and drawn to remedy the situation the PSC sought to correct; petitioner's equal protection rights were not violated because the disclaimer requirement was imposed upon only it and one other utility since government may move forward by gradual progression rather than by [***4] universal application or not at all, and petitioner's due process rights were not violated since it had the opportunity to present evidence regarding the disclaimer. Finally, the disclaimer requirement is not arbitrary, capricious or unsupported by the record.

 

787 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Schultz v. Boy Scouts of Am.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


102 A.D.2d 100; 476 N.Y.S.2d 309; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18307



May 24, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment (one paper), Supreme Court, New York County, entered on March 4, 1983, affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court at Special Term (New York) granted motions by defendants, charitable organization and its employee, to dismiss the complaint against them filed by plaintiffs, parents and administrators of an estate, for the wrongful death of their dead son and injuries sustained by their living son. The trial court found that New Jersey's charitable immunity statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:53A-7, applied to bar recovery under the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The parents and administrators of an estate filed an action against the charitable organization and its employee, claiming that the employee sexually abused their sons at a church and school located in New Jersey. Other acts took place at a summer camp in New York. They claimed that, as a result of those acts, both sons received psychiatric care and one of them committed suicide. The parents and administrators of an estate had filed an identical suit against an official of the charitable organization in New Jersey. The New Jersey court found in favor of the official based on application of New Jersey's charitable immunity statute, § 2A:53A-7. The charitable organization and its employee filed motions to dismiss this action on grounds of collateral estoppel and application of § 2A:53A-7. The court found that much of the sexual abuse of the two boys took place in New Jersey as did the alleged wrongful hiring and supervision of the employee. Because New Jersey was the only state having any interest in the resolution of the case, § 2A:53A-7 applied to bar the suit. The court also found that because the two complaints were identical, collateral estoppel applied to bar the suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the complaint filed by the parents and administrators of an estate.


HEADNOTES

Conflict of Laws -- Law Governing Tort Action -- Collateral Estoppel

The New York Supreme Court properly applied New Jersey's charitable immunity statute and dismissed the complaint in an action by plaintiffs alleging that their sons were sexually abused by an individual employed by defendant Franciscan Brothers of the Poor; that these acts took place at a church and school in New Jersey and at a camp run by defendant Boy Scouts of America in New York, where the same man acted as a troop leader, and that, as a result of these events, both boys received psychiatric care and one boy committed suicide; although some of the torts occurred in New York, New Jersey law is applicable to plaintiffs' claims since much of the sexual abuse of the two boys took place in New [***2] Jersey, the alleged wrongful hiring and supervision took place in New Jersey and all of the parties resided there. Furthermore, a New Jersey Supreme Court decision that identical claims brought by plaintiffs in New Jersey against the Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Newark were barred by the New Jersey charitable immunity statute collaterally estops plaintiffs from relitigating those claims against defendants.

 

788 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Zimmerman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


101 A.D.2d 294; 475 N.Y.S.2d 127; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17815



May 7, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, rendered May 6, 1983, affirmed.

The case is remitted to the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, for further proceedings pursuant to CPL 460.50 (subd 5).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court in Suffolk County (New York), which convicted him of criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress physical evidence obtained by an illegal search of defendant's daughter's vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to suppress weapons and ammunition found as a result of an alleged illegal search by the police of the trunk of defendant's daughter's car. The trial court held, in its conclusions of law, that the police had not met their heavy burden of establishing beyond a reasonable doubt the voluntariness of defendant's alleged consent to the otherwise illegal search, but that suppression of the physical evidence was not warranted in view of the fact that the police believed in good faith the quality of the consent to be sufficient, this good faith was reasonable, and any error by the police was a mere judgmental error. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the evidence. The court affirmed the conviction and the denial of defendant's motion to suppress, holding that the state met its burden of establishing that defendant gave his consent to the search of the trunk because he was cooperative with all of the police officers' requests at the time he was stopped, he was never handcuffed, and he voluntarily opened the trunk for the officers to search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction and denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence acquired from the search of defendant's daughter's car.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Unlawful Search and Seizure -- Consent to Search

When the People rely on consent to justify an otherwise unlawful police intrusion, they bear the burden of establishing that consent by clear and positive evidence; moreover, the voluntariness of the consent must be evaluated from the totality of the circumstances. Accordingly, the People met their heavy burden of proving defendant's consent to the search of the trunk of his daughter's car when stopped by police where defendant, who had a record of prior arrests, appeared calm and cooperated with all of the police officers'  [***2] requests, the officers never drew their guns and defendant was never handcuffed and, following the officers' request that he open the trunk, defendant, seeming neither upset nor concerned, took the keys and did so. The fact that the police never informed defendant of his right to refuse consent does not, by itself, vitiate the voluntariness of consent.
