In re Ronald "YY"


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


101 A.D.2d 895; 475 N.Y.S.2d 597; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18617



May 3, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother sought review of the order of the Family Court of Tompkins County (New York), which adjudicated her children to be permanently neglected and ordered guardianship and custody rights to petitioner, the Tompkins County Department of Social Services (department), for the purpose of adoption.


OVERVIEW: The department filed a permanent neglect petition and was awarded guardianship and custody rights over the children. On appeal, the court affirmed the family court's order. The court noted that the family court decided the matter prior to a United States Supreme Court decision, which held that a fair preponderance of the evidence was an unconstitutional standard of proof. However, the court concluded that a reversal on that basis was not required. Because the family court conducted a plenary hearing, the court was authorized to review the sufficiency of the order under the clear and convincing standard. The court held that the family court's finding that the mother failed to plan for the future of the children, was in and of itself, sufficient support for the determination of permanent neglect. The mother's poor financial situation did not prevent her from developing realistic and feasible plans for the children's future. Moreover, she abandoned the alcoholism treatment programs devised by the department. The court found that the department had made diligent efforts to encourage and strengthen the parental relationship, as required by N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 384-b(7)(a), (f).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the family court's order that adjudicated the children as permanently neglected and awarded the department guardianship and custody rights.

 

790 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pace


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


101 A.D.2d 336; 475 N.Y.S.2d 443; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17821



April 30, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Two judgments (one as to each defendant) of the Supreme Court, Kings County, rendered March 1, 1982 and March 12, 1982, respectively, reversed, on the law and the facts, motion to suppress granted to the extent that all physical evidence obtained as a result of the entry into Economy Auto Salvage on February 12, 1979 and the subsequent search conducted pursuant to a search warrant issued on February 13, 1979 is suppressed, and the matters are remitted to the Supreme Court, Kings County, for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, owners of an auto salvage business, appealed from judgments from the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), denying their motions to suppress physical evidence arising from a conviction of criminal possession of stolen property pursuant to the New York City Charter §436.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, owners of an auto salvage business, were convicted of criminal possession of stolen property pursuant to the New York City Charter § 436. Police officers surveyed defendants' salvage yard, not for the purposes of an administrative inspection but expressly to gather evidence of a crime and found certain parts that were obtained from stolen vehicles. Thereafter, the officers secured a search warrant. Defendants sought to suppress this evidence but, at trial, the court found that the initial stop was proper, that the warrantless search of the yard was sustainable as an administrative search under §436 and that the search conducted pursuant to the warrant should be upheld. The issue concerned the construction of §436, which authorized the police department to conduct warrantless administrative inspections of certain enterprises. On appeal, the court reversed and remitted, because the police officers expressly maintained that their mission was to gather evidence of a crime rather than to administer any regulatory scheme. When a search was not undertaken as a routine regulatory inspection, the administrative search rationale was simply inapplicable.


OUTCOME: Court reversed the judgment and granted the motion to suppress to the extent of suppressing all physical evidence obtained as a result of the entry into defendants' salvage yard and the subsequent search conducted pursuant to a search warrant. Officers were properly in a public area of the yard and once they were told that the police book had been stolen, nothing prevented them from guarding the area while a search warrant was obtained.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Unlawful Search and Seizure

Although the initial [***2] stop and seizure of a truck was lawful and justified by the belief that defendant was operating the vehicle in violation of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, the subsequent warrantless search of the auto salvage yard owned by defendant was illegal and cannot be justified by section 436 of the New York City Charter, which authorizes the police department to conduct warrantless administrative inspections of certain enterprises; the police officers expressly maintained that their mission was to gather evidence of a crime rather than to administer any regulatory scheme, and when a search is not undertaken as a routine regulatory inspection the administrative search rationale is simply inapplicable. The subsequently obtained search warrant did not validate the seizure of the fruits of the illegal entry, and accordingly, evidence obtained pursuant to the warrant must also be suppressed.

 

791 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Gandolfi v. Yonkers


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


101 A.D.2d 188; 475 N.Y.S.2d 429; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17801



April 23, 1984 



DISPOSITION: In Gandolfi v City of Yonkers: Judgment and order (one paper) of the Supreme Court, Westchester County, dated January 10, 1984, modified, on the law, by deleting (1) the second decretal paragraph, (2) so much of the third and fourth decretal paragraphs as limits injunctive relief "with respect to any future taxation which is neither the subject of the municipal budget of the County of Westchester or [sic] the City of Yonkers enacted * * * by such municipality prior to the date of the entry of [the] judgment [and order]", and (3) so much of the sixth decretal paragraph [***3] as dismisses the second cause of action asserted in plaintiffs' complaint seeking a refund of taxes paid. As so modified, judgment and order affirmed insofar as appealed from, and matter remitted to the Supreme Court, Westchester County, for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion by Titone, J. P.

In Platzner Organization v Shulman: Judgment and order (one paper) of the Supreme Court, Westchester County, dated January 10, 1984, modified, on the law, by deleting (1) the second decretal paragraph, and (2) so much of the third and fourth decretal paragraphs as limits injunctive relief "to any future taxation which is neither the subject of the municipal budget of the County of Westchester or [sic] the cities of Yonkers, Mt. Vernon, and New Rochelle enacted by such municipality prior to the date of entry of [the] judgment [and order]". As so modified, judgment and order affirmed insofar as appealled from.

The plaintiffs in both actions are awarded one bill of costs against the defendants in said actions appearing jointly and filing separate briefs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and county, in a consolidated action, challenged two orders of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which entered judgments declaring N.Y. Tax Law §1262-b in violation of N.Y. Const. art. VIII, § 10. Plaintiff property owners cross appealed the orders, which disallowed any refund of taxes paid and enjoined only future taxation that was not already part of the city and county budget.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were a group of property owners in the county that paid real property taxes pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 1262-b, which operated to hold three cities, including defendant city, harmless from a loss of their sales tax revenues resulting from the implementation of a county-wide sales tax by the county. Section 1262-b enabled the county to recover an amount equal to the sales tax revenues returned to those cities by means of a county real property tax imposed in those cities. The property owners sought a determination that § 1262-b was unconstitutional under N.Y. Const. art VIII, § 10, a permanent injunction against its enforcement, and refunds. The trial court found § 1262-b to be unconstitutional, but made the relief prospective by allowing the municipalities to continue to utilize § 1262-b in their then-current budgets and denying refunds for taxes paid. The court affirmed, holding that § 1262-b conflicted with N.Y. Const. art VIII, § 10, but deleted the portions of the order making the relief prospective and denying the tax refunds. The court remanded for a hearing on whether the taxpayers requesting a refund had properly protested the taxes.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order, deleting the limitation on the injunction to future taxation not already budgeted by the city and county, and deleting the portion of the order dismissing plaintiffs' cause of action for a refund. The court affirmed the order as modified, finding that the tax law at issue was in violation of New York State Constitution, and remanded for a determination of the property owners' eligibility for a refund.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes -- Recovery of Sales Tax by Means of County Real Property Tax

1. Section [***4] 1262-b of the Tax Law, which is expressly made operative only until such time as the real property tax limitations in the Constitution of the State of New York with respect to cities are increased, and authorizes Westchester County to pay its share of sales tax revenue to certain cities in the county and to levy an additional property tax in those cities for the amount of taxes so paid, is violative of section 10 of article VIII of the New York Constitution and therefore unconstitutional, that section providing that the real property tax is subject to a constitutional ceiling of 2% of assessed full valuation averaged over a five-year period with respect to cities and counties; section 1262-b, which operates to hold the Cities of Mount Vernon, New Rochelle and Yonkers harmless from the loss of their sales tax revenues resulting from the implementation of a county-wide sales tax and enables Westchester County to recover an amount equal to the sales tax revenues returned to those cities by means of a county real property tax imposed in those cities, was intended to circumvent the constitutional limitation, as it is simply an attempt to disguise a city real estate tax.

Taxation  [***5] -- Sales and Use Taxes -- Corrective Action for Constitutional Violation

2. In an action in which section 1262-b of the Tax Law, which authorizes Westchester County to pay its share of the sales tax revenue to certain cities in the county and to levy an additional property tax in those cities for the amount of taxes so paid, was properly declared violative of section 10 of article VIII of the New York Constitution, which provides that the real property tax is subject to a constitutional ceiling of 2% of assessed full valuation averaged over a five-year period with respect to cities and counties, the prospective declaration of unconstitutionality, to take effect upon the adoption of the next municipal budgets, was improper; although a court may delay implementation of a judicial mandate in extraordinary circumstances, local subdivisions have been put on notice that patent circumvention of constitutional limitations on their taxing powers will not be tolerated and the defendants were aware of the potential challenges to the legislation. Those taxpayers who filed appropriate protest should not be precluded from obtaining a refund of real property taxes paid, and because the parties [***6] dispute whether protest was, in fact, made and the record is unclear, summary disposition of the issue is improper and the matter is remitted for a hearing.

Actions -- Class Actions -- Governmental Operations

3. In an action in which section 1262-b of the Tax Law, which authorizes Westchester County to pay its share of sales tax revenue to certain cities in the county and to levy an additional property tax in those cities for the amount of taxes so paid, was declared violative of section 10 of article VIII of the New York Constitution, which provides that the real property tax is subject to a constitutional ceiling of 2% of assessed full valuation averaged over a five-year period with respect to cities and counties, class action status was properly denied; class action status is inappropriate where governmental operations are involved and subsequent plaintiffs will be adequately protected under principles of stare decisis.

 

792 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Lai Chun Chan Jin v. Board of Estimate


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


101 A.D.2d 97; 474 N.Y.S.2d 504; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17789



April 17, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on July 26, 1983, unanimously reversed, on the law and the facts, and in the exercise of discretion, and the motion is denied, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent agencies sought review of an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term, New York County (New York), which granted a motion by petitioners, individuals and neighborhood organizations, to amend a petition and to add two new parties as respondents. Petitioners objected to the creation of a zoning district in their original petition and, in an amended petition, sought to raise the issue of environmental quality review.


OVERVIEW: In an amended petition, petitioners alleged that the environmental quality review was legally insufficient for want of an environmental assessment form and by its allegedly incorrect conclusion with respect to the environmental impact of the district. On appeal, the court reversed the grant of the motion to amend the petition and to add new parties. The petition was governed by the four-month statute of limitations contained in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 217. Contrary to the trial court's decision, only an action seeking to declare a statute unconstitutional was cognizable after the four months has expired and an action could not be labeled as one for a declaratory judgment merely to avoid the limitations period. Further, the relation back provision in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 203(e) did not save petitioner's proposed environmental quality review challenge. Petitioners originally complained of the wisdom of the board's approval of the district and attacked the procedures for convening a public hearing before a community board. The agencies could not be said to have been put on notice thereby of errors in the environmental quality review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and denied petitioners' motion to amend and to add new parties.


HEADNOTES

Pleading -- Amendment

In an action objecting to the creation by the New York City Board of Estimate of the Special Manhattan Bridge District (SMBD) and seeking to annul the Board's action on the ground that City Planning Commission (CPC) regulations providing for notice of a hearing before local community boards whenever proposals are made to alter existing land use guidelines violated the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, the Supreme Court improperly granted petitioners' motion, made after submission of papers but prior to decision and renewed after reversal of the Supreme Court's decision declaring the CPC notice regulations to be constitutionally defective, to amend their petition to assert two additional claims and [***2] to add two additional parties, the Department of Environmental Protection and the Department of City Planning, which conduct the "City Environmental Quality Review" (CEQR) of proposed zoning amendments, in order to allege that the CEQR of SMBD was legally insufficient. Such a proceeding for review of the CEQR is barred by the four-month Statute of Limitations of CPLR 217 and the "relation back" provision of CPLR 203 (subd [e]) does not save the proposed CEQR changes; while the CPC and the Department of City Planning are related entities, the latter has a distinct and separate role when it functions as a lead agency for CEQR and the two cannot be considered "united in interest"; furthermore, the original and first amended petition did not give notice of any challenge to the CEQR.

 

793 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Arcara v. Cloud Books, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


101 A.D.2d 163; 475 N.Y.S.2d 173; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17799



April 12, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bookstore sought review of an order from the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which denied a motion by the bookstore for partial summary judgment in an action by appellee state to abate alleged common law and statutory nuisances at an adult bookstore.


OVERVIEW: The state moved under the common law and N.Y. Pub. Health Law tit. II, art. 23 to abate alleged nuisances that had been observed at the bookstore, which sold sexually explicit material. It also sought under N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2320 to close the store and seize its assets. The bookstore filed a motion for partial summary judgment on the statutory cause of action on the ground that the statute was inapplicable to its situation and unconstitutionally infringed on its First Amendment rights. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed because § 2320, which defined the scope of tit. II, art. 23, placed no restriction on the premises subject to the law and was clearly aimed at prohibited conduct and not just houses of prostitution if the state by a preponderance of the evidence could establish that the premises were being used for a lewd purpose. Moreover, the bookstore's First Amendment rights were not threatened by the action because it was aimed at the prohibited conduct and not the content of the store's inventory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied the bookstore's motion for partial summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Nuisance -- Lewd Behavior at Bookstore

1. Title II of article 23 of the Public Health Law, entitled "Houses of Prostitution: Injunction and Abatement", is applicable to enjoin a nuisance in the form of lewd and illegal acts committed by patrons at a bookstore which sells books, magazines and novelties of a sexually frank nature and maintains coin-operated movie machines which show explicit sexual material; section 2320 of the Public Health Law defines the scope of the title and provides that whoever erects, establishes, or maintains a place used for the purpose of lewdness, assignation or prostitution is guilty of maintaining a nuisance and that the place where any such conduct occurs constitutes a nuisance and shall be enjoined and abated. A premises may have multiple purposes and if one of those is the promotion [***2] of lewdness, assignation or prostitution, it will run afoul of the statute; if the statute were intended to apply exclusively to houses of prostitution such a broad definition would not have been given to the term "nuisance", and the substance of a statute is to be determined by its provisions and not by its title. While the People need not demonstrate that the sole, or even dominant, use of the premises is devoted to the illegality prohibited in the statute, the People will have to show by a preponderance of the evidence a consistent pattern of conduct sufficient to prove that the premises are being employed for a proscribed use.

Nuisance -- Lewd Behavior at Bookstore -- Mandatory Closure

2. The mandatory closure provisions of title II of article 23 of the Public Health Law, which provide for the enjoining and abatement of lewdness, assignation or prostitution occurring at premises, do not infringe upon the First Amendment freedoms of the owner and operator of a bookstore which sells books, magazines and novelties of a sexually frank nature and maintains coin-operated movie machines which show explicit sexual material, at which premises it is alleged that a nuisance in [***3] the form of lewd and illegal acts committed by patrons is occurring. The statute is not required to contain any of the procedural safeguards mandated by Freedman v Maryland (380 U.S. 51), nor would closure of the bookstore constitute a prior restraint on protected First Amendment speech since the purpose of an action to enjoin the conduct occurring at the bookstore is to enjoin illegal conduct and not to regulate the content of presumptively protected materials distributed by the bookstore, and since the conduct sought to be enjoined is not "constitutionally preferred activity" the overbreadth doctrine is inapplicable.

 

794 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Broadway & 67th St. Corp. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


100 A.D.2d 478; 475 N.Y.S.2d 1; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17784



April 10, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on November 3, 1982, unanimously reversed, on the law, and the motion granted, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and city rent commissioner, sought review of a decision from the Supreme Court at Special Term in New York County (New York), which denied their summary judgment motion that sought dismissal of plaintiff landlord's complaint. The landlord alleged a prima facie tort asserting that the city and the commissioner had conspired intentionally to interfere with the landlord's business and to violate his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The landlord alleged a prima facie tort and a violation of his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The city and the commissioner brought a motion for summary judgment, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court reversed and held that § 1983 authorized a civil action for damages or equitable relief, or both, to redress any deprivation of civil rights perpetrated against an individual under color of state law. The court found that there was no constitutional right to a rent compatibility hearing in establishing a maximum rent base for the landlord's apartments. The court determined the compatibility hearing to ascertain the rents generally prevailing in the same area for substantially similar housing was merely one procedure to be utilized in fixing the rent. The court ruled no cause of action pursuant to § 1983 had been stated. The court held that the allegation of a prima facie tort was also with basis. The court held that the landlord had not demonstrated that the acts of the city and commissioner in denying rent increases sought by the landlord were motivated out of malice towards the landlord.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order from the trial court denying the motion for summary judgment brought by the city and the city commissioner in the landlord's action for an alleged § 1983 violation and a prima facie tort. The court granted the motion and dismissed the landlord's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation -- Maximum Legal Rent

1. In an action in which it was alleged that defendants, the City of New York and various officials of the Department of Rent and Housing Maintenance, had maliciously and intentionally conspired to interfere with plaintiff's business and violate its constitutional rights to due process and equal protection, in connection with the determination of the maximum legal rent to an apartment in petitioner's building, the Supreme Court had no power to order defendants to comply with a prior order of the Supreme Court made in a CPLR article 78 proceeding directing defendants, in determining the maximum legal rent, to rely upon a comparability study to ascertain the rents generally [***2] prevailing in the same area for substantially similar housing accommodations and to set a new maximum rent within 60 days, since the Appellate Division, in a subsequent article 78 proceeding, had reversed a Supreme Court order remanding the proceeding to hold the comparability study and remanded the subsequent proceeding to permit defendants to interpose an answer so that the issue of whether a comparability hearing had been held, or was viable or feasible, could be litigated; in the face of the Appellate Division's action, the alleged violation of the Supreme Court's order could provide no basis on which to found a collateral action, and the determination that there had been such violation was plainly premature, if not erroneous.

Civil Rights -- Federal Civil Rights Claim

2. In an action in which it was alleged that defendants, the City of New York and various officials of the Department of Rent and Housing Maintenance, had maliciously and intentionally conspired to interfere with plaintiff's business and violate its constitutional rights to due process and equal protection, in connection with the alleged violation of a Supreme Court order directing defendants to hold [***3] a comparability study in order to determine the maximum legal rent for an apartment in petitioner's building, no cause of action for deprivation of civil rights under section 1983 of title 42 of the United States Code is stated; the refusal by a State agency to comply with a State court order is an isolated event not of such magnitude as to involve constitutional rights to be redressed in damages under section 1983, and there is no showing that there is a constitutional right to a comparability hearing in connection with establishing a maximum base rent, such a hearing being merely one procedure to be utilized in fixing such rent. There are adequate State remedies to correct agency abuses such as violation of a court order, and at the time of the institution of the action and the Supreme Court's order appealed from, plaintiff had failed to pursue to completion its article 78 remedies; there has been no showing that the administrative and judicial procedure available to redress the alleged governmental misconduct is not adequate.

Torts -- Prima Facie Tort

3. In an action in which it was alleged that defendants, the City of New York and various officials of the Department [***4] of Rent and Housing Maintenance, had maliciously and intentionally conspired to interfere with plaintiff's business and violate its constitutional rights to due process and equal protection, in connection with the alleged violation of a Supreme Court order directing defendants to hold a comparability study in order to determine the maximum legal rent for an apartment in petitioner's building, no cause of action for prima facie tort is stated; neither the complaint nor plaintiff's bill of particulars sufficiently itemizes special damages, and plaintiff has not demonstrated that defendants' acts in denying a rent increase were motivated out of malice toward plaintiff. While defendants may have failed to comply with a court order, no evidence has been shown that such omission was an intentional wrong constituting tortious conduct. Prima facie tort is not designed to provide a basis for collateral attack on an agency determination parallel with the judicial proceeding challenging such determination, or where contempt proceedings provide an adequate remedy.

 

795 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


R & G Outfitters, Inc. v. Bouchard


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


101 A.D.2d 642; 475 N.Y.S.2d 549; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18184



April 9, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Tax Commission and respondent taxpayers filed cross appeals seeking review of the judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which conditionally granted the Commission's motion to dismiss the taxpayers' petition for failure to post the undertaking required by N.Y. Tax Law § 1138(a)(4) unless the taxpayers filed an undertaking in an amount equal to the net value of the estate of one of the taxpayers plus $ 1,000.


OVERVIEW: The Commission determined that the taxpayers owed sales and use taxes plus interest and penalties. The taxpayers filed an action pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 to review the Commission's determination. The Commission moved to dismiss the petition on the ground that the taxpayers had failed to either deposit the amount owed or to file an undertaking as required by N.Y. Tax Law § 1138(a)(4). The lower court conditionally granted the motion to dismiss unless the taxpayers filed an undertaking in an amount equal to the value of the estate of one of the taxpayers plus $ 1,000. Both sides appealed. The court rejected the taxpayers' argument that § 1138(a)(4) was unconstitutional and that requiring them to pay before they litigated deprived them of due process. The Commission countered that § 1138(a)(4) did not provide for a reduction in the amount to be deposited. The court held that § 1138(a)(4) was constitutional, noting that the United States Supreme Court had ruled that the principle of pay first and litigate later was constitutionally permissible. The court held that the taxpayers' failure to deposit the required undertaking deprived the lower court of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court modified the lower court judgment by deleting therefrom all of the decretal provisions except that which dismissed the taxpayers' petition to review the Commission's tax assessment. The court added a provision to the judgment declaring that the deposit and undertaking requirements of the Tax Law were constitutional. The court affirmed the decree as modified.

 

796 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Singer


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


101 A.D.2d 606; 474 N.Y.S.2d 854; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18148



April 5, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the County Court of Ulster County (New York), which convicted defendant for criminal sale of a controlled substance in the second degree and for the crime of bail jumping and sentenced defendant to concurrent terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for the crimes of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the second degree and bail jumping and the county court sentenced defendant to concurrent terms of imprisonment. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court rejected defendant's contention that the evidence at defendant's trial established the defense of entrapment as a matter of law because the conduct of the police did not rise to the level of active inducement or encouragement. The court also held that defendant was precluded from raising the entrapment defense on appeal because he failed to raise the defense in the trial court. The court also ruled that N.Y. Penal Law § 220.00(1) was not unconstitutionally vague because the statute was clear on its face. The court also concluded that defendant's sentence was not harsh or excessive under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant for the crimes of criminal sale of controlled substance and bail jumping.

 

797 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Casaburi v. Dow


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


100 A.D.2d 693; 474 N.Y.S.2d 629; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17676



March 29, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mobile home owner sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court, Ulster County (New York), which granted summary judgment to respondent tax foreclosure sale purchaser in the purchaser's action to bar the owner's claim to the mobile home.


OVERVIEW: The owner parked his mobile home on a lot he rented. The lot owners defaulted on payment of their taxes and the lot was sold at a tax foreclosure sale to the purchaser. The deed from the county to the purchaser purported to convey " three acres, described as trailer." The purchaser then filed an action to bar the owner's claim to the mobile home. The trial court granted summary judgment to the purchaser and the owner appealed. The court found that the trial court had based its decision on an erroneous application of N.Y. Real Property Tax Law § 102(12)(g), which required that the value of a mobile home be included in the assessment of the land on which it was located, thereby concluding that inasmuch as the value of the mobile home was assessed against the lot owners, it was subject to the foreclosure sale. The court stated that the lot owners had not acquired ownership of the trailer by virtue of having its value assessed against them, therefore ownership of the mobile home remained in the owner. The court held that title acquired under a tax deed was no greater than that of the parties assessed against, concluding that the county did not obtain title to the mobile home.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment granted to the purchaser and granted summary judgment to the owner who claimed title to the mobile home located on a lot acquired by the purchaser at a tax foreclosure sale.

 

798 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Matherson v. Marchello


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


100 A.D.2d 233; 473 N.Y.S.2d 998; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16993



March 26, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, dated April 8, 1982, reversed insofar as appealed from, with costs, defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint denied, and complaint reinstated. Defendants' time to answer is extended until 20 days after service upon them of a copy of the order to be made hereon, with notice of entry.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, sought review of an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Suffolk County (New York), which granted a motion to dismiss by defendants, members of a singing group and their record company. The husband and wife alleged that comments made during a radio interview were defamatory. The lower court dismissed the complaint, holding that the husband and wife failed to allege special damages.


OVERVIEW: A husband and wife brought an action alleging defamation against a singing group, members of which made comments during a radio interview suggesting that the husband was homosexual. The husband and wife sought compensatory and punitive damages for humiliation, mental anguish, loss of reputation, and injury to their marital relationship as well as for the loss of customers, business opportunities, and good will allegedly suffered by the husband. The lower court dismissed their complaint, holding that they did not sufficiently plead the special damages necessary to sustain a slander action. The court found that the husband and wife were actually alleging libel because the alleged defamation was broadcast over the airwaves. The court noted that parties alleging libel did not have to plead special damages if the defamatory statement would expose the party to public contempt, ridicule, aversion or disgrace. The court found that the complaint of the husband and wife was actionable without proof of special damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court. The singing group's motion to dismiss the complaint was denied, and the complaint of the husband and wife was reinstated.


HEADNOTES

Libel and Slander -- Radio Broadcast -- Statements Made in Radio Interview

In an action brought by plaintiffs, husband and wife, against the members of a singing group, as individuals and against their record company, alleging that statements made by defendants in a radio interview that "we used to fool around with his wife" and "I don't think it was his wife that he got upset about, I think it was when somebody started messing around with his boyfriend that he really freaked out" were defamatory, defendants' motion to dismiss is denied and the complaint is reinstated; although plaintiffs' nonspecific conclusory allegations do not meet the stringent [***2] requirements imposed for pleading special damages, a plaintiff suing in libel need not plead or prove special damages if the defamatory statement tends to expose the plaintiff to public contempt, ridicule, aversion or disgrace, or induce an evil opinion of him. Defamation which is broadcast by means of radio or television should be classified as libel and the statements, which could have been interpreted to mean that plaintiff wife was having an affair with one of the defendants, and as imputing homosexuality, are libelous on their face, thus obviating any need to allege and prove special damages.

 

799 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Department of Social Servs. ex rel. Sandra C. v. Thomas J. S.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


100 A.D.2d 119; 474 N.Y.S.2d 322; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16982



March 19, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, with one bill of costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father challenged a decision of the Family Court, Suffolk County (New York), which denied the putative father's motion to vacate a demand that he submit to a blood-grouping test.


OVERVIEW: The putative father contended that N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 532 (1981), which authorized the results of human leucocyte antigen (HLA) to be used as affirmative proof of paternity, violated due process, equal protection, and the putative father's privilege against self-incrimination. The putative father also contended that the proceeding was time-barred. The court held that § 532 did not violate due process. According to the court, the probative value of admitting HLA test results outweighed any prejudicial effect of admitting such results. The court also held that § 532 did not violate equal protection. According to the court, the legislature had a rational basis for failing to grant judicial discretion in ordering blood tests in paternity proceedings. Furthermore, the court held that § 532 did not violate the privilege against self-incrimination because the blood test results were not testimonial in nature. Finally, the court held that the 10-year statute of limitations for paternity actions instituted by public welfare officials was constitutional. According to the court, the 10-year time period did not violate due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied the putative father's motion to vacate a demand that he submit to a blood-grouping test.


HEADNOTES

Children Born out of Wedlock -- Paternity Proceeding -- HLA Test

1. Section 532 of the Family Court Act, which provides that the results of a human leucocyte antigen (HLA) blood tissue test may be received in evidence to aid in the determination of whether the alleged father is or is not the father except where exclusion has already been established by other blood-grouping tests, does not deprive a putative father of his Fourteenth Amendment rights to due process of law and equal protection of the laws and his Fifth Amendment privilege against self incrimination. The HLA test can increase the probability of exclusion to such a high degree as to affirmatively prove paternity where a putative father is not excluded by the test [***2] results, and the probative value of such a test result outweighs the danger of any undue prejudice; the recent amendment to section 418 of the Family Court Act permitting any party in a support proceeding to move for an order directing the mother, her child and the alleged father to submit to HLA tests has removed any disparity of treatment among a class of citizens similarly situated; although in a paternity proceeding section 532 requires the court to order blood tests upon motion of any party and in a support proceeding section 418 allows the court to exercise discretion in ordering such tests, there is a rational basis for conferring such discretion in support proceedings, in order to enable the court to protect children born during marriage from spurious claims of illegitimacy by a parent seeking to avoid the legal obligation to pay support; and finally, since blood test results are not testimonial in nature, the statutory privilege contained in section 531 of the Family Court Act is neither violated nor implicated by submitting to HLA testing.

Limitation of Actions -- Paternity Proceeding -- Proceeding by Public Welfare Official

2. The 10-year Statute of Limitations [***3] for commencement of a paternity proceeding where the petitioner is a public welfare official (Family Ct Act, § 517) is not repugnant to either the due process clause or the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment; the determination of the Legislature, in balancing a public welfare official's right to prosecute an otherwise valid filiation claim against the right of a putative father to be protected from defending a stale claim, that a period of limitation of 10 years after the birth of the child was appropriate, was not unreasonable or arbitrary in view of the strong public interest in protecting the community against burdensome taxation produced by the acts of individuals in derogation of public policy; the 1981 amendment to section 532 of the Family Court Act, which authorized the results of human leucocyte antigen testing to be used as affirmative proof of paternity, did not render unreasonable the original balance struck at the time of the enactment of section 517, and the interest in avoiding litigation of stale or fraudulent claims is outweighed by the need to provide the class of children born out of wedlock with a reasonable opportunity to institute paternity proceedings [***4] and to establish their right to support.

 

800 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Foster


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


100 A.D.2d 200; 473 N.Y.S.2d 978; 1984 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16989



March 12, 1984 



DISPOSITION: Two judgments (one as to defendant Fred Foster and the other as to defendant Gregory Reed) of the Supreme Court, Kings County, both rendered January 8, 1980, and order of the same court (upon appeal by permission) dated March 16, 1983, affirmed.

Judgment (as to defendant Jerry Foster) of the same court rendered January 8, 1980, reversed, on the law, and new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and his co-defendants sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court in Kings County (New York), which convicted defendant and his co-defendants for murder in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: A defendant and his co-defendants were convicted of murder in the second degree. Defendant challenged the conviction because the trial court had erroneously denied his challenge for cause a venireman. The court agreed there was error. The court reversed defendant's conviction, and remanded for a new trial. The main issue on appeal was whether defendant's challenge for cause was preserved for appellate review when he did not exercise his preemptory challenge because his co-defendants refused to do so. The court found defendant's challenge for cause that he made pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 270.20 was not waived. The court reasoned that the challenge for cause did bring the issue to the attention of the trial judge in a manner that pinpointed the legal question, and did satisfy the primary consideration of preserving an error for review. However, the court did not extend such a holding to his co-defendants who did not join him in his challenge for cause. The court affirmed the co-defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of murder in the second degree, but affirmed his co-defendants' convictions.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Challenge to Jury

The erroneous denial of a challenge for cause was preserved for review when the defendant who made the challenge was unable to exercise a peremptory challenge because his codefendants refused to join the exercise with him. Although the verdicts convicting the three codefendants are not jurisdictionally defective by virtue of the presence of a juror who should have been disqualified on the ground that he had served on another jury [***2] within the preceding two years (Judiciary Law, § 511, subd 5), the verdict convicting the defendant who made the challenge and who attempted to exercise a peremptory challenge cannot stand and he is granted a new trial, since a majority of jointly tried defendants must exercise a peremptory challenge ( CPL 270.25, subd 3) and this defendant's attempt to exercise such a challenge, which failed because his codefendants refused to join with him, cannot be construed as an intent to waive his position; the failure to exclude a disqualified juror after a timely and adequate objection necessarily affects the verdict against him and cannot be considered harmless error. The codefendants who made no objection to the venireman before he was sworn as a trial juror waived the issue of disqualification and cannot avail themselves of their colleague's objection.
